This instruction implements Air Force Policy Directive (AFPD) 36-30, Military Entitlements, and Depart-
ment of Defense Instruction (DoDI) 1300.18, Military Personnel Casualty Matters, Policies, and Proce-
dures. It describes procedures for the Casualty Services Program for all levels of command and all Air
Force organizations. This publication can be supplemented.
Refer recommended changes and conflicts between this and other publications to HQ AFPC/DPFCS, 550
C Street West, Suite 14, Randolph AFB, Texas 78150-4716 on Air Force Information Management Tool
(IMT) 847, Recommendation for Change of Publication. Send an information copy to HQ AFPC/
DPDXI, 550 C Street West, Suite 48, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4750.
This instruction requires collecting and maintaining information protected by the Privacy Act of 1974
authorized by Title 10, United States Code (U.S.C.), Sections 1475 through 1489, 2771, and 8013; Title
37, U.S.C., Sections 551 through 559. System of Records Notice F036 AF PC R, Casualty Files, applies.
This publication applies to Air National Guard (ANG) and Air Force Reserve Command (AFRC).
Any organization may supplement this publication. Major commands (MAJCOM), field operating agen-
cies (FOA), and direct reporting units (DRU) must send one copy of their published and or posted supple-
ment to HQ AFPC/DPFCS and a courtesy copy to HQ AFPC/DPDXI. Other organizations send one copy
of each published and or posted supplement to the next higher headquarters.
2                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


Process supplements that affect military personnel functions as shown in Air Force Instruction (AFI)
33-360, Volume 1, AF Content Management Program-Publications, and coordinate with Air Force Per-
sonnel Center, Casualty Services Branch (AFPC/DPFCS). Refer to Attachment 1 for glossary of refer-
ences and supporting information. The Paperwork Reduction Act of 1995 affects this instruction. The use
of the name or mark of any specific manufacturer, commercial product, commodity, or service in this
publication does not imply endorsement by the Air Force. The Content Management Program per AFI
33-360, volume 2, AF Content Management-Information Management Tools affects this instruction.

(50SW) This instruction implements AFI 36-3002, Casualty Services 25 Jul 2005, is supplemented as
follows and applies to the 50th Space Wing, its subordinate units at Schriever Air Force Base, Colorado
and the organizations supported by the 50th Space Wing located at Schriever Air Force Base. Ensure that
all records created as a result of processes prescribed in this publication are maintained in accordance with
AFMAN 37-123 (will convert to AFMAN33-363), Management of Records, and disposed of in accor-
dance with the Air Force Records Disposition Schedule.

SUMMARY OF CHANGES
This document is substantially revised and must be completely reviewed. It updates organizations,
office symbols, and renames numerous paragraph titles. For major commands (MAJCOM) or comparable
command levels, military personnel flight (MPF) commanders, Air Reserve Component (ARC) MPFs,
MPF customer support section chiefs, and casualty assistance representatives (CARs), it updates and clar-
ifies responsibilities, and establishes an annual requirement of 1 October to submit AF IMT 1075, Casu-
alty Personnel Roster, to the Air Force Personnel Center, Casualty Services Branch (AFPC/DPFCS). It
adds base agencies the MPF customer support section chief should include when preparing supplements
to this AFI, outlining and assigning local responsibilities. Defines the MPF customer support section chief
as responsible for training, with help from the CAR, geographically separated unit (GSU), personnel sup-
port for contingency operation (PERSCO), and casualty augmentation support team (CAST) members.
Defines the MPF commander and designated PERSCO trainer as responsible for ensuring team members
are trained on all aspects of casualty reporting and the training is documented on AF IMT 623, Individual
Training Record. Clarifies when casualty information on foreign nationals during peacetime, to include
terrorist acts, will be released to the installation public affairs office. Deletes the requirement to report
newsworthy events. Standardizes reporting procedures for members who are very seriously ill or injured
(VSI), seriously ill or injured (SI), or who have an incapacitating illness or injury (III) for both overseas
and the continental United States (CONUS). Clarifies the Emergency Family Member Travel Program
responsibilities and procedures. Adds new addresses to Table 2.1. Deletes the requirement for HQ AFPC/
DPFCS to send condolence mailgrams to the next of kin (NOK) who were either present when the casu-
alty occurred or notified by a source other than Air Force. Implements the requirements of Title 10,
U.S.C., Chapter 76, Sections 1501-1513, Missing Persons, and DoDI 2310.5, Accounting for Missing
Persons, pertaining to declaring personnel missing under hostile conditions. Defines and clarifies respon-
sibilities for death, duty status-whereabouts unknown (DUSTWUN), or missing notifications (non-hostile
and hostile). Includes information on communication support for notification officers and teams. Adds
new benefit information and additional casualty assistance instructions for active Air Force members, Air
National Guard (ANG) and United States Air Force Reserve (USAFR) members in a duty status, retiree
deaths within and more than 120 days after retirement. Defines and clarifies circumstance and condolence
letters in separate sections. Adds instructions and procedures for management of the Air Force Virtual
Record of Emergency Data (vRED), and provides new instructions for completing, maintaining, and dis-
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                                                               3


tributing the DD Form 93, Record of Emergency Data. Deletes the requirement to forward DD Forms 93
to HQ AFPC/DPFCS on disc. Deletes requirement for use of AF Form 1246, Record of Emergency Data
Mailing Envelope, AF Form 5, Certificate of Honorable Service, and AF Form 1312, Report of
Retired Casualty. Adds a new chapter on Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance (SGLI), Family Mem-
ber Servicemembers' Group Life Insurance (FSGLI), and Veterans’ Group Life Insurance (VGLI), and
supersedes AFI 36-3008, 20 May 1994. Deletes the following attachments: CONUS Emergency Family
Member Travel confirmation message; sample death notification letter worksheet; benefits for depen-
dents and survivors of active duty Air Force casualties; and benefits for dependents and survivors of
retired Air Force casualties: casualty assistance area of responsibility by zone improvement plan (ZIP)
Code; Survivor Benefit Plan (SBP) Annuity message. Adds a format and specific instruction paragraph to
Attachment 2 through Attachment 5, and Attachment 10 through Attachment 15, and a specific
instruction paragraph to Attachment 6. Adds item L, Emergency Family Member Travel to the Medical
Progress Report. Adds the following new attachments: Abbreviated “Hasty” casualty report for multiple
reportable casualties or incident; Air Force retiree death within 120 days after retirement; retired Air
Force general officer death; and a sample condolence letter from a squadron commander. Expands the
information in the Casualty Notification Officer Checklist. The bar (|) preceding the title indicates a major
revision from the previous edition.
(50SW) The Casualty Services AFI, AFI 36-3002, requires written instructions outlining the responsibil-
ities of various agencies. This publication needs a complete revision due to title changes, organization
changes and new information in accordance with the new AFI which was published in July 2005. A bar
( | ) indicates a revision from the previous edition.
(50SW) (Note specific changes on topics etc. and location within document)

Chapter 8— SERVICEMEMBERS’ GROUP LIFE INSURANCE (SGLI), FAMILY

                                                    Chapter 1

                         THE AIR FORCE CASUALTY SERVICES PROGRAM

Section 1A—General Information

1.1. Overview.
     1.1.1. Dealing with casualties is an important function of command.
     1.1.2. Commanders at all levels must give the Casualty Services Program their personal attention.
     1.1.3. Prompt, accurate reporting, dignified and humane notification, and efficient, thorough, and
     compassionate assistance to the next of kin (NOK) are the program’s primary goals.
     1.1.4. This instruction outlines the Air Force’s obligations to members and families of the active Air
     Force, Air National Guard (ANG), United States Air Force Reserve (USAFR), and Air Force retirees.
     1.1.5. Procedures in Chapter 2 through Chapter 5 apply to members of the active Air Force, ANG
     and USAFR in a duty status, and retired Air Force members receiving or eligible to receive retired
     pay.
     1.1.6. Chapter 6 describes casualty reporting, notification, and assistance procedures for members of
     the ANG and USAFR in a non-duty status, and USAFR retired awaiting pay at age 60.
     1.1.7. The CAR provides limited casualty services to members of sister Services, certain foreign
     nationals, and civilians as indicated in Table 1.1.
     1.1.8. See AFI 36-809, Civilian Survivor Assistance, for casualty notification and assistance proce-
     dures for appropriated fund civilian employees, including USAFR and ANG Title 5 employees.

1.2. Program Objectives.
     1.2.1. To closely track all casualty reports and notifications in accordance with procedures set by
     AFPC, Directorate of Force Operations (DPF).
     1.2.2. The CAR reports casualties, ensures timely notification has been made to the NOK, and pro-
     vides compassionate assistance to NOK until all claims and personal affairs are settled.
     1.2.3. To eliminate delays in providing benefits to the NOK.

1.3. HQ AFPC/DPFC Responsibilities.
     1.3.1. Administers policies on deceased, missing, duty status-whereabouts unknown (DUSTWUN),
     very seriously ill or injured (VSI), seriously ill or injured (SI), incapacitating illness or injury (III), and
     not seriously ill or injured (NSI) personnel.
     1.3.2. Administers the worldwide personal notification program.
     1.3.3. Monitors the casualty assistance program.
     1.3.4. Refers ANG and USAFR units without an MPF to the nearest active duty Air Force installation
     for help in carrying out their casualty service responsibilities.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                   15


1.4. MAJCOM or Comparable Command Level Responsibilities.
   1.4.1. Ensures squadron commanders are provided casualty services information and training during
   the MAJCOM Commander’s Orientation Program.
   1.4.2. Establishes procedures to ensure:
      1.4.2.1. Installation MPFs publish required supplements to this AFI defining responsibilities
      between base agencies when dealing with casualty cases.
      1.4.2.2. Installation MPFs conduct an annual review of the installation supplement to this AFI for
      currency and accuracy of information.
      1.4.2.3. Host tenant support agreements are in place between active duty and Air Reserve Com-
      ponent and Guard MPFs.
   1.4.3. Each ANG state headquarters will maintain a roster of designated unit casualty representatives.

1.5. Installation Commander Responsibilities.
   1.5.1. Implements the installation’s Casualty Services Program by:
      1.5.1.1. Ensuring all base agencies fully support the objectives of the Air Force Casualty Services
      Program, and providing the CAR access to all known information and documents needed to report
      casualties (see Table 5.2.).
      1.5.1.2. Determining the servicemember’s casualty status.
      1.5.1.3. Informing the NOK of all known circumstances surrounding the servicemember’s death.
      1.5.1.4. Approving the release of personnel (including ANG and USAFR personnel) assigned and
      performing duties as the CAR or casualty standby duty from other additional duties which conflict
      with casualty duties. EXAMPLE: A member of the Critical Incident Stress Management (CISM)
      Team.

1.6. MPF Commander Responsibilities.
   1.6.1. Provides the CAR a private office for counseling the NOK.
   1.6.2. Assign responsibility for casualty services at its level, to include GSUs, and inform HQ AFPC/
   DPFCS by submitting an original AF IMT 1075, whenever a change occurs and annually on 1 Octo-
   ber.
   1.6.3. Assigns only casualty-related duties as the CAR’s primary duties and responsibilities, not as an
   additional duty.
   1.6.4. Publishes required installation supplements to this AFI, and conducts an annual review of the
   supplements for currency and accuracy of information.
   1.6.5. Ensures a host-tenant support agreement is in place between the active duty and Air Reserve
   Component and Guard MPF.
   1.6.6. Establishes casualty reporting procedures, to include chains of command, on what the CAR
   should do when reporting of casualties becomes impossible because of an attack on the installation,
   natural disaster, or any other circumstances.
16                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


     1.6.7. Appoints the CAST members in writing.
     1.6.8. Ensures casualty services training is conducted IAW this AFI, to include the CAR, PERSCO
     and CAST members, GSUs, and squadron commanders.
     1.6.9. Ensures the CAR, PERSCO and CAST members are exercised and evaluated on casualty sce-
     narios at every available opportunity.
     1.6.10. For situations involving multiple casualties:
        1.6.10.1. Authorizes recall of the CAST to augment the CAR, as necessary.
        1.6.10.2. Requests temporary duty (TDY) manning assistance from other MPFs to provide addi-
        tional support for casualty reporting, assistance, and other duties as necessary.
        1.6.10.3. Determines if the CAST must submit abbreviated casualty reports whenever the MPF
        cannot establish telephone contact with HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
     1.6.11. Monitors casualty assistance cases to ensure satisfactory assistance is being provided to the
     NOK.
     1.6.12. Establishes procedures to ensure the CAR:
        1.6.12.1. Reviews the active duty and retiree deceased casualty assistance cases and administra-
        tively closes casualty assistance cases within 6 months from date of death.
        1.6.12.2. Completes an AF IMT 58, on both active duty and retired cases, to include:
            1.6.12.2.1. A chronological record of contacts with the NOK, other government agencies,
            civilian agencies, and CAR’s actions on behalf of the NOK.
            1.6.12.2.2. Ensuring entries are typed, accurate and include an explanation for benefits
            denied.
            1.6.12.2.3. Retaining in each casualty case file copies of all messages, memorandums, and
            claim forms sent to agencies and the NOK, and any other relevant documents.
            1.6.12.2.4. Maintaining and disposing of cases IAW AFI 37-138, and AF Records Disposition
            Schedule (RDS) located at https://webrims.amc.af.mil/index.cfm, table 36-3.

1.7. Casualty Assistance Representative Responsibilities.
     1.7.1. Prepares written instructions to supplement this AFI (without duplication), outlining the
     responsibilities of the:
        1.7.1.1. Installation command post.
        1.7.1.1. (50SW) Installation Command Post. Will immediately notify the Casualty Assistance
        Representative (CAR) or the on-call casualty representative when learning of a casualty of an
        active duty member assigned to Schriever AFB, this includes active duty members who are
        declared dead; very seriously injured (VSI); seriously ill or injured (SI), as determined by military
        medical personnel IAW AFI 36-3002; duty status-whereabouts unknown (DUSTUN), as deter-
        mined by the responsible commander; or missing, as determined by HQ AFPC/DPFC. All first
        responders to casualty incidents will immediately contact the CP. The CP in turn will notify the
        CAR and appropriate agencies according to their emergency checklists. CP will be responsible for
        Operational Reporting
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                17


     1.7.1.2. Unit commanders.
     1.7.1.2. (50SW) Unit Commanders.
        1.7.1.2.1. (Added-50SW) Unit commanders and their representatives must ensure the 50 SW
        Command Post is notified of all casualties (to include VSI and SI) who are assigned to their
        unit.
        1.7.1.2.2. (Added-50SW) The unit commander or designated representative will maintain
        close contact with the active duty member’s doctor and ensure the family, CP and CAR is kept
        informed of the member’s condition. They will also act as the Casualty Notification Officer
        (CNO) for deceased members assigned to the unit who’s Next-of Kin (NOK) reside in the
        area.
        1.7.1.2.3. (Added-50SW) If Emergency Family Member Travel (EFMT) is approved, the
        unit commander will assign a unit member to act as a personal escort to the NOK. The com-
        mander will brief the escort on duties contained in AFI 36-3002, paragraphs 2.29.4.3.2. and
        2.29.4.3.3.
        1.7.1.2.4. (Added-50SW) Unit commanders will ensure no unauthorized notification of NOK
        is made by unit members or co-workers, and provide all available information to 50 MSS/
        DPM. Under no circumstances will unit commanders make casualty notification without prior
        guidance and instruction from the HQ AFPC Casualty Services Branch via the Casualty Assis-
        tance Office. Commanders will also perform casualty notification only after coordinating with
        the Schriever CAR or the on-call casualty representative.
        1.7.1.2.5. (Added-50SW) Unit commanders will send circumstance and condolence letters to
        NOK of deceased military members within 5 calendar days from the date the Air Force noti-
        fies the NOK of the casualty. Commanders may have information pertaining to the casualty
        such as drug/alcohol, disciplinary, personal or mental problems which may be required for cir-
        cumstance letters. If the member’s conduct was improper, the facts should be related truthfully
        and tactfully, with as much empathy as possible. These facts must be reported to 50 MSS/
        DPM. The circumstance and condolence letters must be approved by the CAR before sending
        them to the NOK.
        1.7.1.2.6. (Added-50SW) Unit commanders will complete an AF IMT 348, Line of Duty
        Determination on all active duty deaths.
        1.7.1.2.7. (Added-50SW) Unit commanders and their Support Staff (CSS) will require all
        newly assigned personnel to have a current virtual Record of Emergency Data (vRED) on file
        in the virtual Military Personnel Flight (vMPF) and stress the importance of keeping the vRED
        current for prompt notification of NOK. Commanders will establish procedures to ensure
        members departing for TDY in excess of 30 days have a current vRED prior to departure.
     1.7.1.3. Security Forces.
     1.7.1.3. (50SW) 50 SFS (Security Forces). On all calls received pertaining to an active duty
     casualty, obtain (as possible): name, grade, SSAN, place of occurrence, brief account of the cir-
     cumstances, and the informant’s name and phone number. Provide this information to the CP and
     the CAR (Schriever MPF).
18                                                  AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        1.7.1.3.1. (Added-50SW) When necessary, assist the CAR in obtaining information neces-
        sary to complete casualty reporting by coordinating with other law enforcement agencies to
        obtain copies of accident reports for casualty case files.
     1.7.1.4. Medical treatment facility (MTF) personnel.
     1.7.1.4. (50SW) 21 MDG (Medical Treatment Facility/Schriever AFB Clinic). Immediately
     notifies Schriever CAR or the standby casualty representative and the 50 SW/CP of an active duty
     member, or dependant family member assigned to Schriever AFB, or retired member’s death that
     falls within Schriever AFB’s responsibility as outlined in the zip code listing IAW AFI 36-3002.
        1.7.1.4.1. (Added-50SW) Provides a 24-hour point of contact for medical confirmation of
        details, to include, name, time and date, place of accident, causative agents, name of individ-
        ual(s) that notified NOK if present, and NOK that were notified and the date/time notified.
        1.7.1.4.2. (Added-50SW) Medical personnel will notify the CP and the member’s com-
        mander of VSI, SI, and incapacitating illness or injury (III) personnel who are in the base
        clinic or civilian hospitals. Patient Affairs will assign a Case Manager for hospitalized mem-
        bers who will report condition and prognosis updates to the CAR as needed for casualty
        reporting.
        1.7.1.4.3. (Added-50SW) Provide a qualified medical attendant to assist in notification of the
        NOK. Will provide a standby list of medical attendants to 50 MSS/DPM and 50 SW/CP to
        accompany the notification officer on casualty notifications.
        1.7.1.4.4. (Added-50SW) Assist 50 MSS/DPM in obtaining copies of autopsy/toxicology
        reports, death certificates, and medical examiners/coroners reports.
     1.7.1.5. Installation chaplains.
     1.7.1.5. (50SW) 50 SW/HC (Chapel Services). Provides a standby duty roster to 50 MSS/DPM
     and 50 SW/CP of on-call chaplain support to assist in casualty notification actions. The Duty
     Chaplain will serve as a member of the notification team and assist the Casualty Notification
     Officer in the event assistance to the NOK is necessary. At no time shall the Duty Chaplain be
     required to make the casualty notification alone.
     1.7.1.6. Mortuary services officer.
     1.7.1.6. (50SW) 50 SVD (Mortuary Affairs Officer). Provides 50 MSS/DPM and 50 SW/CP
     with a 24-hour on-call duty roster of points of contact. Additionally, the Mortuary Affairs Officer
     provides evidence of viewing, information of confirmation of death, and any other information
     pertinent to the incident as soon as it becomes available.
        1.7.1.6.1. (Added-50SW) Assists the Person Authorized to Direct Disposition (PADD) or
        NOK with funeral arrangements, to include military honors and uniform preparation. Briefs
        the PADD/NOK on status of remains and transportation support to desired resting place of the
        deceased.
        1.7.1.6.2. (Added-50SW) Provides training to the Family Liaison Officer appointed by the
        unit commander.
     1.7.1.7. Civilian personnel flight (CPF).
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    19


     1.7.1.7. (50SW) 50 MSS (Civilian Personnel Flight). If a civilian employee death occurs while
     on duty, the CPF will assist in locating the employees NOK. The unit commander and immediate
     supervisor will notify the NOK in person if in the local area.
        1.7.1.7.1. (Added-50SW) The CPF will counsel the NOK on benefits and assist with claim
        forms.
        1.7.1.7.2. (Added-50SW) The CPF will provide the CAR with information necessary for
        casualty reporting.
     1.7.1.8. Family support center (FSC).
     1.7.1.8. (50SW) 50 MSS (Airman & Family Readiness Center). The A&FRC will furnish the
     CP and CAR with an on-call flight representative, in case of an active duty death and the NOK
     needs immediate assistance.
     1.7.1.9. Transportation officer.
     1.7.1.9. (50SW) 50 LRF (Transportation Officer). The LRF will provide a vehicle upon
     request from the CAR for the notification team. When possible, the Transportation Officer will
     bring the vehicle to building 210 for the team to sign it out in order to prevent a delay in notifica-
     tion to the NOK.
     1.7.1.10. Base telecommunications center and telephone operators.
     1.7.1.10. (50SW) 50 SCS (Base Telecommunications center and telephone operators).
     Ensures all base telephone operators expedite or prioritize all calls pertaining to casualties. Oper-
     ators will relay casualty calls to the 50 SW/CP at extension 567-2180. The CP in turn, is responsi-
     ble for notifying the CAR at the casualty office, home phone number or on the casualty cell phone,
     440-6072.
     1.7.1.11. Public affairs (PA) office.
     1.7.1.11. (50SW) 50 SW (Public Affairs). Upon confirmation and verification from the MPF
     commander of official notification to the NOK, releases information and details of the casualty
     IAW applicable Air Force Instructions.
        1.7.1.11.1. (Added-50SW) For media event situations, the PA officer will assist families in
        how to deal with the civilian media, and offer assistance with any public statements and fam-
        ily’s desires on how and when to answer media questions.
     1.7.1.12. Disaster preparedness office.
     1.7.1.12. (50SW) 50 CES (Emergency Management). Ensure the 50 MSS Office of Collateral
     Responsibility (OCR) member to the Emergency Operations Center is trained. The MSS OCR will
     assist the on-scene commander and local agencies as needed and will ensure the CAR receives all
     information required for casualty reporting. The 50 MSS OCR will prepare checklists to imple-
     ment actions specified in 50 SW Full Spectrum Threat Response Plan 10-2, if tasked.
     1.7.1.13. ARC MPF attached to or on the installation.
     1.7.1.13. (50SW) 50 CPTS (Financial Services). Prepares death gratuity checks within 24 hours
     after death notification, or as required. Finance will provide the casualty office an on-call list of
     personnel to be contacted during duty/ non-duty hours, who are capable of processing documenta-
     tion and issuing a death gratuity check.
20                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        1.7.1.14. (Added-50SW) AFOSI/Det 807 (Office of Special Investigations). Assists the CAR
        in acquiring civilian police reports, autopsy, toxicology, coroner or medical examination reports
        or copies of court verdicts, when OSI directives allow.
        1.7.1.15. (Added-50SW) 50 SW/JA (Legal Office). The Legal Office will provide the CAR
        with a finalized copy of Line of Duty Determinations on all active duty deaths.
        1.7.1.16. (Added-50SW) 50 SW/IG (Exercise Evaluation Team (EET)). The EET will plan
        detailed and realistic exercise scenarios using AFI 36-3002 as a reference for events involving
        casualties.. By integrating the AFI with exercise scenarios, EET will ensure the CAR and Casualty
        Augmentation Support Team receive valuable experience for real world casualty and mass casu-
        alty reporting.
     1.7.2. Addresses these situations in the supplemental instructions:
        1.7.2.1. Prompt and effective reporting of casualties as listed in Table 1.1.
        1.7.2.2. Notifying the NOK.
        1.7.2.3. Providing assistance to the NOK.
        1.7.2.4. Handling calls or requests from the NOK and from government agencies.
        1.7.2.5. Handling calls from the general public and the news media (refer to the installation PA
        office).
        1.7.2.6. Reporting military and civilian casualties from assigned or attached units (see Table 1.1.)
        occurring on or near the installation during both on-duty and off-duty hours.
        1.7.2.7. Reaching the MPF casualty standby representatives during off-duty hours.
        1.7.2.8. Obtaining information from MTF and civilian hospitals during on-duty and off-duty
        hours on personnel classified as deceased, VSI, SI, III, NSI, imminent death, or responding to sit-
        uations involving multiple casualties.
     1.7.3. Ensures the MPF commander or mission support squadron (MSS) commander sends the instal-
     lation supplemental instruction to this AFI, with a signed transmittal memorandum, through MAJ-
     COM to HQ AFPC/DPFCS, 550 C Street West, Suite 14, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4716 for
     coordination according to AFI 33-360, volume 1. EXCEPTION: Air Reserve Component units, see
     paragraphs 1.8.2.1. and 1.8.2.2.
     1.7.4. Sends, e-mails or faxes an original AF IMT 1075 listing MPF personnel responsible for casu-
     alty standby duties, whenever a change occurs and annually on 1 October to HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
     1.7.5. Sends, e-mails or faxes an original AF IMT 1075 to HQ AFPC/DPFCS listing all officers
     (major and above) assigned casualty services duties at serviced GSUs outside a 50-mile radius of an
     active duty base, whenever a change occurs and annually on 1 October.
     1.7.6. Trains all casualty services personnel at serviced GSUs, PERSCO and CAST members, using
     this AFI, the installation supplemental instructions, and sample messages and letters for reporting
     casualties and notifying NOK.
     1.7.7. Provides the mortuary services officer and the PA office the following information once all
     family members have been notified:
        1.7.7.1. Member’s name and rank.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                  21


      1.7.7.2. Age.
      1.7.7.3. Home of record.
      1.7.7.4. Race and religion.
      1.7.7.5. Total Active Federal Military Service Date (TAFMSD).
      1.7.7.6. Awards, decorations, and badges.
   1.7.8. If a family member dies, ensures the member is advised of the opportunity to apply for a
   humanitarian reassignment (see AFI 36-2110, Assignments, attachment 7):
      1.7.8.1. Discusses humanitarian reassignments with the member discreetly at an appropriate time
      and place.
   1.7.9. When an incident involves multiple casualties:
      1.7.9.1. Recalls the CAST on orders from the MPF commander.
      1.7.9.2. Establishes immediate telephone contact (DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048) with HQ
      AFPC/DPFCS, if possible.
      1.7.9.3. Coordinates with military and civilian organizations, including local hospitals and local
      authorities, to expedite the flow of information for casualty reporting.
      1.7.9.4. Advises the installation commander or on-scene commander on conclusive evidence of
      death (see paragraph 2.9.) if recovery and positive identification of remains are delayed or impos-
      sible.
   1.7.10. Reports the status of casualties to HQ AFPC/DPFCS and intermediate levels of command and
   interested agencies.
   1.7.11. Assists commanders with notifications to the NOK.
   1.7.12. Provides assistance to the NOK or other eligible beneficiaries of a deceased member to claim
   all government and civilian benefits to which they are entitled.
      1.7.12.1. Advises the NOK of their right to request a copy of all required documentation on the
      case in accordance with Public Law 102-484, Section 1072, National Defense Authorization Act.
   1.7.13. Becomes familiar with the role and responsibilities of the family liaison officer (FLO), and
   AFI 34-1101, Assistance to Survivors of Persons Killed in Air Force Aviation Mishaps and Other
   Incidents.
      1.7.13.1. Establishes a cohesive working relationship with each appointed FLO.
      1.7.13.2. Ensures the base mortuary officer is aware of the CAR’s role in assisting the next of kin
      in the application for benefits and entitlements.
      1.7.13.3. Provides training to potential FLOs when requested by the installation Survivor Assis-
      tance Program Manager (generally the installation mortuary officer).

1.8. Air Reserve Component MPF Responsibilities.
   1.8.1. Helps ANG or USAFR unit commanders, including GSUs, in preparing written instructions to
   supplement this AFI (without duplication) for ANG, USAFR, or active duty casualties.
22                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        1.8.1.1. Conducts an annual review of the supplement for currency and accuracy of information.
     1.8.2. Ensures the MPF commander or MSS commander signs a transmittal memorandum, and sends
     the supplemental instructions to the appropriate office:
        1.8.2.1. For ANG, sends the instructions through the state adjutant general and ANG/DPFOC,
        1411 Jefferson Davis Highway, Suite 10500, Arlington VA 22202-3231, to HQ AFPC/DPFCS for
        review and coordination, according to AFI 33-360, volume 1.
        1.8.2.2. For USAFR, sends the instructions through Headquarters Air Force Reserve, Customer
        Service Branch (HQ AFRC/DPMC), 155 2nd Street, Robins AFB GA 31098-1635, to HQ AFPC/
        DPFCS for review and coordination according to AFI 33-360, volume 1.
     1.8.3. Ensures a host-tenant support agreement is in place between the ARC and active duty MPF.
     1.8.4. Sends, e-mails or faxes an original AF IMT 1075, listing MPF personnel qualified for casualty
     reporting, notification, and assistance, and casualty standby duties, whenever a change occurs and
     annually on 1 October to HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
        1.8.4.1. For ANG MPFs, sends one copy to ANG/DPFOC, 1411 Jefferson Davis Highway, Suite
        10500, Arlington VA 22202-3231.

1.9. Designated PERSCO Trainer Responsibilities.
     1.9.1. Ensures team members are trained on all aspects of casualty reporting and ensures such train-
     ing is documented on AF IMT 623.
     1.9.2. Establishes procedures for reporting casualties to include:
        1.9.2.1. Communicating to and from the deployed site.
        1.9.2.2. Transmitting casualty reports to and from the deployed site.
        1.9.2.3. Establishing liaisons with military and civilian hospitals within the deployed site.
        1.9.2.4. Briefing deployment commanders of casualty duties and responsibilities.

1.10. Individual Member’s Responsibilities.
     1.10.1. All active AF, ANG and USAFR members must support the AF Casualty Services Program.
     1.10.2. Department of Defense Instruction (DoDI) 1300.18, requires any person serving in a Depart-
     ment of Defense (DoD) component to participate in the casualty notification program.
     1.10.3. Any officer, including some noncommissioned officers, may act as the personal representa-
     tive of the AF Chief of Staff to notify NOK:
        1.10.3.1. Master sergeant through chief master sergeant may only be used to notify the NOK of a
        VSI, SI, or III member, if assigned.
        1.10.3.2. Performs this duty with dignity, compassion, and consideration for the NOK.

1.11. Required Casualty Services. Table 1.1. provides a list of required casualty actions for general cat-
egories of military and civilian personnel.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                 23


   1.11.1. Unit commanders (or designated representatives) notify the NOK or other concerned persons
   of:
       1.11.1.1. A military or civilian member’s casualty status.
       1.11.1.2. Search efforts for DUSTWUN or missing military or civilian members.
       1.11.1.3. Medical progress on military VSI, SI, or III members.
   1.11.2. The CAR or deployed PERSCO team chief:
       1.11.2.1. Reports the status of casualties to HQ AFPC/DPFCS and other interested agencies listed
       in Table 2.1., Table 2.2. and Table 2.3.
   1.11.3. The CAR:
       1.11.3.1. The CAR assists commanders with notifications to the NOK.
       1.11.3.2. Provides assistance to the NOK or other eligible beneficiaries of a deceased member to
       claim all government and civilian benefits to which they are entitled.

Section 1B—Administrative Requirements

1.12. Releasing Casualty Information.
   1.12.1. The following publications apply to releasing information on Air Force casualties:
       1.12.1.1. AFI 35-101, Public Affairs Policies and Procedures.
       1.12.1.2. AFSUPDODR 5400.7, Freedom of Information Act Program.
       1.12.1.3. AFI 33-332, Air Force Privacy Act Program.
   1.12.2. Section 546 of Public Law 108-136, the National Defense Authorization Act for FY 2004.
       1.12.2.1. No casualty information on deceased military personnel may be released to the media or
       general public until 24 hours after notification of the next of kin.

1.13. Adverse Effects. Each person involved in the casualty reporting, notification and assistance pro-
cess should give every consideration to ensure the release of casualty information does not adversely
affect the member, the NOK, the Air Force, or public morale.

1.14. Peacetime Casualties.
   1.14.1. After the CAR confirms with HQ AFPC/DPFCS (AF Casualty Operations) that all NOK have
   been notified, the MPF commander is authorized to release casualty information to the installation PA
   office:
       1.14.1.1. If the casualty is an Air Force member, notification officer must confirm completed
       notification with the servicing CAR and HQ AFPC/DPFCS before the MPF commander releases
       the names of the casualty to the installation PA office.
       1.14.1.2. If the casualty is a foreign national, information will not be released until HQ AFPC/
       DPFCS confirms notification through the embassy attaché, Ministry of Defense, or equivalent.

1.15. Hostile Casualties and Terrorist Acts.
24                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


     1.15.1. When the United States is involved in hostilities or terrorist acts, HQ AFPC/DPFCS releases
     casualty information to HQ AFPC/PA after notifying all NOK.
     1.15.2. HQ AFPC/PA forwards the information to OASD/PA for initial public release.
     1.15.3. The CAR refers all requests for information on any hostile casualty (including those from
     friendly fire) to the installation PA office.
     1.15.4. The installation PA office refers requests for information from members of Congress and state
     or local officials to the Secretary of the Air Force, Office of Legislative Liaison (SAF/LL).

1.16. Information that May be Shared with Public Affairs.
     1.16.1. The Privacy Act determines the type of personal information that may be shared with PA, and
     varies depending on the type of casualty.
     1.16.2. Follow the guidelines in the following paragraphs, unless otherwise instructed (EXCEP-
     TION: If a member does not want their NOK notified, do not provide any information to PA).
        1.16.2.1. For ill or injured casualties, personal information that may be released includes:
            1.16.2.1.1. Name and sex.
            1.16.2.1.2. Rank, date of rank, commission source, and promotion number.
            1.16.2.1.3. Assigned CONUS unit and Service or job specialty.
            1.16.2.1.4. Pay date, military base pay and allowances (EXCEPTIONS: Basic Allowance for
            Housing (BAH) or Family Separation Allowance would indicate marital and family status).
            1.16.2.1.5. Date entered active duty.
            1.16.2.1.6. Date and location of the incident.
            1.16.2.1.7. Military awards and decorations the member holds.
            1.16.2.1.8. Professional Military Education (PME) completed.
        1.16.2.2. For ill or injured casualties, information not shared without the member’s permission
        includes:
            1.16.2.2.1. SSN.
            1.16.2.2.2. Gross pay and BAH.
            1.16.2.2.3. Age or date of birth.
            1.16.2.2.4. National origin and race.
            1.16.2.2.5. Marital status.
            1.16.2.2.6. Home of record, home address and telephone number.
            1.16.2.2.7. Civilian awards.
            1.16.2.2.8. Civilian education completed.
            1.16.2.2.9. Any information on the member’s family.
        1.16.2.3. For deceased casualties, personal information that may be shared includes:
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                              25


          1.16.2.3.1. Name and sex.
          1.16.2.3.2. Rank, date of rank, commission source, promotion number.
          1.16.2.3.3. Assigned CONUS unit and Service or job specialty.
          1.16.2.3.4. Date entered active duty.
          1.16.2.3.5. Pay date, military base pay, and allowances (EXCEPTION: BAH would indicate
          marital and family status).
          1.16.2.3.6. Age and date of birth.
          1.16.2.3.7. Home of record (city and state only).
          1.16.2.3.8. National origin and race.
          1.16.2.3.9. Date and location of the incident.
          1.16.2.3.10. Military awards and decorations the member holds.
          1.16.2.3.11. PME completed.
          1.16.2.3.12. Civilian awards the member holds.
          1.16.2.3.13. Civilian education completed.
      1.16.2.4. For deceased casualties, information that may not be shared without the NOK’s permis-
      sion:
          1.16.2.4.1. Home address and telephone number.
          1.16.2.4.2. Marital status.
          1.16.2.4.3. Names and addresses of the NOK.
          1.16.2.4.4. Information on family members.
          1.16.2.4.5. Specific details concerning the cause and circumstances of death.
      1.16.2.5. For DUSTWUN and Missing casualties in peacetime, personal information that may be
      shared is limited to:
          1.16.2.5.1. Name and rank.
          1.16.2.5.2. Casualty status.
          1.16.2.5.3. Date and location of incident.
      1.16.2.6. During wartime:
          1.16.2.6.1. HQ AFPC/DPF and HQ AFPC/PA, determines what information the AF shares on
          DUSTWUN and Missing members, through SAF/PA.
          1.16.2.6.2. Sharing of specific personal information could jeopardize a member’s chance for
          survival. NOTE: Tell NOK to be aware of this possibility when considering news media inter-
          view requests.

1.17. Transfer of Records on Officers and Enlisted Members.
   1.17.1. See AFI 36-2608, Military Personnel Records System:
26                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        1.17.1.1. Table A6.6, Disposition of Records of an Individual Who Dies.
        1.17.1.2. Table A6.10, Disposition of Records of an Individual Placed in a Missing Status.

1.18. Maintenance and Disposition of Casualty Case Files.
     1.18.1. The CAR should:
        1.18.1.1. Maintain and dispose of casualty case files in accordance with:
            1.18.1.1.1. AFI 37-138.
            1.18.1.1.2. AF Records Disposition Schedule (RDS) located at HTTPS://
            webrims.AMC.af.mil/RDS/INDEX.cfm, table 36-3.
        1.18.1.2. Establish a case file for each assigned casualty and file them alphabetically.
     1.18.2. Case files should contain:
        1.18.2.1. A completed AF IMT 58, on both active duty and retired cases, to include:
            1.18.2.1.1. A chronological record of contacts with the NOK, other government and civilian
            agencies, the CAR’s actions on behalf of the NOK, and an explanation for benefits denied.
            1.18.2.1.2. Copies of all messages, memorandums and claim forms sent to agencies and the
            NOK, and any other relevant documents.
     1.18.3. Installations reporting casualties but having no assistance responsibilities establish an interim
     case file for each casualty reported, containing reporting and notification documents (messages, mem-
     orandums, telegrams, and so on).

1.19. Using DD Form 1300, Report of Casualty (DD-P&R(AR) 1664, Report of Casualty):
     1.19.1. HQ AFPC/DPFCS:
        1.19.1.1. Prepares DD Form 1300 for deceased and missing:
            1.19.1.1.1. Officers and enlisted members in the active Air Force.
            1.19.1.1.2. United States Air Force Academy (USAFA) cadets.
            1.19.1.1.3. ANG and USAFR officers and airmen in a duty status or traveling directly to or
            from duty.
            1.19.1.1.4. Air Force Reserve Officer Training Corps (AFROTC) applicants or cadets partic-
            ipating in or traveling to or from military training.
            1.19.1.1.5. Department of the Air Force (DAF) civilian employees assigned overseas, on
            TDY overseas, or traveling to or from an overseas duty location.
        1.19.1.2. Prepares DD Form 1300 for deceased:
            1.19.1.2.1. Officers and enlisted members in absent without leave (AWOL) or deserter status.
            1.19.1.2.2. Officer and enlisted members retired with pay that die within 120 days of retire-
            ment.
        1.19.1.3. Sends copies of the DD Form 1300 to:
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                               27


         1.19.1.3.1. The CAR assisting the NOK (5 copies).
         1.19.1.3.2. The CAR reporting the casualty (5 copies, if not the same as assisting).
         1.19.1.3.3. The CAR at the member’s permanently assigned base (5 copies, if not the same as
         assisting).
         1.19.1.3.4. AFPC Retirements and Separations Branch (DPPR) (3 copies for active duty
         members).
         1.19.1.3.5. AFPC Rated Management Branch (DPAO) (1 copy, for active duty pilots only).
         1.19.1.3.6. AFPC Staging and Shipping Branch (DPFFCMR) (1 copy for active duty mem-
         bers and 120-day retiree deaths).
         1.19.1.3.7. USAF Senior Leadership Management Office (SLMO), 1040 Air Force, Penta-
         gon, Washington D.C. 20330-1040 (1 copy for colonels (O-6) and above only).
         1.19.1.3.8. Defense Finance and Accounting Service-Denver Center, Special Assistance
         Office (DFAS-DE/PMJ), 6760 East Irvington Place, Denver CO 80279-7000 (1 copy, for
         active duty members).
         1.19.1.3.9. Director/Veterans Affairs (VA) Records Center (233), P.O. Box 5020, St. Louis
         MO 63115-5000 (1 copy, for active duty members and 120-day retiree deaths).
         1.19.1.3.10. Air Force Research Laboratories, Human Effectiveness Bioeffects Division
         (AFRL/HEDB), 2608 Flight Nurse, Bldg 807, Brooks AFB TX 78235-5250 (1 copy for active
         duty members and 120-day retiree deaths).
         1.19.1.3.11. National Cemetery System, Monument System, 810 Vermont Avenue N.W.,
         Washington D.C. 20420 (1 copy for active duty members and 120-day retiree deaths).
         1.19.1.3.12. Defense Manpower Data Center (DMDC) Statistical Information Analysis Divi-
         sion (DMDC/SIAD); 1225 Clark St, Suite 504, Arlington, VA 22202-4302 (1 copy for active
         duty members).
         1.19.1.3.13. Social Security Administration, 727 East Durango, San Antonio TX 78206 (1
         copy for active duty members and 120-day retiree deaths).
  1.19.2. The CAR distributes the DD Form 1300 as follows:
     1.19.2.1. One copy to the summary courts officer.
     1.19.2.2. One copy to the Department of Veterans Affairs (VA) office providing assistance to the
     NOK.
     1.19.2.3. One copy to the Social Security Administration (SSA) office providing assistance to the
     NOK.
     1.19.2.4. One copy to be retained in the case file.
     1.19.2.5. Remaining copies to the NOK.
  1.19.3. Government agencies use DD Form 1300 to:
     1.19.3.1. Pay benefits.
     1.19.3.2. Close active files.
28                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


     1.19.4. The NOK use DD Form 1300 to:
        1.19.4.1. Cash bonds.
        1.19.4.2. Settle commercial insurance claims.
        1.19.4.3. Support any other claims requiring proof of death.

1.20. Using AF IMT 1613, Statement of Service.
     1.20.1. HQ AFPC/DPPR prepares an AF IMT 1613 on active duty members in the Air Force.
     1.20.2. HQ ARPC Service Document Branch (DPPAOR) prepares an AF IMT1613 on all ANG and
     USAFR members regardless of duty status at the time of death.
     1.20.3. AF IMT 1613 verifies a member’s periods of service since DD Forms 214, Certificate of
     Release or Discharge From Active Duty, are not prepared for deceased servicemembers.
     1.20.4. HQ AFPC/DPFCS sends 5 copies of the form to the CAR assisting the NOK.
     1.20.5. The CAR distributes the AF IMT 1613 as follows:
        1.20.5.1. Two copies to the NOK.
        1.20.5.2. One copy to the VA office providing assistance to the NOK.
        1.20.5.3. One copy to the SSA office providing assistance to the NOK.
        1.20.5.4. One copy to be retained in the case file.
     1.20.6. The applicable agency (VA or SSA) requests an AF IMT 1613 for deceased retirees from the
     National Personnel Records Center (NPRC), Military Personnel Records, 9700 Page Ave, St. Louis
     MO 63132-5100, to process claims:
        1.20.6.1. If the CAR receives an AF IMT 1613 on a deceased retiree, the CAR distributes the AF
        IMT 1613 as follows:
            1.20.6.1.1. Two copies to the NOK.
            1.20.6.1.2. One copy to the VA office providing assistance to the NOK.
            1.20.6.1.3. One copy to the SSA office providing assistance to the NOK.
            1.20.6.1.4. One copy to be retained in the case file.

1.21. Obtaining Forms/IMTs. AF IMTs referenced in this instruction are available on the Air Force
Electronic Publishing Web site (http://e-publishing.af.mil). (EXCEPTION: HQ AFPC/DPFCS stocks
and prepares DD Form 1300 and Headquarters Air Reserve Personnel Center stocks and prepares IMT
1613 for Reserve and Guard personnel).
