NOTES:
(X=Mandatory)
     1. Report all military aircraft or Air Mobility Command (AMC) contract or chartered aircraft
        involved in an aircraft accident or incident (regardless of location, mission, or circumstances) to
        HQ AFPC/DPFCS. If there are no casualties submit an abbreviated report (Attachment 13) when
        directed by HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
     2. Applicable to military members only.
     3. Subcategories of Missing include Beleaguered, Besieged, Captured, Detained, Interned, Missing,
        and Missing In Action.
     4. Ensure the requirements of paragraph 2.22., Declaring a Person Missing (Hostile), are met.
     5. Submit an Abbreviated Casualty Report unless otherwise directed by HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
     6. Required when Emergency Family Member Travel authority is requested and approved. (IAW
        JFTR Volume, 1 U 5246, paragraph A, Emergency Family Member Travel is not authorized for
        the families of cadets/midshipmen.)
     7. Required when requesting AFPC to make notification to the NOK.
     8. Casualty services will be provided for all AF inmates who are incarcerated in a military or civilian
        institution and who are still members of the AF. Limited casualty services may be provided for
        inmates who have been released from the AF only when the CAR is requesting HQ AFPC/
        DPFCS assistance to make notification to the NOK.
     9. If the member is able to communicate, the member’s desires will be honored unless, in the judg-
        ment of the commander, this service is necessary.
     10. Whenever a casualty occurs as the result of either hostile action or terrorist activity, initial notifi-
         cation(s) shall also be made in person to parents who are secondary NOK, unless unusual circum-
         stances exist.
     11. Whenever a casualty occurs as the result of hostile action or terrorist activity and the casualty is
         classified as NSI, notification to the NOK will only be made if the member expressly requests it,
         unless in the judgment of the commander this service is necessary.
     12. If an injury or illness renders the member physically or mentally incapable of communicating
         with the NOK or involves serious disfigurement, major diminution of sight or hearing, or loss of a
         major extremity, initial notification(s) shall be made to the NOK.
     13. Contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS by phone or e-mail when assistance is required to resolve claims, ben-
         efits, dependency, or other issues.
     14. Required when requested by the NOK.
     15. Required if directed by HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
     16. Overseas only (non-hostile) for civilians hired in the U.S. and sent abroad.
     17. Casualty assistance is not provided to NOK of deserters.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                33


  18. See AFI 36-809 for instructions on casualty reporting and assistance for civilians. Casualty ser-
      vices for DoD civilian employees are the responsibility of the base civilian personnel flight and
      HQ AFPC/DPCMB. Casualty services for contractors are the responsibility of the contractor’s
      employer. Military casualty services will be performed when directed by HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
  19. Benefits and entitlement counseling provided by the employer.
  20. Dependent deaths will be reported via the SGLV Form 8700, Report of Death of Family Mem-
      ber, if dependent is insured under the Family Member Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance
      (FSGLI) program.
34                                                        AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


                                                  Chapter 2

                                       CASUALTY REPORTING

Section 2A—General Information

2.1. Casualty Reports.
     2.1.1. Overview:
        2.1.1.1. See Table 1.1., Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3., to determine which commander
        submits reports and who receives them.
        2.1.1.2. Report the type of casualty as either:
           2.1.1.2.1. Hostile.
           2.1.1.2.2. Non-Hostile.
           2.1.1.2.3. Pending.
        2.1.1.3. Report the status of the casualty as:
           2.1.1.3.1. Deceased.
           2.1.1.3.2. DUSTWUN.
           2.1.1.3.3. Missing.
           2.1.1.3.4. VSI, SI, II3.16I, or NSI.
           2.1.1.3.5. Return to Military Control.
        2.1.1.4. Reports must include an accurate, explicit account of the circumstances surrounding the
        casualty. NOTE: This information is essential in assisting HQ AFPC/DPFC in further categoriz-
        ing the casualty as killed in action (KIA), missing in action (MIA), detained, captured, etc., for
        reporting to DoD.
     2.1.2. The CAR:
        2.1.2.1. Immediately telephones HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048
        (CONUS bases only) upon learning of a casualty without waiting for confirmation of the data.
        2.1.2.2. Faxes the following documents on military members to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN
        665-2348, then mails the original copies to HQ AFPC/DPFCS the next duty day.
           2.1.2.2.1. vRED/DD Form 93, Record of Emergency Data (if in UPRG).
           2.1.2.2.2. SGLV 8286, Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance Election and Certificate.
           2.1.2.2.3. DD Form 4, Enlistment/Reenlistment Document, Armed Forces of the United
           States (for enlisted members only).
           2.1.2.2.4. Any other VA forms related to SGLI found in Section 1 of the member’s UPRG.
           2.1.2.2.5. For ANG or USAFR casualties:
               2.1.2.2.5.1. A copy of the order or other document placing the member on active duty
               (AD).
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                   35


      2.1.2.3. Prepares Casualty Reports and sends them at once to HQ AFPC/DPFCS by the most
      expeditious means (pouch, courier, or first class mail when telephone or electronic communica-
      tion is not possible due to combat, natural disaster, etc.).
      2.1.2.4. Transmits or delivers to the base telecommunications center, the appropriate casualty
      message, as determined by HQ AFPC/DPFCS, within 4 hours of learning of a casualty. NOTE:
      Casualty Reports are exempt from MINIMIZE.
   2.1.3. Defense Casualty Information Processing System - Forward (DCIPS-Forward) is an unclassi-
   fied casualty reporting system. It is the primary method for transmitting all casualty reports to AFPC/
   DPFCS and other agencies as outlined in Table 2.1., Table 2.2. and Table 2.3.
      2.1.3.1. When DCIPS-Forward is not available, transmit the casualty report using Attachment 2,
      Attachment 3, Attachment 10, Attachment 11, Attachment 12, Attachment 13, Attachment
      14, Attachment 16, and Attachment 17 as appropriate.
   2.1.4. Format for Casualty Reports:
      2.1.4.1. See Attachment 2 through Attachment 5, Attachment 10 through Attachment 14,
      Attachment 16 and Attachment 17 for completion of the appropriate report.
   2.1.5. Initial and Supplemental Casualty Reports:
      2.1.5.1. Casualty Reports are transmitted in an unclassified format.
      2.1.5.2. If any item on the Casualty Report is classified then indicate by stating “classified” for
      that item.
      2.1.5.3. Label unknown or unconfirmed items “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” or “UNCON-
      FIRMED” respectively, and report or confirm the information as soon as possible in a supplemen-
      tal report.
      2.1.5.4. Do not label any item “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” if there is reportable information
      available that would be of interest to family members or of value to the addressees of the report.
      Instead, label such information “UNCONFIRMED.”
      2.1.5.5. Label any item not required or not applicable “N/A.”
      2.1.5.6. If an initial Casualty Report contains incorrect information, submit a supplemental report
      at once and label the corrected items “CORRECTED.”
      2.1.5.7. Prepare initial Casualty Reports on deceased and missing DoD or DAF civilian employ-
      ees overseas in order to facilitate transportation of the NOK and household goods back to
      CONUS.

2.2. Confirming Report Delivery.
   2.2.1. The reporting unit must:
      2.2.1.1. Notify HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 of the
      report’s transmission.
      2.2.1.2. Confirm delivery of all:
          2.2.1.2.1. Initial Casualty Reports.
36                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


            2.2.1.2.2. Search Progress Reports.
            2.2.1.2.3. Medical Progress Reports.
        2.2.1.3. Check with HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048, or the
        telecommunications center, if they transmitted the report, every 2 hours until confirmation of
        delivery by HQ AFPC/DPFCS has been received.

2.3. Reporting Casualties during Exercises.
     2.3.1. The MPF commander or CAR obtains HQ AFPC/DPFCS approval prior to transmitting exer-
     cise Casualty Reports.
     2.3.2. Send exercise Casualty Reports only to addressees:
        2.3.2.1. Participating in the exercise.
        2.3.2.2. Approved by HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
     2.3.3. When sending simulated Casualty Reports for training purposes, follow all procedures as
     though it was a real report:
        2.3.3.1. Indicate “EXERCISE REPEAT EXERCISE” in the subject line and closing sentence.
        2.3.3.2. Place only the “EXERCISE” report or message on the computer disk used for transmis-
        sion.

2.4. Reporting Casualties by Geographically Separated Units (GSU) and PERSCO Teams.
     2.4.1. Immediately report information by telephone (DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048) to HQ
     AFPC/DPFCS and submit an initial report by electronic message as outlined in paragraph 2.1.4.
        2.4.1.1. If a GSU or PERSCO Team does not have electronic message capability, report the infor-
        mation by telephone to the servicing MPF, who then submits the required Casualty Report.
     2.4.2. The CAR at the member's servicing MPF submits a supplemental report completing all
     unknown or unconfirmed information, or items to be supplemented from the member's records within
     4 hours of receiving the initial Casualty Report.

2.5. Reporting Casualties on Members of Other Services (see Table 1.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3.):
     2.5.1. Follow the format for Air Force Casualty Reports and report all applicable items.
     2.5.2. Precede each item by its plain text title so the member's Service, which may not follow the
     same procedures, can understand the data. Do not use abbreviations.

2.6. Reporting Casualties on Foreign Nationals in the United States under the Auspices of the Air
Force:
     2.6.1. The reporting installation includes the orders-issuing headquarters of the appropriate nation’s
     military as an action addressee. If the foreign casualty is assigned as part of the Personnel Exchange
     Program, the reporting installation will include SAF/IAPA as an action addressee. SAF/IAPA will
     coordinate NOK notification and disposition of remains with the appropriate foreign embassy.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    37


   2.6.2. If the orders-issuing headquarters is unknown, send the report to a Military Assistance Advi-
   sory Group (MAAG) or Defense Attaché Office (DAO) in the foreign national's home country.
   2.6.3. If the CAR is unaware of the orders-issuing headquarters or a MAAG or DAO in the foreign
   national’s home country, call these offices to obtain the information:
      2.6.3.1. Headquarters, United States Air Force, Foreign Liaison Division (HQ AF/CVAI), DSN
      225-2251.
      2.6.3.2. The Air Force Operations Center, DSN 227-6103, after duty hours.
   2.6.4. State in the initial Casualty Report that the orders-issuing headquarters will:
      2.6.4.1. Notify the NOK.
      2.6.4.2. Confirm NOK notification by message to all addressees listed on the initial Casualty
      Report.

2.7. Reporting Casualties on Military Aircraft or AMC Commercially Contracted Aircraft:
   2.7.1. Reporting Requirements:
      2.7.1.1. The Air Force requires reports on all casualties resulting from an aircraft incident or dis-
      appearance.
      2.7.1.2. The CAR must account for all personnel aboard the aircraft.
      2.7.1.3. The proper reporting method depends on the nature of the incident and the number of
      casualties. In all incidents, immediately contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone (DSN 665-3505
      or 1-800-433-0048), if possible, to determine which of these methods to use:
          2.7.1.3.1. If the casualties are all NSI, report them immediately by telephone followed by an
          abbreviated Casualty Report (Attachment 13).
          2.7.1.3.2. If there are multiple casualties, make an initial report by telephone and follow it
          with an abbreviated Casualty Report or a standard report as HQ AFPC/DPFCS directs.
          2.7.1.3.3. If telephone contact with HQ AFPC/DPFCS cannot be made, the MPF commander
          or PERSCO team chief determines whether to use an abbreviated or standard Casualty Report
          for initial reporting.
   2.7.2. Determining onboard crew and passengers. These documents and sources can help you deter-
   mine onboard personnel:
      2.7.2.1. Crew: Review DD Form 175, Military Flight Plan. It shows the name, grade, SSN, crew
      position, and home installation of each crewmember.
      2.7.2.2. Passengers:
          2.7.2.2.1. Review available passenger manifests and other documentation from flight origina-
          tion and stops en route. These contain information such as passengers' names, grades, SSNs,
          passport numbers, emergency addresses, and units of assignment.
          2.7.2.2.2. Consult passenger service terminals, base operations, flight control centers at civil-
          ian airports, and AMC Aerial Port Operations offices for information on passengers aboard
          military aircraft.
38                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


            2.7.2.2.3. If difficulties are encountered in obtaining the information, immediately contact
            HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone (DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048) and they will request
            assistance from HQ AMC Tanker Airlift Control Center, Aerial Port Control Center (HQ
            AMC TACC/XOGC) (DSN 576-1755).
     2.7.3. Release of Casualty Information: Installation commanders must be able to determine casualty
     statuses. Crew and passenger names, and any other information that would assist commanders in mak-
     ing casualty determinations, will be immediately released to the CAR.

2.8. Reporting Casualties on DoD and DAF Civilian Employees. (See Table 1.1., note 18; Table 2.2.,
and Table 2.3.)
     2.8.1. The Air Force requires reports on DoD and DAF civilian employees in certain circumstances.
     Refer to Table 1.1. for guidance.
     2.8.2. Immediately report information by telephone (DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048) to HQ
     AFPC/DPFCS and submit an initial report by electronic message as outlined in paragraph 2.1.4.
     2.8.3. Follow the format for Air Force Casualty Reports and report all applicable items.

Section 2B—Reports on Deceased Persons

2.9. Obtaining Conclusive Evidence of Death.
     2.9.1. The installation commander or the on-scene commander must obtain conclusive evidence
     before reporting the death of an individual.
     2.9.2. If more than one commander or Service is involved, they must coordinate their investigations
     and agree on their casualty status determinations:
        2.9.2.1. Do not submit a Casualty Report until all involved commanders agree on their determina-
        tions.
        2.9.2.2. If the commanders cannot reach an agreement, consult HQ AFPC/DPFCS (DSN
        665-3505) for instructions.
     2.9.3. The Air Force does not require recovery of remains for conclusive evidence of death, since sit-
     uations will arise where remains cannot be recovered, but where the chance of survival is deemed
     impossible. The important factor is whether or not the commanders determine that survival is possi-
     ble.
        2.9.3.1. The Air Force considers these situations to be conclusive evidence of death:
            2.9.3.1.1. The commander determines death is the only plausible explanation for the mem-
            ber’s absence.
            2.9.3.1.2. Available information indicates beyond any reasonable doubt that an individual
            could not have survived. Such information includes:
                2.9.3.1.2.1. Statements of witnesses to the incident.
                2.9.3.1.2.2. Circumstances of the incident.
                2.9.3.1.2.3. Search results.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    39


              2.9.3.1.2.4. Local conditions of terrain, climate, water temperature and currents, etc.
           2.9.3.1.3. The total number of individual remains recovered from an aircraft or group accident
           equals the total number of persons known to be on board the aircraft or in the group, unless
           there is reasonable doubt:
              2.9.3.1.3.1. As to whether the remains are from the aircraft or group in question.
              2.9.3.1.3.2. Regarding the validity of the aircraft clearance and passenger manifest
              records.

2.10. Local Laws Governing Brain Death. The CAR must be aware of local laws governing brain
death, as they differ among states and countries. Submit death reports in accordance with the local legal
definition of brain death.

Section 2C—Reports on Members Declared DUSTWUN or Persons Declared Missing (Non-Hostile
and Hostile)

2.11. Declaring a Member DUSTWUN.
   2.11.1. DUSTWUN is a transitory casualty status applicable only to military personnel.
   2.11.2. The responsible commander declares a member DUSTWUN when the commander:
       2.11.2.1. Suspects a member's absence is involuntary and that the member may be a casualty.
       2.11.2.2. Does not feel there is sufficient evidence to make a definitive determination of missing
       (non-hostile), recommendation of missing (hostile), or deceased. DUSTWUN allows the com-
       mander time to gather additional facts and statements from witnesses in order to make a definitive
       status determination (non-hostile), or recommendation of missing (hostile).
   2.11.3. Once a commander declares a military member DUSTWUN, the CAR submits an initial
   DUSTWUN Report (see paragraph 2.14. and Attachment 3) to the addressees in Table 2.1. or Table
   2.2..
   2.11.4. Generally, commanders may not keep a member in DUSTWUN status for more than 10 days,
   unless extended by HQ AFPC/DPFC (DSN 665-2909). During this period, the commander:
       2.11.4.1. Closely monitors the case and makes every effort to determine the member's true status.
       2.11.4.2. Receives the results of any search and investigative efforts.
       2.11.4.3. Submits daily Search Progress Reports (see paragraph 2.15. and Attachment 4) to the
       addressees in Table 2.1. or Table 2.2..

2.12. Factors Commanders Should Consider to Determine Whether a Member's Absence is Volun-
tary or Involuntary.
   2.12.1. Member’s relationship with others both on and off duty:
       2.12.1.1. Marital discord.
       2.12.1.2. Problems with supervisors or coworkers.
   2.12.2. Financial activities prior to or subsequent to disappearance:
40                                                        AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        2.12.2.1. Recent large withdrawals from bank accounts.
        2.12.2.2. Use of credit cards for airline tickets, hotels, or gas.
     2.12.3. Evidence of departure preparations:
        2.12.3.1. Luggage or personal belongings missing from the member's residence.
        2.12.3.2. Remarks made by the member to friends, relatives, or coworkers hinting at the possibil-
        ity of a departure.

2.13. Examples of When it May be Appropriate to Declare a Member DUSTWUN.
     2.13.1. An aircraft is overdue and the responsible commander has made an initial investigation, to
     include the following, with negative results:
        2.13.1.1. Checks of scheduled stops along route.
        2.13.1.2. Possible emergency landing sites.
        2.13.1.3. Other places the aircraft may have landed.
     2.13.2. A member disappears while participating in a recreational activity such as hunting, fishing,
     hiking, or camping:
        2.13.2.1. The member's commander initiates a search for the absent member and investigates the
        circumstances surrounding the member’s disappearance.
            2.13.2.1.1. The search must be sufficiently extensive for the commander to determine
            whether the member could freely return.
            2.13.2.1.2. Include Security Forces, local police, Air Force Office of Special Investigations
            (AFOSI), Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI), and other investigative agencies.
     2.13.3. Initial attempts to find the member fail and the commander determines the member is not
     AWOL.
     2.13.4. A member observes a lead aircraft as it is hit by enemy ground fire. Before the aircraft hits the
     ground, the member observes a flash, possibly from a seat ejection. Hostilities preclude launching a
     search and rescue attempt.
     2.13.5. A member disappears and there are no known circumstances:
        2.13.5.1. Personal belongings such as military ID card, wallet, car keys, checkbook, passport,
        camera, television set, savings bonds, etc., are still in member’s dormitory room or private resi-
        dence.
        2.13.5.2. First sergeant, supervisor and co-workers believe voluntary absence would be out of
        character for the member.

2.14. CAR Responsibilities for Filing DUSTWUN and Subsequent Reports.
     2.14.1. Once a commander declares a military member DUSTWUN:
        2.14.1.1. Immediately telephone HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048
        (CONUS bases only) and advise them of the commander’s decision.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                41


     2.14.1.2. Fax the following documents to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348:
        2.14.1.2.1. vRED/DD Form 93 (if in UPRG).
        2.14.1.2.2. SGLV 8286.
        2.14.1.2.3. DD Form 4 (for enlisted members only).
        2.14.1.2.4. Any other VA forms related to SGLI found in Section 1 of the member’s UPRG.
        2.14.1.2.5. For ANG and USAFR casualties:
            2.14.1.2.5.1. A copy of the order or other document placing the member on AD.
            2.14.1.2.5.2. A statement from the ANG unit finance officer, Reserve Pay Unit, or the
            Defense Finance and Accounting Service-Denver (DFAS-DE) Center indicating the
            amount of Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance deductions and the date of the first and
            last deduction.
     2.14.1.3. Submit an initial DUSTWUN Report (RCS: DD-P&R[AR] 1664, Report of Casualty)
     for military persons indicated in Table 1.1. (see Attachment 3).
  2.14.2. Submit daily Search Progress Reports unless waived by HQ AFPC/DPFCS (see paragraph
  2.15. and Attachment 4).
  2.14.3. Within 10 days of filing the initial DUSTWUN Report, unless extended by HQ AFPC/DPFC
  (DSN 665-2909), the CAR must submit one of these reports or messages (referencing the initial
  DUSTWUN Report):
     2.14.3.1. Death Report (RCS: DD-P&R[AR] 1664, Report of Casualty).
        2.14.3.1.1. Immediately submit an initial Death Report (see Attachment 2) if the commander
        determines a member is dead at any time during the 10-day period:
        2.14.3.1.2. Use the date and time when the member was declared DUSTWUN as the date and
        time of death, unless there is conclusive evidence of a different date or time.
        2.14.3.1.3. If it is impossible to recover remains, state in item H of the initial Death Report
        that the Air Force has investigated the circumstances surrounding the death in accordance with
        this AFI and has determined that there is conclusive evidence of death.
        2.14.3.1.4. Mail original copies of the following documents on military members to HQ
        AFPC/DPFCS:
            2.14.3.1.4.1. vRED/DD Form 93 (if in UPRG).
            2.14.3.1.4.2. SGLV 8286.
            2.14.3.1.4.3. DD Form 4.
            2.14.3.1.4.4. Any other VA forms related to SGLI found in Section 1 of the member’s
            UPRG.
     2.14.3.2. Non-Hostile Missing Report (RCS: DD-P&R[AR]1664, Report of Casualty):
        2.14.3.2.1. Submit an initial Missing Report if the commander declares the member missing
        (see paragraph 2.17. and Attachment 3).
        2.14.3.2.2. Complete items A, B, C, F, G, J, L, M, and N.
42                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


            2.14.3.2.3. Use date and time when the member was declared DUSTWUN as the date and
            time of loss in Item F., unless there is evidence of a different date or time.
            2.14.3.2.4. Include in item G a detailed account of the facts and circumstances surrounding
            the member’s disappearance (see Attachment 3).
        2.14.3.3. AWOL Message:
            2.14.3.3.1. If the commander decides the member’s absence was voluntary, revoke the
            DUSTWUN status with a message to all addressees on the initial DUSTWUN Report.
            2.14.3.3.2. State “CHANGE OF STATUS TO AWOL FROM DUSTWUN” in the subject
            line.
            2.14.3.3.3. Reference the initial DUSTWUN Report.
            2.14.3.3.4. Include items A, B, C, and G from the initial DUSTWUN Report.
            2.14.3.3.5. Explain in detail in item G the rationale for the revocation.
            2.14.3.3.6. State that the member’s official status is AWOL and give the effective date.
            2.14.3.3.7. See AFI 36-2911, Desertion and Unauthorized Absence, for further guidance.
        2.14.3.4. Returned to Military Control Report (RCS: DD-P&R(AR) 1663, Designated Reporting
        of Combat Area Casualties):
            2.14.3.4.1. If the member returns, immediately notify HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at
            DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048.
            2.14.3.4.2. Following the telephone notification to HQ AFPC/DPFCS, submit a Returned to
            Military Control (RMC) Report (see Attachment 5) to all addressees on the initial DUST-
            WUN Report.

2.15. Search Progress Reports on DUSTWUN Members (RCS: HAF-DP[AR]9476, Missing Per-
sons Reports).
     2.15.1. The responsible commander orders a search and investigation for all DUSTWUN situations:
        2.15.1.1. Acceptable search and rescue methods include visual aerial search, ground teams, and
        electronic search.
        2.15.1.2. Electronic monitoring by aircraft flying in the area on other than search and rescue mis-
        sions is not an acceptable search method.
     2.15.2. The CAR submits daily Search Progress Reports to the addressees in Table 2.1. or Table 2.2.
     on:
        2.15.2.1. The extent and progress of the search.
        2.15.2.2. Any pertinent information on the investigation.
     2.15.3. The CAR submits similar Search Progress Reports in hostile situations if a search is possible.
     2.15.4. Once the search is terminated, the commander:
        2.15.4.1. Evaluates all available evidence.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                43


      2.15.4.2. Ensures the CAR submits the appropriate Casualty Report in accordance with paragraph
      2.14.

2.16. Declaring a Person Missing (Non-Hostile).
   2.16.1. This casualty status applies to both military members and civilian personnel.
   2.16.2. When a commander determines that a person's absence is involuntary and there is insufficient
   evidence to declare the person deceased, the commander:
      2.16.2.1. Consults with HQ AFPC/DPFCM by telephone at DSN 665-3752 or 1-800-531-5501
      prior to declaring a person missing or submitting a Missing Report.
      2.16.2.2. After consulting with HQ AFPC/DPFCM, declares the person missing (see Attachment
      1, Terms), and has the CAR submit an initial Missing Report (see paragraph 2.17. and Attach-
      ment 3).
   2.16.3. Declaring a military member missing (non-hostile) automatically invokes the statutory provi-
   sions of 37 U.S.C, chapter 10 (Payments to Missing Persons).
      2.16.3.1. Once the commander declares a person missing and notifies the NOK, HQ AFPC/
      DPFCM must issue any further official correspondence to the NOK, including notifications of a
      change in casualty status to deceased. NOTE: The CAR continues to provide casualty assistance
      to the NOK as described in paragraph 4.5.5.
   2.16.4. The commander must submit AF IMT 484, Non-Hostile Missing Person(s) Supplementary
   Report (see paragraphs 2.18. and 2.19., and Attachment 6), directly to HQ AFPC/DPFCM, and one
   copy to the CAR within 5 calendar days from the date he or she:
      2.16.4.1. Declares the person missing.
      2.16.4.2. Terminates the search for the person.

2.17. CAR Responsibilities for Filing Missing and Subsequent Reports (Non-Hostile).
   2.17.1. When the commander declares a person missing, the CAR:
      2.17.1.1. Immediately telephones HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048
      (CONUS bases only) and advises them of the commander’s decision.
      2.17.1.2. Submits an initial Missing Report (RCS: DD-FM&P[AR] 1664, Report of Casualty) on
      those persons indicated in Table 1.1. (see Attachment 3).
      2.17.1.3. If a military member, faxes the following documents to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN
      665-2348:
          2.17.1.3.1. vRED/DD Form 93 (if in UPRG).
          2.17.1.3.2. SGLV 8286.
          2.17.1.3.3. DD Form 4.
          2.17.1.3.4. Any other VA forms related to SGLI found in Section 1 of the member’s UPRG.
      2.17.1.4. For ANG and USAFR casualties:
          2.17.1.4.1. A copy of the order or other document placing the member on AD.
44                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


            2.17.1.4.2. A statement from the ANG unit finance officer, Reserve Pay Unit, or DFAS-DE
            indicating the amount of Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance deductions and the date of
            the first and last deduction.
     2.17.2. Submit daily Search Progress Reports (see paragraph 2.21., and Attachment 4).
     2.17.3. Immediately notify HQ AFPC/DPFCM by telephone at DSN 665-3752 or 1-800-531-5501 if
     any of these situations develop after submission of an initial Missing Report:
        2.17.3.1. New information:
            2.17.3.1.1. If additional information surfaces that might help HQ AFPC/DPFCM determine
            the person's casualty status:
               2.17.3.1.1.1. Submit a supplemental Missing Report (see Attachment 3).
               2.17.3.1.1.2. Reference the initial Missing Report.
               2.17.3.1.1.3. Complete items A, B, C, and G.
               2.17.3.1.1.4. Describe in item G of the report, the circumstances and factors that justify a
               supplemental report. For example, if the reporting unit learns that a member is categorized
               as missing in action and has been captured, it submits a supplemental Missing Report so
               HQ AFPC/DPFCM can change the casualty category from missing in action to captured.
            2.17.3.1.2. HQ AFPC/DPFCM notifies the NOK as appropriate.
        2.17.3.2. If the commander learns of a missing person being RMC, immediately contact AFPC/
        DPFCM by telephone at DSN 665-3752.
            2.17.3.2.1. Once notification to HQ AFPC/DPFCM has been made, submit an RMC Report
            (see Attachment 5) to all addressees on the initial Missing Report.
            2.17.3.2.2. HQ AFPC/DPFCM notifies the NOK.
        2.17.3.3. AWOL Message:
            2.17.3.3.1. If the commander decides the person's absence is voluntary, revoke the missing
            status with a message to all addressees on the initial Missing Report.
            2.17.3.3.2. State "CHANGE OF STATUS TO AWOL FROM MISSING" in the subject line.
            2.17.3.3.3. Reference the initial Missing Report.
            2.17.3.3.4. Include items A, B, C, and G from the initial Missing Report (see Attachment 3).
            2.17.3.3.5. Explain in detail in item G of the message, the rationale for the revocation.
            2.17.3.3.6. State that the person's official status is AWOL and give the effective date.
            2.17.3.3.7. HQ AFPC/DPFCM notifies the NOK.
            2.17.3.3.8. See AFI 36-2911. for military members, and Federal Regulations (CFR), Part 630,
            Absence and Leave, for civilian personnel, for further guidance.
        2.17.3.4. Death Report (RCS: DD FM&P[AR]1664, Report of Casualty):
            2.17.3.4.1. If the commander determines a missing person is dead, submit an Initial Death
            Report (see Attachment 2) including all addressees on the initial Missing Report.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    45


          2.17.3.4.2. Reference the initial Missing Report.
          2.17.3.4.3. Include in item G of the report, the date and time of death, if known.
          2.17.3.4.4. If it is impossible to recover remains, state in item G that the Air Force has inves-
          tigated the circumstances surrounding the death in accordance with this AFI and has deter-
          mined that there is conclusive evidence of death.
          2.17.3.4.5. Submission of the report does not automatically change the person's casualty sta-
          tus from missing to deceased. The Missing Persons Act requires a formal status review:
          2.17.3.4.6. Only HQ AFPC/DPFCM may officially change the casualty status to deceased.
          2.17.3.4.7. HQ AFPC/DPFCM notifies the NOK if the casualty status is changed to deceased.
          2.17.3.4.8. Mail original copies of the following documents on military members to HQ
          AFPC/DPFCS:
              2.17.3.4.8.1. vRED/DD Form 93 (if in UPRG).
              2.17.3.4.8.2. SGLV 8286.
              2.17.3.4.8.3. DD Form 4, (for enlisted members only).
              2.17.3.4.8.4. Any other VA forms related to SGLI found in Section 1 of the member’s
              UPRG.

2.18. AF IMT 484 (RCS: HAF-DP[AR]9476, Missing Persons Report).
   2.18.1. The responsible commander must submit AF IMT 484 (see Attachment 6), directly to HQ
   AFPC/DPFCM, 550 C Street West, Suite 15, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4717, and one copy to the
   CAR within 5 calendar days from the date he or she recommends placement of a person into missing
   status.
   2.18.2. The commander submits an additional copy of the report through channels to the parent MAJ-
   COM for informational purposes only.
   2.18.3. For an incident that results in multiple missing persons, such as an aircraft mishap, submit one
   report that lists all missing personnel.
      2.18.3.1. Send a copy to each missing person’s home installation commander for information pur-
      poses only, since HQ AFPC/DPFCM is solely responsible for notifying the NOK.
   2.18.4. If the commander cannot submit the AF IMT 484 within the specified time period, notify HQ
   AFPC/DPFCM by message of the reason for the delay and the date you expect to mail the report.
   2.18.5. See Attachment 6 for instructions on completion of the AF IMT 484.

2.19. Submitting AF IMT 484.
   2.19.1. The commander prepares AF IMT 484 based on a review and evaluation of:
      2.19.1.1. The circumstances surrounding the disappearance.
      2.19.1.2. Search results.
      2.19.1.3. Local terrain conditions, climate, water temperature, currents, etc.
46                                                        AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        2.19.1.4. Witness statements (see Attachment 7).
        2.19.1.5. Search and rescue personnel.
        2.19.1.6. Any other relevant information.
     2.19.2. For aircraft accidents and incidents, the commander obtains either of these statements:
        2.19.2.1. Statements from rescued crewmembers and crewmembers of other flights in the area.
        2.19.2.2. Signed statements from crewmembers indicating why they can’t contribute to the
        report.
     2.19.3. The commander sends the form to the installation staff judge advocate to review for:
        2.19.3.1. Legal sufficiency.
        2.19.3.2. Proper preparation of witness statements.
        2.19.3.3. Completeness of the investigation.
     2.19.4. The commander must include either:
        2.19.4.1. A recommendation to change the casualty status to deceased.
        2.19.4.2. Detailed reasons why a person should be placed into a missing status.

2.20. 9-Month Investigation Report on Missing Personnel (Non-Hostile and Hostile) (RCS:
HAF-DP(AR)9476, Missing Persons Reports). If there is no change to a missing person’s casualty sta-
tus within 8 months, the commander concludes the investigation by submitting a 9-month Investigative
Report (see Attachment 8 and Attachment 9) following these guidelines:
     2.20.1. Submits a written report in non-hostile situations.
     2.20.2. The report must arrive at HQ AFPC/DPFCM before the end of the 9th month.
     2.20.3. Attachment 8 explains the contents of the 9-month Investigative Report.
     2.20.4. The report is an integral part of the casualty file used in the formal status review process.
     2.20.5. The review recommends, effective 1 year and 1 day from the date of the initial Missing
     Report, either to continue the missing casualty status or to change the casualty status to deceased.

2.21. Search Progress Reports on Missing Persons (Non-Hostile and Hostile).
     2.21.1. The responsible commander orders a search and investigation.
        2.21.1.1. Acceptable search and rescue methods include visual aerial search, ground teams, and
        electronic search.
        2.21.1.2. Electronic monitoring by aircraft flying in the area on other than search and rescue mis-
        sions is not an acceptable search method.
     2.21.2. The CAR submits daily Search Progress Reports (see Attachment 4) to the addressees in
     Table 2.1. or Table 2.2. on:
        2.21.2.1. The extent and progress of the search.
        2.21.2.2. Any pertinent information on the investigation.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                   47


   2.21.3. Once the search is terminated, the responsible commander:
       2.21.3.1. Evaluates all available evidence.
       2.21.3.2. Ensures the CAR submits the appropriate Casualty Report IAW paragraph 2.17. or 2.22.

2.22. Declaring a Person Missing (Hostile).
   2.22.1. This casualty status applies to military members, DoD civilian employees, or DoD contractor
   employees.
   2.22.2. In those circumstances where the reason for a member’s absence is uncertain and it is possible
   that the member is a casualty whose absence is involuntary, but there is not sufficient evidence to
   determine immediately that the member is missing or deceased, the member should be designated
   DUSTWUN (paragraphs 2.11. through 2.15.) and the commander shall:
       2.22.2.1. Make a preliminary assessment of the circumstances. In circumstances where it is ques-
       tionable whether the involuntary absence is a result of hostile action (or under circumstances sug-
       gesting that the involuntary absence is a result of hostile action), the commander of the unit,
       facility, or area to or in which the person is assigned shall submit a preliminary assessment and
       recommendation.
       2.22.2.2. If, as a result of that assessment, the commander concludes that the person is missing,
       the commander shall:
           2.22.2.2.1. Recommend that the person be placed in a missing status using DD Form 2812,
           Commander’s Preliminary Assessment and Recommendation Regarding Missing Per-
           son (see DoDI 2310.5, Enclosure 3).
           2.22.2.2.2. Not later than 10 days after receiving such information, transmit a report contain-
           ing that recommendation to HQ AFPC/DPFCM with an advisory copy to the theater compo-
           nent commander having jurisdiction over the missing person.
   2.22.3. Upon receipt of the commander’s recommendation to place a person in missing status, HQ
   AFPC/DPFCM will notify the convening authority (AFPC/CC) who will appoint a board of inquiry in
   accordance with DoDI 2310.5 and AFPCI 36-26, Boards of Inquiry for Personnel Missing Under
   Hostile Conditions.

Section 2D—Reports on Members Who Are Very Seriously Ill or Injured (VSI), Seriously Ill or
Injured (SI), Have an Incapacitating Illness or Injury (III), or Imminent Death Casualties, and Emer-
gency Family Member Travel Program

2.23. Reporting VSI, SI, or III Casualties. When a member is hospitalized and determined by medical
authority to be VSI, SI, or have an III, the responsible commander has the CAR submit a Casualty Report
(see Table 1.1. for applicability, and Attachment 10):

2.24. CAR Responsibilities for Reporting VSI, SI, or III Casualties.
   2.24.1. Contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 to report member’s status and pos-
   sible notifications.
48                                                    AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


     2.24.2. Gather information for the Casualty Report from the military Medical Treatment Facility
     (MTF) or civilian hospital.
     2.24.3. Submit the initial Casualty Report (see Attachment 10) the same day notified.
        2.24.3.1. If the attending physician requests, and the MTF commander approves, invitational
        travel authorization for NOK of military members who are determined VSI, SI, or in an imminent
        death situation, use item M, NOK Emergency Family Member Travel, on the report to request
        invitational travel authorization (paragraph 2.29.).
     2.24.4. Submit a report on family members of Air Force military members and DoD or DAF civilian
     employees when requesting HQ AFPC/DPFCS to notify the NOK.
     2.24.5. See AFMAN 33-326, Preparing Official Communications and Attachment 10 for comple-
     tion of the report.

2.25. Reporting Imminent Death Casualties. When a military member is hospitalized, and medical
authorities deem death is imminent (within 72 hours), the responsible commander has the CAR immedi-
ately contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 to report the member’s status and for pos-
sible notification to the NOK.

2.26. CAR Responsibilities for Reporting Imminent Death Casualties.
     2.26.1. Contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 to report the
     member’s status and for possible notification to the NOK.
     2.26.2. Fax the following documents to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348:
        2.26.2.1. vRED/DD Form 93 (if in UPRG).
        2.26.2.2. SGLV 8286.
        2.26.2.3. Any other VA forms related to SGLI found in Section 1 of the member’s UPRG.
        2.26.2.4. For ANG and USAFR casualties:
            2.26.2.4.1. A copy of the order or other document placing the member on AD.
            2.26.2.4.2. A statement from the ANG unit finance officer, Reserve Pay Unit, or the
            DFAS-DE indicating the amount of Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance deductions and
            the date of the first and last deduction.
     2.26.3. Gather information for the VSI Casualty Report from the MTF or civilian hospital.
     2.26.4. Submit the initial VSI Casualty Report (see Attachment 10) the same day notified.
        2.26.4.1. Follow the procedures outlined in paragraph 2.29. concerning invitational travel autho-
        rization for the NOK of military members who are determined VSI, SI, or in an imminent death
        situation.
     2.26.5. See AFMAN 33-326 and Attachment 10 for completion of the report.

2.27. Wartime Casualties and Casualties from Incidents Involving Military Aircraft or AMC Com-
mercially Contracted Aircraft.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    49


   2.27.1. Submit reports for the persons indicated in Table 1.1. for both CONUS and overseas casual-
   ties, unless waived by HQ AFPC/DPFC.
   2.27.2. Follow the procedures outlined in paragraph 2.29. concerning invitational travel authorization
   for the NOK of military members who are determined VSI, SI, or imminent death.

2.28. VSI, SI, and III Medical Progress Reports.
   2.28.1. For Table 1.1., Rules 1 and 2:
      2.28.1.1. The CAR submits Medical Progress Reports (MPR) (see Attachment 11) to HQ AFPC/
      DPFCS within 24 hours of the initial Casualty Report and every 4 days thereafter, or immediately
      when:
      2.28.1.2. There is a change in diagnosis, prognosis, or status.
      2.28.1.3. Surgery is scheduled, indicating the scheduled date and type of surgery:
          2.28.1.3.1. Submit a postoperative report describing the patient’s condition, results of the sur-
          gery and any additional information the attending physician provides.
      2.28.1.4. The Air Force medically evacuates the patient from one medical treatment facility to
      another (MOVED):
          2.28.1.4.1. Report the complete itinerary, including the flight and mission number, and the
          name of the civilian hospital or MTF destination.
          2.28.1.4.2. Include the gaining MTF and servicing MPF at the final destination as addressees,
          and the MTF(s) and MPF(s) at intermediate stops, if applicable, and the losing MTF as infor-
          mation addressees on the message.
      2.28.1.5. The patient is removed (WRITE) from VSI, SI, or III list.
      2.28.1.6. The patient who was previously reported VSI, SI, or III and later removed (WRITE), is
      placed back on the VSI, SI, or III list.
          2.28.1.6.1. Enter at the end of the subject line: “Patient previously removed from VSI, SI, or
          III status and the date removed.
   2.28.2. For Table 1.1., Rules 3, 4, and 5:
      2.28.2.1. Medical Progress Reports (MPR) are not required unless directed by HQ AFPC/
      DPFCS.

2.29. Emergency Family Member Travel Program.
   2.29.1. The Air Force provides round-trip transportation for not more than three family members to
   the medical facility of a member listed as VSI, SI, when hospitalized in or outside the United States,
   if the attending physician or surgeon and the commander or head of the military treatment facility
   exercising military control over the member determine that the presence of the family member may
   contribute to the member’s health and welfare (Title 37, U.S.C, Section 411h).
      2.29.1.1. The Emergency Family Member Travel program applies to family members of a mili-
      tary member serving on active duty to include ANG and USAFR members in a duty status. (This
      does not include Air Force Academy cadets per JFTR and 37 U.S.C. 20[g]).
50                                                     AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        2.29.1.2. The commander or head of the MTF must concur and approve the attending physician’s
        request on AF Form 570, Notification of Patient’s Medical Status, prior to HQ AFPC/DPFCS
        issuing the Emergency Family Member Travel authority. All family members requiring travel
        must be included on the AF Form 570.
     2.29.2. Family members eligible for Emergency Family Member Travel:
        2.29.2.1. The member’s spouse.
        2.29.2.2. The member’s children, including step, adopted, and illegitimate children where pater-
        nity is acknowledged.
        2.29.2.3. The member’s parents, including step and adopted, or persons who stood in loco
        parentis to the member for a period of not less than 1 year immediately before the member entered
        the Air Force.
            2.29.2.3.1. Only one father and one mother or their counterparts in loco parentis may be rec-
            ognized in any one case and provided government-sponsored travel.
        2.29.2.4. The member’s siblings.
     2.29.3. Transportation:
        2.29.3.1. The Air Force reimburses the family members for cost of travel between their residence
        and the location of the MTF in which the member is hospitalized; for personally procured com-
        mercial transportation such as airfare or driving expenses for travel by privately owned vehicle
        (POV).
            2.29.3.1.1. If family members are already at the member’s bedside, the Air Force does not
            offer transportation to other NOK unless the attending physician determines that these family
            members are physically or mentally incapacitated and are unable to contribute to the mem-
            ber’s health and welfare.
        2.29.3.2. Local per diem is authorized to pay for expenses such as food, lodging while in the
        vicinity of the medical facility.
            2.29.3.2.1. Advance payments of per diem is authorized.
        2.29.3.3. It is extremely important to all concerned that care is taken when discussing any
        round-trip transportation with family members. To avoid embarrassing situations, do not obligate
        the Air Force before securing Emergency Family Member Travel approval and ensuring with HQ
        AFPC/DPFCS that family members meet all eligibility requirements.
     2.29.4. Responsibilities and procedures. It takes the coordinated effort of medical personnel, unit
     commanders, the CAR, and HQ AFPC/DPFCS to ensure an effective Emergency Family Member
     Travel Program.
        2.29.4.1. Attending Physician or Surgeon. Initiates the Emergency Family Member Travel
        request whenever the presence of family members may contribute to the member’s health and wel-
        fare.
        2.29.4.2. MTF commander or head of the military medical facility:
            2.29.4.2.1. Ensures MTF personnel are familiar with the Emergency Family Member Travel
            Program and eligibility criteria before requesting round-trip transportation.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                 51


        2.29.4.2.2. Approves or disapproves the attending physician’s or surgeon’s Emergency Fam-
        ily Member Travel request:
           2.29.4.2.2.1. For members in a civilian hospital, the commander of the nearest military
           MTF or the military MTF having administrative responsibility for the member must
           approve or disapprove the attending physician’s or surgeon’s request.
        2.29.4.2.3. Ensures the CAR is immediately notified if the Emergency Family Member
        Travel request is approved.
        2.29.4.2.4. Provides the CAR necessary information to request transportation arrangements
        from AFPC/DPFCS.
        2.29.4.2.5. Coordinates with the member’s unit commander to ensure the NOK are promptly
        notified of the member’s condition (see paragraph 3.24.), whether or not Emergency Family
        Member Travel has been requested.
     2.29.4.3. Member’s unit commander:
        2.29.4.3.1. Coordinates notifying the NOK of the member’s condition with the MTF or civil-
        ian hospital (see paragraph 3.24.3.3.).
        2.29.4.3.2. When notified by the CAR that Emergency Family Member Travel has been
        approved and HQ AFPC/DPFCS has established the family members’ itinerary, assigns a unit
        representative to act as personal escort to receive the family members, arrange for their quar-
        ters and meals, and provide assistance as needed.
        2.29.4.3.3. Ensures the personal escort remains in contact with the family members during
        their stay and informs the CAR when they desire to return home, so HQ AFPC/DPFCS can
        arrange transportation.
     2.29.4.4. The CAR:
        2.29.4.4.1. Is the office of primary responsibility (OPR) for ensuring the policy, responsibili-
        ties and requirements of the Emergency Family Member Travel Program are administered cor-
        rectly and in accordance with this AFI.
        2.29.4.4.2. Establishes local procedures to inform responsible agencies and individuals (med-
        ical personnel, commanders, first sergeants, and command post personnel) about the Emer-
        gency Family Member Travel Program through such media as base supplements,
        commanders’ orientations, first sergeants’ meetings, and training.
        2.29.4.4.3. Ensures base agencies and individuals notify the CAR of all VSI, SI, and immi-
        nent death cases involving military members hospitalized in the MTF or civilian hospitals
        within their area of responsibility.
        2.29.4.4.4. Immediately contacts HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or
        1-800-433-0048 when the MTF commander approves an Emergency Family Member Travel
        request.
        2.29.4.4.5. Submits appropriate Casualty Report to HQ AFPC/DPFCS to confirm the Emer-
        gency Family Member Travel:
           2.29.4.4.5.1. In item M on the initial VSI or SI Casualty Report (see Attachment 10), or
           in item H, on the Medical Progress Report (see Attachment 11).
52                                                    AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


          2.29.4.4.6. On receipt of the family members’ travel itinerary from HQ AFPC/DPFCS,
          informs the personal escort selected by the unit commander.
          2.29.4.4.7. For members hospitalized away from their home installation, arranges for some-
          one to act as the personal escort to receive the family members, arrange for their quarters and
          meals, and provides whatever assistance they need during their stay.
          2.29.4.4.8. Stays in contact with the personal escort and finds out when the NOK want to go
          home and tells HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 or mes-
          sage.
      2.29.4.5. HQ AFPC/DPFCS:
          2.29.4.5.1. Ensures the Emergency Family Member Travel request meets public law require-
          ments and authorizes Emergency Family Member Travel. NOTE: Due to varied locations of
          family members and the extreme urgency of the situation, “message orders” from HQ AFPC/
          DPFCS provide sole authorization for travel and reimbursement of funds.
          2.29.4.5.2. Contacts the NOK by telephone, verifies that the NOK want to travel to the mem-
          ber's bedside, and books the most practical mode of commercial air transportation.
          2.29.4.5.3. Provides the NOK instructional procedures and guidance on obtaining passports,
          passport waivers, visas, required immunizations, and other matters related to travel.
          2.29.4.5.4. Sends the CAR the NOK's itinerary.
          2.29.4.5.5. Informs the NOK that the Air Force may reimburse them for certain transportation
          costs and advises them to save all expense receipts and other travel documentation (such as
          ticket stubs).
          2.29.4.5.6. Authorizes reimbursement of the NOK's travel expenses.
      2.29.4.6. Initiates reimbursement to the NOK for cost of personally procured commercial trans-
      portation such as airfare or driving expenses for travel by POV.
          2.29.4.6.1. NOK who travel at their own expense before the Air Force approves Emergency
          Family Member Travel are subject to the eligibility requirements established for the Emer-
          gency Family Member Travel Program.
             2.29.4.6.1.1. To initiate reimbursement for “after-the-fact” Emergency Family Member
             Travel, the CAR follows the same procedures for requesting and obtaining Emergency
             Family Member Travel approval.
          2.29.4.6.2. The Air Force does not reimburse the NOK until they return home.
          2.29.4.6.3. The Air Force does not reimburse the NOK’s travel expenses paid with other Air
          Force funds, such as unit Operation and Maintenance (O&M) funds.

Section 2E—Abbreviated/Hasty Casualty/Incident Reports (RCS: DD FM&P[AR]1664, Report of
Casualty)

2.30. Purpose.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                 53


   2.30.1. The abbreviated/HASTY Casualty/Incident Reports (see Attachment 12 and Attachment
   13) are used to expedite the flow of casualty information to HQ AFPC/DPFCS when multiple casual-
   ties are involved and submitting standard Casualty Reports would delay notifying the NOK.
   2.30.2. The abbreviated/HASTY Casualty Reports are used to:
      2.30.2.1. Give HQ AFPC/DPFCS information for casualty accountability purposes.
      2.30.2.2. Help HQ AFPC/DPFCS expedite notification without news media interference.
      2.30.2.3. Provide immediate information about an incident with potential mass casualties.

2.31. Reporting Requirements and Procedures.
   2.31.1. If possible, the CAR contacts HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or
   1-800-433-0048 before submitting an abbreviated report:
      2.31.1.1. HQ AFPC/DPFCS may waive the requirement to submit abbreviated reports, depending
      on the nature of the incident and the number of casualties.
   2.31.2. Multiple Reportable Casualties:
      2.31.2.1. When multiple casualties make it difficult to submit standard reports in a timely manner
      using assigned casualty services personnel or a CAST, use the appropriate abbreviated Casualty
      Report (see Attachment 12 through Attachment 13) to initially report casualties.
      2.31.2.2. When an incident occurs, if possible, the CAR immediately contacts HQ AFPC/DPFCS
      by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 for approval of abbreviated reporting.
          2.31.2.2.1. If telephone contact is impossible, the MPF commander determines if abbreviated
          reporting is necessary.
      2.31.2.3. Immediately submit items A through D (see Attachment 12 and Attachment 13).
          2.31.2.3.1. As soon as additional information becomes available, submit another abbreviated
          Casualty Report for the remaining items (Attachment 12).
      2.31.2.4. Once conditions permit, submit standard initial Death Reports (see Attachment 2) on
      the personnel listed in Table 1.1.
      2.31.2.5. You do not have to submit a standard initial Casualty Report on DUSTWUN, missing,
      or injured persons whom you reported in an abbreviated Casualty Report. You must submit these
      standard reports, however, as applicable:
          2.31.2.5.1. Search Progress Reports (see Attachment 4).
          2.31.2.5.2. Returned to Military Control Reports (see Attachment 5).
          2.31.2.5.3. VSI, SI, and III Medical Progress Reports (see Attachment 11). NOTE: You may
          use the abbreviated Medical Progress Report (see Attachment 14) until such time as you can
          submit standard reports.
      2.31.2.6. Complete all applicable items on abbreviated Casualty Reports (see Attachment 12 and
      13) and abbreviated Medical Progress Reports (see Attachment 14).
      2.31.2.7. Report first those casualties requiring personal notification to the NOK.
54                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


            2.31.2.7.1. Give reports on deceased and missing persons priority.
            2.31.2.7.2. Do not delay reporting while obtaining information on less serious casualties.
        2.31.2.8. Report information on injured personnel in a subsequent abbreviated Casualty Report.
        2.31.2.9. HQ AFPC/DPFCS will provide prioritizing guidance during the initial telephone call
        from the reporting unit.

Section 2F—Reporting Air Force Retiree Deaths

2.32. Investigation of Retiree Deaths.
     2.32.1. The CAR nearest the area in which the NOK resides investigates the possible death of a
     retiree:
        2.32.1.1. Treat the possible death of a retiree as an “unconfirmed” death.
        2.32.1.2. Send only inquiries to the NOK; do not send a condolence letter.
     2.32.2. See Attachment 15 for appropriate phrases to use when you are not sure who will receive the
     inquiry at the address on file.
        2.32.2.1. Do not use "To whom it may concern" or "Occupant" as a salutation.
        2.32.2.2. Address the envelope to "Resident."
     2.32.3. If you find that the retiree is alive, send an e-mail or message to Defense Finance and
     Accounting Service-Cleveland Center (DFAS-CL/FRC) with HQ AFPC/DPFCS as an information
     addressee.
     2.32.4. Contact these organizations for help in your investigation:
        2.32.4.1. The VA.
        2.32.4.2. The State or Federal Bureau of Vital Statistics.
        2.32.4.3. The Civilian Personnel Flight.
        2.32.4.4. The Post Office.
        2.32.4.5. Utility companies.
        2.32.4.6. Banks.
        2.32.4.7. Funeral homes.
     2.32.5. If you cannot confirm the retiree's status, contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN
     665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 for assistance and guidance.

2.33. Reporting Air Force Retiree Deaths Within 120 Days After Retirement.
     2.33.1. When an Air Force retiree dies within 120 days after retiring, the CAR notifies HQ AFPC/
     DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048, then submits a message (see Attachment
     16), or e-mail message, the same day or next duty day after learning of the death.
     2.33.2. The CAR immediately faxes (DSN 665-2348), then mails these documents, if available, to
     HQ AFPC/DPFCS:
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                   55


       2.33.2.1. vRED/DD Form 93 (if in UPRG)(signed original).
       2.33.2.2. VA Form SGLV 8286 (signed original).
       2.33.2.3. VA Form SGLV 8283, Claim for Death Benefit (signed original).
       2.33.2.4. Any other VA forms related to Servicemembers’ Group Life Insurance found in Section
       1 of the member’s UPRG (signed original).
       2.33.2.5. DD Form 214 (copy).
       2.33.2.6. Retirement order (copy).
       2.33.2.7. Medical Evaluation Board or Physical Evaluation Board Report, if applicable (copy).
       2.33.2.8. Civilian death certificate (copy).
       2.33.2.9. DD Form 397, Claim Certificate and Voucher for Death Gratuity Payment (copy).
       2.33.2.10. VA Form 21-534, Application for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation, or
       Death Pension Accrued Benefits by Surviving Spouse or Child, (VA Form 21-534a, Applica-
       tion for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation by a Surviving Spouse or Child – In Service
       Death, may be substituted) or VA Form 21-535, Application for Dependency and Indemnity
       Compensation by Parent(s), as applicable (copy).
       2.33.2.11. VA Certification letter (copy).
       2.33.2.12. DD Form 4.

2.34. Reporting Air Force Retired General Officer Deaths. The CAR must report the deaths of
retired general officers to HQ AFPC/DPFCS by telephone at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 immedi-
ately upon receiving notification, or submit a message (see Attachment 17), or e-mail message with the
information contained in Attachment 17.

2.35. Reporting Air Force Retiree Deaths More Than 120 Days After Retirement.
   2.35.1. Procedures for MPFs with Defense Retiree and Annuitant Pay System (DRAPS) Capability:
       2.35.1.1. When an Air Force retiree dies more than 120 days after retiring, the CAR obtains initial
       information from the NOK to report the death and assists them in completion of benefit claim
       applications.
       2.35.1.2. Upon learning of a retiree's death, the CAR:
          2.35.1.2.1. Immediately informs the local financial service office (FSO) of the retiree's name,
          SSN, and the date of death.
       2.35.1.3. The FSO:
          2.35.1.3.1. Provides the information from the CAR to DFAS-CL.
          2.35.1.3.2. Gives the CAR the retiree's pay and beneficiary information.
       2.35.1.4. If a CAR learns of a retiree death and the NOK do not reside in the CAR’s area of
       responsibility, the CAR immediately calls the appropriate CAR and provides them all known
       information on the deceased retiree.
56                                                     AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


            2.35.1.4.1. The appropriate CAR must then immediately notify the local FSO and assist the
            NOK.
     2.35.2. Procedures for MPFs without DRAPS Capability:
        2.35.2.1. When an Air Force retiree dies more than 120 days after retiring, the CAR obtains initial
        information from the NOK to report the death and assist them in completion of benefit claim
        applications.
        2.35.2.2. Upon learning of a retiree's death, the CAR:
            2.35.2.2.1. In the CONUS, immediately telephones DFAS-CL at 1-800-269-5170,
            1-800-321-1080, or commercial at (216) 522-6680. Provides the retiree's name, SSN, and the
            date of death.
               2.35.2.2.1.1. Requests the retiree's pay and beneficiary information.
            2.35.2.2.2. If overseas, obtain pay information from the FSO, or sends a message, or e-mail to
            HQ AFPC/DPFCS requesting the retiree’s pay and beneficiary information:
               2.35.2.2.2.1. Provides the retiree's name, SSN, and the date of death. NOTE: AFPC/
               DPFCS acquires the retiree’s pay and beneficiary information from DFAS-CL and sends it
               to the CAR.
        2.35.2.3. If a CAR learns of a retiree death and the NOK do not reside in the CAR’s area of
        responsibility, the CAR immediately calls or sends a message, or e-mail to the appropriate CAR
        and provides them all known information on the deceased retiree.
            2.35.2.3.1. The appropriate CAR must then immediately contact DFAS-CL by telephone at
            1-800-269-5170 or 1-800-321-1080, or commercial at (216) 522-6680, or HQ AFPC/DPFCS
            by message, or e-mail and assist the NOK.
     2.35.3. The CAR sends a copy of the civilian death certificate to AFRL/HEDB, 2608 Flight Nurse,
     Building 807, Brooks AFB TX 78235-5250, when available.

     7. Dual category-commissioned officer serving as an airman in the active AF.

         for and received benefits.
