        sel the NOK and enter the date counseled.
     4.24.3. Close cases involving members returned to military control from a missing status within 90
     days after the member's return to military control.
     4.24.4. Submit a typed, error-free original AF IMT 58 (see Attachment 21) to HQ AFPC/DPFCS,
     550 C Street West, Suite 14, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4716.
        4.24.4.1. Ensure all items are properly completed to include:
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    97


          4.24.4.1.1. Dates are recorded accurately.
          4.24.4.1.2. Items 13 and 14 are signed and dated by the CAR.
       4.24.4.2. If more than one installation provided assistance, make sure other family members or
       persons designated beneficiaries applied for and received the benefits (see paragraph 4.2.4.).

4.25. Extension Request.
   4.25.1. When benefits have not been settled by the 5th month after the date of death and the 6-month
   period will be exceeded, request an extension from HQ AFPC/DPFCS in a memorandum, e-mail, or
   message.
   4.25.2. The memorandum, e-mail or message should include the:
       4.25.2.1. Reason for the extension.
       4.25.2.2. Efforts made by the CAR to resolve problems.
       4.25.2.3. Estimated date the case will be closed.

4.26. Maintenance of Casualty Assistance Case Files.
   4.26.1. Maintain casualty assistance case files in accordance with RDS.
   4.26.2. Establish a case file for each casualty and file alphabetically.
   4.26.3. Case files must contain:
       4.26.3.1. A chronological record of contacts, listed on AF IMT 58, in item 11, with:
          4.26.3.1.1. NOK.
          4.26.3.1.2. Other family members and persons designated as beneficiaries, if applicable.
          4.26.3.1.3. Other government agencies.
          4.26.3.1.4. Civilian agencies.
       4.26.3.2. CAR’s actions on behalf of the NOK.
       4.26.3.3. Copies of all messages, memorandums, and claim forms sent to other agencies and the
       NOK.
       4.26.3.4. Any other relevant documents.
   4.26.4. Installations reporting casualties only. Installations reporting deaths but having no assistance
   responsibilities should establish an interim case file for each reported casualty, and destroy the case
   file 6 months after the date of death.

4.27. Disposition of Casualty Assistance Case Files. Dispose of casualty case files in accordance with
Air Force Records Disposition Schedule (RDS) located at https://webrims.amc.af.mil/rds/index.cfm,
Casualty Reporting, Notification, and Assistance.
98                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


Section 4C—Benefit Information and Casualty Assistance Procedures for Retiree Deaths Within 120
Days After Retirement

4.28. General Procedures.
     4.28.1. Explain to the NOK all benefits listed on the AF IMT 58 and in AFPAM 36-3028.
     4.28.2. Give the NOK a copy of AFPAM 36-3028.
     4.28.3. Use the AF IMT 58 as a checklist and guide during the counseling session.
     4.28.4. Explain to the NOK that the AF IMT 58 is used to track and document benefits and entitle-
     ments applied for and received.
     4.28.5. Complete the necessary claim applications for applicable benefits (see Table 4.3.).
     4.28.6. Complete all items on the AF IMT 58 using the instructions in Attachment 21 and briefly
     summarize relevant information discussed with the NOK in item 11, and any problems in item 12,
     “Additional Comments.”
     4.28.7. Keep a copy of all claim applications, forms, and supporting documentation in the case file.

4.29. Death Gratuity. A lump sum gratuitous payment made by DFAS-CL Center to eligible beneficia-
ries of a retiree who dies within 120 days following placement on the permanent or temporary disability
retired list (PDRL/TDRL), or who is retired for years of service. Payments can be made only after the VA
determines death was caused by an illness or injury incurred while the retiree was on active duty, ADT, or
IDT. Under no circumstances will the local FSO make payments in these cases. The claim forms required
to apply for this benefit are DD Form 397, Claim Certificate and Voucher for Death Gratuity Pay-
ment, VA DIC Worksheet, VA Form 21-534, Application for Dependency and Indemnity Compensa-
tion, or Death Pension Accrued Benefits by Surviving Spouse or Child, or VA Form 21-535,
Application for Dependency and Indemnity Compensation by Parent(s).
     4.29.1. The death gratuity payment is made to survivors of the deceased in this order:
        4.29.1.1. The member’s lawful surviving spouse.
        4.29.1.2. When there is no spouse, to the child or children of the member, regardless of age or
        marital status, in equal shares (state laws guide payment to minor children).
        4.29.1.3. If none of the above, to the parents, siblings, or any combination as designated by the
        deceased member.
        4.29.1.4. The death gratuity is not paid to any other person when there are no survivors as listed
        above. A will is not a legal designation for death gratuity since such payment is not an allowance
        or a debt due the member and cannot be part of the estate.
     4.29.2. To apply for the death gratuity, the CAR should obtain a copy of DD Form 397 from the base
     FSO.
        4.29.2.1. Complete all items on the form except items 1, 2, 3, 4 and 18, which are left blank.
        4.29.2.2. Add the payee’s SSN in item 5.
        4.29.2.3. Fax the form to HQ AFPC/DPFCS, at DSN 665-2348, along with any supporting docu-
        mentation as listed in Table 4.3.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                       99


       4.29.2.4. Mail the original form and copies of any supporting documentation to DFAS-CL/
       FRCAE, P.O. Box 99191, Cleveland OH 44199-1126 or FAX to DSN: 580-6321 (see Table 4.3.).
   4.29.3. The CAR should complete either a VA Form 21-534a (DIC Worksheet), VA Form 21-534 or
   VA Form 21-535, as applicable, and follow the procedures in paragraph 4.34.

4.30. Financial Assistance.
   4.30.1. The CAR should ask the NOK about their immediate financial needs.
   4.30.2. If the NOK is not eligible for the death gratuity payment, or if immediate payment is not pos-
   sible, with the NOK’s permission, contact the nearest ARC or AFAS representative located in the
   FSC, for possible assistance.

4.31. Unpaid Pay and Allowances. The retirement pay of an Air Force retired member stops on the first
day of the month in which the retiree died. Upon death of a retired member, any pay and allowances due
but not paid to the member are paid to the designated beneficiary named by the member prior to retire-
ment. Normally, this amounts to the retirement pay from the first day of the month of death through the
date of death. Retirement pay electronically deposited into an account held by a retiree will automatically
be recouped by DFAS-CL and reissued to the beneficiary for the correct amount.
   4.31.1. When the designated beneficiary is deceased, or if the member elected “order of precedence,”
   any money due is paid to the first eligible recipient in the following order:
       4.31.1.1. The member’s lawful surviving spouse.
       4.31.1.2. When there is no spouse, to the child or children of the member in equal shares, with the
       share of any deceased child to be distributed among the descendants of that child.
       4.31.1.3. If none of the above, to the parents of the member in equal shares or to the surviving par-
       ent.
       4.31.1.4. If none of the above, to the duly appointed legal representative of the member’s estate.
       4.31.1.5. If none of the above, to the person(s) determined to be entitled under the laws of the
       state in which the member was domiciled.
   4.31.2. To apply for the unpaid pay and allowances, the CAR should complete the required claim
   form as listed in Table 4.3.
   4.31.3. Mail the original claim form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table
   4.3., to DFAS-CL at Defense Finance and Accounting Service, U. S. Military Retirement Pay, P. O.
   Box 7130, London KY 40742-7130.
   4.31.4. When the unpaid pay and allowances are divided, the base with primary assistance responsi-
   bility submits all claim forms in one package.
   4.31.5. Contact the base FSO to check on the payment status of the unpaid pay and allowances prior
   to checking with DFAS-CL.

4.32. SBP. SBP is a monthly annuity paid by the Air Force. This program allows personnel who retired
on or after 21 September 1972, to receive reduced retired pay in order to provide a monthly annuity to
their beneficiaries after the death of the retiree. The retiree designates the beneficiaries. Participation in
100                                                     AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


this program is voluntary. SBP provides an eligible surviving spouse or former spouse or, in some cases,
eligible children financial security similar to the financial security a retiree had in retired pay—a
cost-of-living-adjusted monthly income for life. See AFI 36-3006, for additional benefit information.
      4.32.1. If the retiree participated in SBP, fax the required claim forms and copies of any supporting
      documentation as listed in Table 4.3. to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348, and DFAS at
      1-800-982-8459.
      4.32.2. Mail the original claim forms and copies of any supporting documentation to Defense Finance
      and Accounting Service, U. S. Military Annuitant Pay, P. O. Box 7131, London KY 40742-7131.
      4.32.3. Contact the base FSO to check on the payment status of the SBP annuity prior to checking
      with DFAS.

4.33. RCSBP. RCSBP is a monthly annuity paid by the Air Force to the surviving spouse or, in some
cases, eligible children, of an Air Reserve Component member who dies and has completed the satisfac-
tory years of service to qualify the member for retired pay at age 60. The retiree designates the beneficia-
ries. The beneficiary choices are the same as for SBP. Participation in the program is voluntary. See AFI
36-3006 for additional benefit information:
      4.33.1. If the retiree participated in RCSBP, fax the claim forms and supporting documentation as
      listed in Table 4.3. to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348, and DFAS at 1-800-982-8459.
      4.33.2. Mail the original claim forms and copies of supporting documentation to Defense Finance and
      Accounting Service, U. S. Military Annuitant Pay, P. O. Box 7131, London KY 40742-7131.
      4.33.3. Contact the base FSO to check on the payment status of the RCSBP annuity prior to checking
      with DFAS.

4.34. DIC. DIC is payable by the VA to surviving spouses, unmarried children under age 18, disabled
children, children between the ages of 18 and 23 if attending a VA-approved school, and low-income par-
ents of retirees who die from a disease or injury incurred or aggravated while on active duty or active duty
for training, an injury incurred or aggravated in the line of duty while on inactive duty for training, or a
disability otherwise compensable under laws administered by the VA. DIC is not paid if the VA deter-
mines that the retiree’s own misconduct contributed to the death. The monthly DIC rate paid to a surviv-
ing spouse of a retiree for deaths occurring after 1 January 1993 is the same for all pay grades. The DIC
amount paid for a spouse with one or more children of the deceased retiree is increased for each child. The
amount of the DIC payment for parents varies according to the number of parents, the amount of their
individual or combined total annual income, and whether they live together or, if remarried, live with a
spouse. DIC payments to a surviving spouse are payable for life, as long as the spouse does not remarry.
Should the surviving spouse remarry, payments are terminated, but may be restored if the subsequent
marriage ends in death, divorce or annulment. See VAP 80-XX-1 for additional information. *NOTE:
The second two digits represent the year of publication.
      4.34.1. When assisting the survivor of a member who dies within 120 days following placement on
      the PDRL or TDRL:
         4.34.1.1. Follow the procedures for death gratuity in paragraph 4.29.
         4.34.1.2. Complete the appropriate DIC claim application as listed in Table 4.3.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    101


       4.34.1.3. Fax the claim application and copies of required documents and any supporting docu-
       mentation as listed in Table 4.3. to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348.
       4.34.1.4. Mail the original claim application along with copies of required documents and any
       supporting documentation, as listed in Table 4.3., to VARO-CL, ATTN: Adjudication Officer 21,
       1240 East Ninth Street, Cleveland OH 44199.
   4.34.2. When assisting the survivor of an Air Force member retired for years of service who dies
   within 120 days following retirement:
       4.34.2.1. Follow the procedures for death gratuity in paragraph 4.29.
       4.34.2.2. Complete the appropriate DIC claim application as listed in Table 4.3.
       4.34.2.3. Mail the original claim application and copies of required documents and any support-
       ing documentation, as listed in Table 4.3., to the VARO to process the claim.
   4.34.3. Remember, even if no one is eligible for DIC you should submit the appropriate claim appli-
   cation so the VA can determine if the death is service connected before DFAS-CL will pay the death
   gratuity.
   4.34.4. When the VARO makes a determination of service connection, fax the signed VA Rating
   Decision to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348.
       4.34.4.1. The rating should contain the signature of the VA rating specialist, and the statement
       that basic eligibility for death gratuity, under Title 38, U.S.C., Chapter 35, is established.
   4.34.5. HQ AFPC/DPFCS will advise DFAS-CL that payment of the death gratuity is or is not autho-
   rized, and DFAS-CL will annotate their case file accordingly and make payment if authorized.
       4.34.5.1. When assisting the spouse of a retiree who is in receipt of VA disability compensation,
       the spouse can receive the member’s final month’s VA disability compensation through the DIC
       application only.

4.35. Non-Service-Connected Death Pension. If the VARO determines that the NOK is not eligible for
DIC, they may be eligible to apply for a non-service-connected death pension. Surviving spouses of
deceased members with wartime service and unmarried children under age 18, age 23 if attending a
VA-approved school, may be eligible for this pension if they meet income limitations prescribed by law.
Qualifying children who become incapable of self-support because of a disability before age 18 may be
eligible for a pension as long as the condition exists, unless the child marries or the child’s income
exceeds the income limit. The rate of pension depends on the amount of income the surviving spouse or
child receives from other sources. A pension is not payable to those whose estates are so large that it is
reasonable to assume the estate will maintain them financially. The VA will determine their eligibility.
See VAP 80-XX-1 for additional information. *NOTE: The second two digits represent the year of pub-
lication.
   4.35.1. To apply for a non-service-connected death pension, eligible survivors should visit their local
   VA office to complete the appropriate claim application and provide supporting documentation as
   listed in Table 4.3.

4.36. SGLI. Retirees are covered for 120 days following retirement with no additional premium during
the 120-day period. Retirees rated totally disabled on the date of retirement retain SGLI coverage until the
102                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


disability ceases to be total in degree, but not for more than 1 year. Determination and payment of pro-
ceeds are made by the OSGLI under the jurisdiction of the VA. Payment of proceeds to a beneficiary is
exempt from taxation. The insured member may have designated as principal or contingent beneficiary
any person, firm, corporation or legal entity, including his/her estate, individually or as a trustee. If the
member designated a trust, he/she indicated the name and date of the trust in the beneficiary block. If the
member designated a trust through a will, he/she annotated “Last Will and Testament” in the beneficiary
block. If the member chose not to designate a specific beneficiary but preferred the proceeds be paid in the
order of precedence, the member selected the “By Law” designation.
      4.36.1. When the “By Law” designation is used, the proceeds are automatically paid in the following
      order of precedence:
         4.36.1.1. The member’s lawful surviving spouse.
         4.36.1.2. If there is no spouse, to the child or children of the member in equal shares, with the
         shares of any deceased child to be distributed among the descendants of that child.
         4.36.1.3. If none of the above, to the parents of the member in equal shares or to the surviving par-
         ent.
         4.36.1.4. If none of the above, to the duly appointed legal representative of the member’s estate.
         4.36.1.5. If none of the above, to the person(s) determined to be entitled under the laws of the
         state in which the member was domiciled.
      4.36.2. See paragraph 8.8. and VA Handbook, Servicemembers’ and Veterans’ Group Life Insurance
      Handbook, for additional information.
      4.36.3. To apply for SGLI, the CAR should complete the claim form as listed in Table 4.3.
      4.36.4. Fax the form to HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-2348.
      4.36.5. Fax the form and a copy of the Initial Death Report to OSGLI at 1-877-832-4943.
      4.36.6. Mail the original form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table 4.3., to
      HQ AFPC/DPFCS, 550 C Street West, Suite 14, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4716.
      4.36.7. Contact OSGLI to check on the payment status of the SGLI.

4.37. Service Disabled Veterans Insurance (SDVI) or National Service Life Insurance RH
(NSLI-RH). SDVI is life insurance limited to veterans who left the Service after 24 April 1951. A mem-
ber who had a service-connected disability but was otherwise in good health could apply to the VA for up
to $10,000 in SDVI life insurance coverage at standard rates. Members rated totally disabled by the VA
could apply for a waiver of premiums. For those members eligible for this waiver, additional coverage of
up to $20,000 is available, but the premiums cannot be waived. See VAP 80-XX-1, for additional infor-
mation. *NOTE: The second two digits represent the year of publication.
      4.37.1. If the retiree was covered under SDVI, complete the claim form as listed in Table 4.3.
      4.37.2. Mail the original claim form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table
      4.3., to the VARO and Insurance Center, Box 8079, Philadelphia PA 19101.

4.38. Montgomery GI Bill Death Benefit. The VA will pay a special Montgomery GI Bill death benefit
to a designated survivor if the death is determined to be in the LOD or within 1 year after discharge or
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                       103


release. The deceased must either have been entitled to educational assistance under the Montgomery GI
Bill program or a participant in the program who would have been so entitled but for the high school
diploma or length-of-service requirement. The amount paid will be equal to the participant’s actual mili-
tary pay reduction less any education benefits paid. The death benefit is paid to the SGLI beneficiary. The
CAR should submit a letter, along with the member’s SGLV 8286 listing the beneficiary, and a copy of
the DD Form 1300 and AF IMT 348, Line of Duty Determination, as listed in Table 4.3. to the VARO,
St. Louis Regional Processing Officer, ATTN: Chapter 30, Montgomery GI Bill, PO Box 66830, 331/225,
St. Louis MO 63103-6830. See VAP 80-XX-1*, for additional benefit information. *NOTE: The second
two digits represent the year of publication.

4.39. Social Security Payments. Social Security monthly benefits are paid to a spouse or a divorced
spouse, age 60 or over; a spouse or divorced spouse regardless of age with children of the decedent under
age 16 or disabled in their care and meeting Social Security requirements. A divorced spouse must have
been married to the servicemember at least 10 years. Monthly payments are also paid to children until age
18, or 19 if a full-time student at a primary or secondary school, or age 18 or older if disabled before age
18. Spouses who wait until age 65 to apply for Social Security receive maximum benefits. However, they
can receive reduced Social Security payments between ages 60 and 65. Dependent parents are eligible for
benefits at age 62 if they were more than 50 percent dependent on the deceased servicemember for their
support. The amount paid can only be determined by the Social Security Administration, which has a
record of the wages earned by the member during the period of both military and civilian employment
under the Social Security Program. To apply for this benefit, the CAR should contact the “Expedited
Claims Processing Center” in Philadelphia, PA at 1-866-777-7887, as soon as they obtain sufficient fam-
ily information to establish the claim. This office will explain the benefit, determine their eligibility, the
amount to be paid, and contact the family directly is additional documentation is required. The “Expedited
Claims Processing Center” will establish the claim immediately based on the information provided by the
CAR.

4.40. Social Security Lump Sum Death Payment. The Social Security Administration pays a lump
sum death payment, up to $255, to the surviving spouse living with the member at the time of death. Sep-
aration because of military service, is considered living together. If there is no surviving spouse, it is paid
to the oldest child who was eligible for or entitled to Social Security benefits during the month of the
member’s death. No other survivors are entitled to this benefit. This benefit is paid even if burial, funeral,
or memorial benefits were paid by the Air Force. To apply for this benefit, the CAR should contact the
“Expedited Claims Processing Center” in Philadelphia, PA at 1-866-777-7887, as soon as they obtain suf-
ficient family information to establish the claim. This office will explain the benefit, determine their eligi-
bility, the amount to be paid, and contact the family directly is additional documentation is required. The
“Expedited Claims Processing Center” will establish the claim immediately based on the information pro-
vided by the CAR.

4.41. Other Assistance. The CAR addresses these other matters:
   4.41.1. Living Outside the CONUS. If the NOK plan to establish residence outside the CONUS, the
   CAR should:
       4.41.1.1. Advise them that military privileges may or may not be available to them.
       4.41.1.2. Advise them that the government will not pay import duties on items such as household
       goods and automobiles.
104                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


         4.41.1.3. Contact the overseas installation nearest the NOK’s planned residence to obtain current
         information about military privileges and import duties, then send the information in writing to the
         NOK (see AFI 24-101).
      4.41.2. Status of Forces Agreements. The CAR should:
         4.41.2.1. Tell NOK living overseas that due to host-country restrictions in Status of Forces
         Agreements, they may have to live independently of the overseas installation.
         4.41.2.2. Summarize the relevant information on the AF IMT 58.
      4.41.3. Fraudulent Claims. The CAR should:
         4.41.3.1. Counsel the NOK about possible fraudulent claims against the deceased member's
         estate.
         4.41.3.2. Advise them to refer any suspicious requests for money to the executor of the deceased
         member's estate.
      4.41.4. Uniformed Services Identification (ID) and Privilege Card. The CAR should:
         4.41.4.1. Obtain from the NOK the member’s DD Form 2 (Retired), United States Uniformed
         Services ID Card.
         4.41.4.2. Document the issue and expiration date in the Additional Comments Section of the AF
         Form 58 and ask the NOK if there are any CHAMPUS or TRICARE claims pending against the
         member's ID card.
         4.41.4.3. Destroy the ID card (cut it up or give it to the MPF customer service element for
         destruction).
         4.41.4.4. Escort the NOK to the MPF customer service element and assist them with applying for
         new ID cards.
      4.41.5. Harassment or threats. The CAR should:
         4.41.5.1. Advise the NOK to contact the CAR immediately if anyone harasses them, either by
         telephone or in threatening letters.
         4.41.5.2. Inform the local OSI of such threats or harassment.
      4.41.6. Special surveillance. If necessary, the CAR should arrange for the local police to add special
      surveillance around the NOK's home while they are away for the funeral.
      4.41.7. Mortuary matters. The CAR should refer all questions to the local mortuary services officer or
      HQ AFSVA/SVOM, 9504 Highway 35 North, Suite 320, San Antonio TX 78233-6635, or call them
      toll free at 1-800-531-5803.
      4.41.8. Civilian death certificate. The CAR should:
         4.41.8.1. Tell the NOK that they might need copies of the civilian death certificate in the future.
         4.41.8.2. Explain that the Air Force is not authorized to purchase the death certificate for the
         NOK.
         4.41.8.3. Provide the cost of the document and the address of the appropriate State Vital Statistics
         Office or Health Department.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                  105


      4.41.8.4. Refer the NOK to the funeral director for assistance in obtaining copies of the death cer-
      tificate.

4.42. Transferring Casualty Assistance Case Files.
   4.42.1. HQ AFPC/DPFCS monitors the transfer of all case files.
   4.42.2. Do not transfer a 120-day retiree case file:
      4.42.2.1. When the NOK leaves the area temporarily.
      4.42.2.2. If the NOK does not want the case transferred.
      4.42.2.3. To an overseas installation without approval from HQ AFPC/DPFCS.
   4.42.3. To transfer a 120-day retiree case file:
      4.42.3.1. Transfer a case file only when the NOK leaves the area permanently and provides a firm
      address or location.
      4.42.3.2. The CAR should:
          4.42.3.2.1. Obtain from the NOK a firm address and telephone number at the new location,
          and the projected date of their arrival at the new location.
          4.42.3.2.2. Immediately notify HQ AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048, and
          the gaining CAR of the NOK’s new address, telephone number and projected date of arrival at
          the new address.
          4.42.3.2.3. Review the AF IMT 58 to ensure all items, except addresses, are typed error-free,
          legible, and up to date. NOTE: The gaining CAR must update addresses when the case is
          closed.
          4.42.3.2.4. Complete the “1st IND To” and “From” blocks, type your signature block, and
          sign below the last entry in item 11 on the AF IMT 58.
              4.42.3.2.4.1. Do not complete items 13 and 14.
          4.42.3.2.5. Send the case file by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the gaining CAR,
          including the typed original copy of the partially completed AF IMT 58.
          4.42.3.2.6. Mail a copy of the AF IMT 58 to:
              4.42.3.2.6.1. HQ AFPC/DPFCS, 550 C Street West, Suite 14, Randolph AFB TX
              78150-4716.
          4.42.3.2.7. Keep a file copy of the entire file for 6 months.
          4.42.3.2.8. Send a ROUTINE message to the gaining CAR, with HQ AFPC/DPFCS as an
          information addressee, when the case file is mailed, and:
              4.42.3.2.8.1. Provide information on assistance given to and completed for the NOK.
              4.42.3.2.8.2. Provide the NOK’s new address, telephone number, and projected date of
              arrival at the new address.
106                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


                 4.42.3.2.8.3. Request the gaining CAR contact the losing CAR when the case file is
                 received. If the case file does not arrive within 10 calendar days, the gaining CAR should
                 advise the losing CAR.

4.43. Gaining CAR’s Initial Contact With NOK.
      4.43.1. The gaining CAR must contact the NOK within 24 hours of the NOK’s projected date of
      arrival at the new address and comply with paragraph 4.5. and 4.6.:
         4.43.1.1. Make initial contact by telephone.
         4.43.1.2. Find out if the NOK has any immediate concerns or problems.
         4.43.1.3. Confirm the address.
         4.43.1.4. Offer a casualty assistance visit.
      4.43.2. A casualty assistance visit to the NOK is mandatory whenever a retiree dies within 120 days
      of retiring. EXCEPTION: If the losing CAR made a casualty assistance visit or the NOK advises that
      additional visits are not necessary, this requirement is waived. This does not preclude a visit if the
      NOK wants one.
      4.43.3. Offer a casualty assistance visit to other beneficiaries, or assist them by mail and telephone if
      they agree.

4.44. Administrative Closing of Casualty Assistance Cases.
      4.44.1. Closing casualty assistance cases is an administrative action for control of records and does
      not preclude further assistance to the NOK, such as appealing denials of benefits. The CAR follows
      these procedures to close a casualty assistance case:
      4.44.2. Close cases on deceased members 6 months from the date of death:
         4.44.2.1. Close cases as soon as complete and satisfactory assistance has been provided to the
         NOK, but not before all monetary benefits have been received.
         4.44.2.2. If benefits applied for are denied or delayed, contact HQ AFPC/DPFCS for assistance
         and to request an extension.
         4.44.2.3. Don't hold a case open to complete items 10K through 10W on the AF IMT 58. Counsel
         the NOK and enter the date counseled.
      4.44.3. Close cases involving members returned to military control from a missing status within 90
      days after the member's return to military control.
      4.44.4. Submit a typed, error-free original AF IMT 58 (see Attachment 21) to HQ AFPC/DPFCS,
      550 C Street West, Suite 14, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4716.
         4.44.4.1. Ensure all items are properly completed, including:
             4.44.4.1.1. Dates are recorded accurately.
             4.44.4.1.2. Items 13 and 14 are signed and dated by the CAR.
         4.44.4.2. If more than one installation provided assistance, make sure other family members or
         persons designated beneficiaries applied for and received the benefits (see paragraph 4.2.4.).
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                   107


4.45. Extension Request.
   4.45.1. When benefits have not been settled by the 5th month after the date of death and it appears the
   6-month period will be exceeded, request an extension from HQ AFPC/DPFCS in a memorandum,
   email, or message.
   4.45.2. The memorandum, email, or message should include the:
      4.45.2.1. Reason for the extension.
      4.45.2.2. Efforts made by the CAR to resolve problems.
      4.45.2.3. Estimated date the case will be closed.

4.46. Maintenance of Casualty Assistance Case Files.
   4.46.1. Maintain casualty assistance case files in accordance with AFI 37-138.
   4.46.2. Establish case files for each casualty and file them alphabetically.
   4.46.3. Case files must contain:
      4.46.3.1. A chronological record of contacts, listed on AF IMT 58, in item 11, with:
          4.46.3.1.1. NOK.
          4.46.3.1.2. Other family members and persons designated as beneficiaries, if applicable.
          4.46.3.1.3. Other government agencies.
          4.46.3.1.4. Civilian agencies.
      4.46.3.2. CAR’s actions on behalf of the NOK.
      4.46.3.3. Copies of all messages, memorandums, and claim forms sent to other agencies and the
      NOK.
      4.46.3.4. Any other relevant documents.
   4.46.4. Installations reporting casualties only. Installations reporting deaths but having no assistance
   responsibilities should establish an interim case file for each casualty reported, and destroy the case
   file 6 months after the date of death.

4.47. Disposition of Casualty Assistance Case Files. Dispose of casualty case files IAW Air Force
Records Disposition Schedule (RDS) located at https://webrims.AMC.AF.MIL/RDS/INDEX.cfm,
Records Disposition Schedule.

Section 4D—Benefit Information and Casualty Assistance Procedures for Retiree Deaths More Than
120 Days After Retirement

4.48. General Procedures.
   4.48.1. If assistance with the NOK is by personal visit:
      4.48.1.1. Explain to the NOK all benefits listed on the AF IMT 58, and in AFPAM 36-3028.
      4.48.1.2. Give the NOK a copy of AFPAM 36-3028.
108                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


         4.48.1.3. Use the AF IMT 58 as a checklist and guide during the counseling session.
         4.48.1.4. Explain to the NOK that the AF IMT 58 is used to track and document benefits and enti-
         tlements applied for and received.
         4.48.1.5. Complete the necessary claim applications for applicable benefits.
             4.48.1.5.1. See Table 4.1. for laws and publications concerning benefits.
             4.48.1.5.2. See Table 4.3. for required claim forms, applications and supporting documenta-
             tion needed to submit with all claims.
         4.48.1.6. Complete all items on the AF IMT 58 using the instructions in Attachment 21 and
         briefly summarize relevant information discussed with the NOK in item 11, and any problems in
         item 12, Additional Comments.
         4.48.1.7. Submit the claim applications and supporting documentation to the appropriate agencies
         as soon as possible.
         4.48.1.8. Keep a copy of all claim applications, forms, and supporting documentation in the case
         file.
      4.48.2. If assistance with the NOK is by mail and/or telephone, send the NOK:
         4.48.2.1. A copy of AFPAM 36-3028.
         4.48.2.2. All necessary claim forms (partially completed before mailing).
         4.48.2.3. An error-free cover letter tailored to their needs (see Attachment 24).
         4.48.2.4. Sign the cover memorandum or have the noncommissioned officer in charge (NCOIC)
         of the customer support element sign it.

4.49. Establishing Initial Contact With NOK.
      4.49.1. Initial contact may be made by telephone or in person.
      4.49.2. Determine if a casualty assistance visit is necessary or if you can assist the NOK through mail
      and telephone contact.
      4.49.3. Contact other family members or the estate executor according to their needs, as determined
      during the initial contact with the NOK.
      4.49.4. Obtain from the NOK, a copy (original or certified copy not required) of the civilian death
      certificate, and mail it to AFRL/HEDB, 2608 Flight Nurse, Bldg 807, Brooks AFB TX 78235-5250.
         4.49.4.1. If the death certificate indicates an autopsy was completed, obtain a copy of the autopsy
         report and mail it to AFRL/HEDB.
         4.49.4.2. If the cause of death on the death certificate reads “unknown, undetermined, pending
         investigation, and/or autopsy,” obtain a copy of the amended death certificate and/or autopsy
         report, if performed, and mail it to AFRL/HEDB.
         4.49.4.3. If the manner of death on the death certificate reads “pending investigation,” obtain a
         copy of the amended death certificate and/or autopsy report, if performed, and mail it to AFRL/
         HEDB.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    109


   4.49.5. Each contact, by personal visit, telephone, or mail, must be annotated on AF IMT 58, in item
   11 (see Attachment 21):
       4.49.5.1. Using Attachment 21, briefly summarize relevant information in item 11, and any
       problems in item 12, “Additional Comments.”

4.50. Benefit Assistance to Parents of a Deceased Member.
   4.50.1. The CAR must advise the parents of a deceased member of their possible entitlement to VA
   and Social Security benefits and how to apply.
   4.50.2. Send a letter (see Attachment 22 and Attachment 23) to the parents no later than 15 days
   after the first contact with the NOK. EXCEPTION: If the parents as NOK are receiving an initial
   casualty assistance visit, advise them in person during the initial visit.

4.51. Unpaid Pay and Allowances. The retirement pay of an Air Force member stops on the day the
retiree dies. Upon the death of a retired member, any pay and allowances due but not paid to the member
are paid to the designated beneficiary named by the member prior to retirement. Normally, this amounts
to the retirement pay from the first day of the month of death through the date of death. Retirement pay
electronically deposited into an account held by a retiree will automatically be recouped by DFAS-CL and
reissued to the beneficiary for the correct amount.
   4.51.1. When the designated beneficiary is deceased, or if the member elected “order of precedence,”
   any money due is paid to the first eligible recipient in the following order:
       4.51.1.1. The member’s lawful surviving spouse.
       4.51.1.2. When there is no spouse, to the child or children of the member in equal shares, with the
       share of any deceased child to be distributed among the descendants of that child.
       4.51.1.3. If none of the above, to the parents of the member in equal shares or to the surviving par-
       ent.
       4.51.1.4. If none of the above, to the duly appointed legal representative of the member’s estate.
       4.51.1.5. If none of the above, to the person(s) determined to be entitled under the laws of the
       state in which the member was domiciled.
   4.51.2. To apply for the unpaid pay and allowances, the CAR should complete the claim form as
   listed in Table 4.3.
       4.51.2.1. Mail the original claim form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in
       Table 4.3., to Defense Finance and Accounting Service, U. S. Military Retiree Pay, P. O. Box
       7131, London KY 40742-7131
       4.51.2.2. When unpaid pay and allowances are divided, the base with primary assistance respon-
       sibility submits all claim forms in one package.

4.52. Retired Serviceman’s Family Protection Plan (RSFPP). The RSFPP program allowed person-
nel who retired before 21 September 1972 to receive reduced retired pay in order to provide an annuity for
certain beneficiaries after the death of the retiree. Participation in this program was voluntary. See AFI
36-3006, for additional information.
110                                                        AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      4.52.1. If the retiree elected to participate in RSFPP, follow the applicable instructions listed in para-
      graph 4.55. or 4.56.

4.53. SBP. SBP is a monthly annuity paid by the Air Force. This program allows personnel who retired
on or after 21 September 1972, or before if they enrolled in the program during an open season, to receive
reduced retired pay in order to provide a monthly annuity to their beneficiaries after the death of the
retiree. The retiree designates the beneficiaries. Participation in this program is voluntary. SBP provides
an eligible surviving spouse or former spouse or, in some cases, eligible children, financial security simi-
lar to the financial security a retiree had in retired pay—a cost-of-living-adjusted monthly income for life.
See AFI 36-3006 for additional information.
      4.53.1. If the retiree elected to participate in SBP, follow the applicable instructions listed in para-
      graph 4.55. or 4.56.

4.54. RCSBP. RCSBP is a monthly annuity paid by the Air Force to the surviving spouse or, in some
cases, eligible children, of an Air Reserve Component member who dies and has completed the satisfac-
tory years of service to qualify the member for retired pay at age 60. The retiree designates the beneficia-
ries. The beneficiary choices are the same as for SBP. Participation in the program is voluntary. See AFI
36-3006 for additional benefit information.
      4.54.1. The three options that were available to the member at time of election are:
         4.54.1.1. Option A. Member declines to make an election until age 60. If death occurs prior to age
         60, no annuity is payable.
         4.54.1.2. Option B. Coverage provides for an annuity to begin on the 60th anniversary of mem-
         ber’s birth, if death occurs before age 60, or to begin immediately when death occurs after age 60.
         4.54.1.3. Option C. Coverage provides for an annuity to begin immediately, whether death occurs
         before or after age 60.
      4.54.2. If the retiree participated in RCSBP, follow the applicable instructions listed in paragraph
      4.55. or 4.56.
      4.54.3. Mail the original claim forms and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table
      4.3., to Defense Finance and Accounting Service, U. S. Military Annuitant Pay, P. O. Box 7131, Lon-
      don, KY 40742-7131.
      4.54.4. Contact the base FSO to check on the payment status of the RCSBP annuity prior to checking
      with DFAS.

4.55. Processing RSFPP, SBP or RCSBP Annuities at Installations With Defense Retiree and
Annuitant Pay System (DRAPS) Access.
      4.55.1. Payment should begin within 30 days of the death notification date. The CAR and FSO must
      process the annuity in time to meet this goal.
      4.55.2. If the retiree participated in RSFPP, SBP or RCSBP, the CAR should:
         4.55.2.1. Inform the local FSO of a confirmed death.
         4.55.2.2. Give the FSO the retiree’s name, SSN, date of retirement, grade, and date of death.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                     111


   4.55.3. The FSO should give the CAR information on the deceased's retired pay and beneficiary.
   4.55.4. Within 10 workdays, the CAR should obtain from the NOK the required claim forms and sup-
   porting documentation as listed in Table 4.3., and provide them to the base FSO for processing:
       4.55.4.1. When RSFPP, SBP or RCSBP is divided between more than one child, and they do not
       reside together, the assisting CARs send all documentation using overnight mail service, to the
       CAR with primary assistance responsibility who will then submit all claim applications in one
       package to the FSO.
       4.55.4.2. Mail all claim forms and supporting documentation directly to Defense Finance and
       Accounting Service, U. S. Military Annuitant Pay, P. O. Box 7131, London KY 40742-7131.
   4.55.5. The local FSO:
       4.55.5.1. Determines the need for additional documents, depending on data already in DRAPS,
       and advises the CAR accordingly.
       4.55.5.2. Advises the CAR if security restrictions or questionable entitlements prevent DFAS
       from processing the annuity package.

4.56. Processing RSFPP, SBP or RCSBP Annuities at Installations Without DRAPS Access.
   4.56.1. When the casualty assistance base does not have DRAPS access, claim applications for
   RSFPP, SBP or RCSBP, with supporting documentation, should be submitted directly to DFAS for
   processing.
   4.56.2. Payment should begin within 30 days of the death notification date. The CAR and DFAS
   should process the annuity in time to meet this goal.
   4.56.3. The CAR must inform DFAS by telephone at DSN 580-6153 or 1-800-321-1080 of a con-
   firmed death on the same day the CAR is notified.
   4.56.4. When informed of the death, DFAS-CL/FRCAE immediately gives the CAR information rel-
   ative to the retired pay account of the deceased, to include RSFPP or SBP election, allotments, net
   pay, VA and retirement pay, and beneficiary data.
   4.56.5. The CAR contacts the NOK to arrange a personal visit to complete the claim forms and obtain
   the supporting documentation as listed in Table 4.3. to establish the account.
       4.56.5.1. The CAR should consider the wishes of the NOK.
   4.56.6. Within 10 workdays of being notified of the death, the CAR mails the claim forms along with
   copies of any supporting documentation as listed in Table 4.3., to Defense Finance and Accounting
   Service, U. S. Military Annuitant Pay, P.O. Box 7131, London KY 40742-7131.

4.57. DIC. DIC is payable by the VA to surviving spouses, unmarried children under age 18, disabled
children, children between the ages of 18 and 23 if attending a VA-approved school, and low-income par-
ents of retirees who die from a disease or injury incurred or aggravated while on active duty or active duty
for training, an injury incurred or aggravated in the line of duty while on inactive duty for training, or a
disability otherwise compensable under laws administered by the VA. DIC payments may also be autho-
rized for the survivor of a retiree who had a service-connected total disability at the time of death but
whose death was not the result of his/her service-connected disability. The survivor qualifies if the retiree
112                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


was continuously rated totally disabled for a period of 10 or more years immediately preceding death, or
the retiree was so rated for a period of not less than 5 years from the date of discharge from military ser-
vice. Payments under this provision are subjected to offset by the amount received from judicial proceed-
ings brought on account of the retiree’s death. DIC is not paid if the VA determines that the retiree’s own
misconduct contributed to the death. The monthly DIC rate paid to a surviving spouse of a retiree for
deaths occurring after 1 January 1993 is the same for all pay grades. The DIC amount paid for a spouse
with one or more children of the deceased retiree is increased for each child. The amount of the DIC pay-
ment for parents varies according to the number of parents, the amount of their individual or combined
total annual income, and whether they live together or, if remarried, live with a spouse. DIC payments to
a surviving spouse are payable for life, as long as the spouse does not remarry. Should the surviving
spouse remarry, payments are terminated, but may be restored if the subsequent marriage ends in death,
divorce or annulment. See VAP 80-XX-1* *NOTE: The second two digits represent the year of publica-
tion.
for additional information.
      4.57.1. To apply for DIC complete the appropriate claim application as listed in Table 4.3.
      4.57.2. Mail the original claim application and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in
      Table 4.3., to the VARO.

4.58. Non-Service-Connected Death Pension. If the VARO determines that the NOK is not eligible for
DIC, they may be eligible to apply for a non-service-connected death pension. Surviving spouses of
deceased members with wartime service and unmarried children under age 18, age 23 if attending a
VA-approved school, may be eligible for this pension if they meet income limitations prescribed by law.
Qualifying children who become incapable of self-support because of a disability before age 18 may be
eligible for a pension as long as the condition exists, unless the child marries or the child’s income
exceeds the income limit. The rate of pension depends on the amount of income the surviving spouse or
child receives from other sources. A pension is not payable to those whose estates are so large that it is
reasonable to assume the estate will maintain them financially. The VA will determine their eligibility.
See VAP 80-XX-1*, for additional information. *NOTE: The second two digits represent the year of pub-
lication.
      4.58.1. To apply for a non-service-connected death pension, eligible survivors should visit their local
      VA office to complete the appropriate claim application as listed in Table 4.3.
      4.58.2. Survivors will need to provide the supporting documentation as listed in Table 4.3.

4.59. SGLI. Retirees rated totally disabled on the date of retirement retain SGLI coverage until the dis-
ability ceased to be total in degree, but not for more than 1 year. Determination and payment of proceeds
are made by the OSGLI under the jurisdiction of the VA. Payment of proceeds to a beneficiary is exempt
from taxation. The insured member may have designated as principal or contingent beneficiary any per-
son, firm, corporation or legal entity, including his/her estate, individually or as a trustee. If the member
designated a trust, he/she indicated the name and date of the trust in the beneficiary block. If the member
designated a trust through a will, he/she annotated “Last Will and Testament” in the beneficiary block. If
the member chose not to designate a specific beneficiary but preferred the proceeds be paid in the order of
precedence, the member selected the “By Law” designation.
      4.59.1. When the “By Law” designation is used, the proceeds are automatically paid in the following
      order of precedence:
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    113


       4.59.1.1. The member’s lawful surviving spouse.
       4.59.1.2. If there is no spouse, to the child or children of the member in equal shares, with the
       shares of any deceased child to be distributed among the descendants of that child.
       4.59.1.3. If none of the above, to the parents of the member in equal shares or to the surviving par-
       ent.
       4.59.1.4. If none of the above, to the duly appointed legal representative of the member’s estate.
       4.59.1.5. If none of the above, to the person(s) determined to be entitled under the laws of the
       state in which the member was domiciled.
   4.59.2. For additional information on beneficiaries, see paragraph 8.8. of this AFI and VA Handbook,
   for additional information.
   4.59.3. If the retiree was covered under SGLI, complete the claim form as listed in Table 4.3.
   4.59.4. Mail the original claim form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table
   4.3., to OSGLI, 209 Mt. Pleasant Ave, Livingston NJ 07039-2747.

4.60. Veterans’ Group Life Insurance (VGLI). This program allows retirees, upon retirement, to con-
vert their SGLI coverage during the first 120 days following retirement, or 1 year following retirement for
totally disabled retirees. VGLI is a 5-year renewable term policy, administered by the OSGLI under the
jurisdiction of the VA. VGLI is issued up to the maximum allowed by law for SGLI, but not for more than
the amount of SGLI the retiree had in force at the time of retirement.
   4.60.1. See the Servicemembers’ and Veterans’ Group Life Insurance Handbook, for additional
   information.
   4.60.2. If the retiree was covered under VGLI, complete the claim form as listed in Table 4.3.
   4.60.3. Mail the original claim form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table
   4.3., to OSGLI, 209 W. Mt. Pleasant Ave., Livingston NJ 07039-2747.

4.61. SDVI. SDVI is life insurance limited to veterans who left the Service after 24 April 1951. A mem-
ber who had a service-connected disability but was otherwise in good health could apply to the VA for up
to $10,000 in SDVI life insurance coverage at standard rates. Members rated totally disabled by the VA
could apply for a waiver of premiums. For those members eligible for this waiver, additional coverage of
up to $20,000 is available, but the premiums cannot be waived. See VAP 80-XX-1* for additional infor-
mation. *NOTE: The second two digits represent the year of publication.
   4.61.1. If the retiree was covered under SDVI, complete the claim form as listed in Table 4.3.
   4.61.2. Mail the original claim form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table
   4.3., to the VARO and Insurance Center, Box 8079, Philadelphia PA 19101.

4.62. National Service Life Insurance (NSLI). Except for RH (disability) policies, no retiree has
enrolled in this program since 23 April 1951.
   4.62.1. If the retiree was covered under NSLI, complete the claim form as listed in Table 4.3.
   4.62.2. Mail the original form and copies of any supporting documentation, as listed in Table 4.3., to
   the VARO and Insurance Center, Box 8079, Philadelphia PA 19101.
114                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


4.63. Veterans’ Educational Assistance Program (VEAP) and Montgomery GI Bill Refunds. T h e
VA will pay a special death benefit to a designated survivor in the event of the service-connected death of
an individual within 1 year after discharge or release. The deceased must either have been entitled to edu-
cational assistance under these programs or a participant in the programs who would have been so entitled
but for the high school diploma or length-of-service requirement. The amount paid will be equal to the
participant’s actual military pay reduction less any education benefits paid. If the retiree contributed to
these programs, the NOK may be entitled to the death benefit. The death benefit is paid to the SGLI ben-
eficiary. The CAR should submit a letter, along with the SGLI Certificate (SGLV 8286) and a copy of the
DD Form 1300 as listed in Table 4.3., to the appropriate VARO listed below. See VAP 80-XX-1*, for
additional benefit information. *NOTE: The second two digits represent the year of publication.
      4.63.1. Claims for the Montgomery GI Bill death benefit should be sent to the VARO, St. Louis
      Regional Processing Officer, ATTN: Chapter 30, Montgomery GI Bill, PO Box 66830, 331/225, St.
      Louis MO 63103-6830.
      4.63.2. Claims for a VEAP refund should be sent to:
         4.63.2.1. Eastern Region (CT, DE, DC, MA, MD, ME, NH, NJ, NY, OH, PA, RI, VA, VT, WV,
         and Foreign Schools). VARO, PO Box 4616, Buffalo NY 14240-4616, ATTN: Chapter 30, Death
         Benefit.
         4.63.2.2. Central Region (CO, IA, IL, IN, KS, KY, MI, MN, MO, MT, NE, ND, SD, WI, WY).
         VARO, PO Box 66830, St. Louis MO 63166-6830, ATTN: Chapter 30, Death Benefit.
         4.63.2.3. Southern Region (AL, AR, FL, GA, LA, MS, NC, SC, TN, and Puerto Rico). VARO,
         PO Box 54346, Atlanta GA 30308-0346, ATTN: Chapter 30, Death Benefit.
         4.63.2.4. Western Region (AK, AZ, CA, HI, ID, NM, NV, OK, OR, TX, UT, WA, and Philip-
         pines). VARO, PO Box 8888, Muskogee OK 74402-8888, ATTN: Chapter 30, Death Benefit.

4.64. Social Security Payments. Social Security monthly benefits are paid to a spouse or a divorced
spouse, age 60 or over; a spouse or divorced spouse regardless of age with children of the decedent under
age 16 or disabled in their care and meeting Social Security requirements. A divorced spouse must have
been married to the servicemember at least 10 years. Monthly payments are also paid to children until age
18, 19 if a full-time student at a primary or secondary school, or age 18 or older if disabled before age 18.
Spouses who wait until age 65 to apply for Social Security receive maximum benefits. However, they can
receive reduced Social Security payments between ages 60 and 65. Dependent parents are eligible for
benefits at age 62 if they were more than 50 percent dependent on the deceased servicemember for their
support. The amount paid can only be determined by the Social Security Administration, which has a
record of the wages earned by the member during the period of both military and civilian employment
under the Social Security Program. To apply for this benefit, eligible survivors should make application
through the nearest Social Security Office. This office will explain the benefit, determine their eligibility,
the amount to be paid, and help them complete the required claim forms. Survivors should apply early, as
the law generally permits retroactive payments of only 12 months. Survivors will need to provide support-
ing documentation as listed in Table 4.3.

4.65. Social Security Lump Sum Death Payment. The Social Security Administration pays a lump
sum death payment, up to $255, to the surviving spouse living with the member at the time of death. Sep-
aration because of military service, is considered living together. If there is no surviving spouse, it is paid
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                      115


to the oldest child who was eligible for or entitled to Social Security benefits during the month of the
member’s death. No other survivors are entitled to this benefit. This benefit is paid even if burial, funeral,
or memorial benefits were paid by the Air Force. To receive this benefit, eligible survivors must make
application through the nearest Social Security Office. This office will explain the benefit, determine their
eligibility, the amount to be paid, and help them complete the required claim forms. Survivors will need
to provide supporting documentation as listed in Table 4.3.

4.66. Other Assistance. The CAR addresses these other matters:
   4.66.1. Living outside the CONUS. If the NOK plan to establish residence outside the CONUS, the
   CAR should:
       4.66.1.1. Advise them that military privileges may or may not be available to them.
       4.66.1.2. Advise them that the government will not pay import duties on items such as household
       goods and automobiles.
       4.66.1.3. Contact the overseas installation nearest the NOK’s planned residence to obtain current
       information about military privileges and import duties, and send the information in writing to the
       NOK (see AFI 24-101).
   4.66.2. Status of Forces Agreements. The CAR should:
       4.66.2.1. Tell NOK living overseas that due to host-country restrictions in Status of Forces
       Agreements, they may have to live independently of the overseas installation.
       4.66.2.2. Summarize the relevant information on the AF IMT 58.
   4.66.3. Fraudulent claims. The CAR should:
       4.66.3.1. Counsel the NOK about possible fraudulent claims against the deceased member's
       estate.
       4.66.3.2. Advise them to refer any suspicious requests for money to the executor of the deceased
       member's estate.
   4.66.4. Uniformed Services Identification (ID) and Privilege Card. The CAR should:
       4.66.4.1. Obtain from the NOK the member’s DD Form 2 (Retired), United States Uniformed
       Services ID Card.
       4.66.4.2. Document the issue and expiration date in the Additional Comments Section of the AF
       IMT 58 and ask the NOK if there are any CHAMPUS or TRICARE claims pending against the
       member's ID card.
       4.66.4.3. Destroy the ID card (cut it up or give it to the MPF customer service element for
       destruction).
       4.66.4.4. Escort the NOK to the MPF customer service element and assist them with applying for
       new ID cards.
   4.66.5. Civilian death certificate: The CAR should:
       4.66.5.1. Tell the NOK they might need copies of the civilian death certificate in the future.
116                                                       AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


         4.66.5.2. Explain that the Air Force is not authorized to purchase the death certificate for the
         NOK.
         4.66.5.3. Provide the cost of the document and the address of the State Vital Statistics Office or
         Health Department.
         4.66.5.4. Refer the NOK to the funeral director for assistance in obtaining copies of the death cer-
         tificate.

4.67. Additional Casualty Assistance Visits or Contacts: The CAR should:
      4.67.1. Contact the NOK of a deceased retiree at least once every:
         4.67.1.1. 30 days for the first 2 months after a retiree’s death.
         4.67.1.2. 60 days thereafter until the NOK receives all benefits or the case is closed.
      4.67.2. Make additional contacts based on problems encountered and the NOK’s desires.
      4.67.3. Monitor the case for receipt of DIC, unpaid pay and allowances, RSFPP, SBP, or RCSBP and
      Social Security Administration entitlements.
      4.67.4. While it is not mandatory that you personally apply for DIC in each case, it is imperative that
      the NOK be given the opportunity to apply. If local VA or service agencies are not available, it is your
      responsibility to ensure the NOK applies when appropriate.
      4.67.5. When making contact with the NOK:
         4.67.5.1. Give the NOK additional advice regarding benefits, if necessary, and help them file
         claims and applications.
         4.67.5.2. Ask about the status of benefit claims or applications already processed and offer to help
         expedite settlement, if applicable.
         4.67.5.3. Return one-of-a-kind documents (i.e., marriage or birth certificate, or divorce decree) to
         the NOK in person if possible or by certified mail, return receipt requested.
         4.67.5.4. Annotate each contact with the NOK, and summarize relevant information on the AF
         IMT 58, using Attachment 21.

4.68. Administrative Closing of Casualty Assistance Cases.
      4.68.1. Closing casualty assistance cases is an administrative action for control of records and does
      not preclude further assistance to the NOK, such as appealing denials of benefits.
      4.68.2. The CAR follows these procedures:
         4.68.2.1. Close retiree cases, regardless of the installation’s DRAPS capability, 6 months after
         learning of the retiree’s death, on AF IMT 58.
         4.68.2.2. If benefits applied for are denied or delayed by other than an Air Force agency, continue
         to monitor these applications until a final determination has been made.
         4.68.2.3. E-mail or mail the error-free AF IMT 58 to HQ AFPC/DPDXIDL, 550 C Street West,
         Suite 50, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4752, within 5 workdays after learning the NOK has received
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                    117


       all benefits and entitlements in blocks 10A through 10J. as appropriate, or a final determination
       has been made (see Attachment 21). E-mail address is: afpc.dpdxidl@randolph.af.mil.
          4.68.2.3.1. The first page of the AF IMT 58 is mandatory. The assistance summary on the
          reverse is optional.
          4.68.2.3.2. Retain a copy of the entire form in the case file.
          4.68.2.3.3. Ensure all items on the form are properly completed and dates are recorded accu-
          rately.
          4.68.2.3.4. Ensure items 13 and 14 are signed and dated by the CAR.
          4.68.2.3.5. If more than one installation provided assistance, make sure other family members
          or persons designated beneficiaries applied for and received the benefits.
          4.68.2.3.6. Keep proof of e-mail transmission to HQ AFPC/DPDXIDL on file with the signed
          AF IMT 58 in the case file.

4.69. Maintenance of Casualty Assistance Case Files:
   4.69.1. Maintain casualty assistance case files in accordance with AFI 37-138.
   4.69.2. Establish case files for each casualty and file them alphabetically.
   4.69.3. Case files must contain:
       4.69.3.1. A chronological record of contacts, listed on AF IMT 58, in item 11, with:
          4.69.3.1.1. NOK.
          4.69.3.1.2. Other family members and persons designated as beneficiaries, if applicable.
          4.69.3.1.3. Other government agencies.
          4.69.3.1.4. Civilian agencies.
       4.69.3.2. CAR’s actions on behalf of the NOK.
       4.69.3.3. Copies of all messages, memorandums, and claim forms sent to other agencies and the
       NOK.
       4.69.3.4. Any other relevant documents.
   4.69.4. Installations reporting casualties only. Installations reporting retiree deaths but having no
   assistance responsibilities should establish an interim case file for each casualty reported, and destroy
   the case file 6 months after the date of death (AF RDS, table 36-03, rule 02.00).

4.70. Disposition of Casualty Assistance Case Files. Dispose of casualty case files IAW AF Records
Disposition Schedule (RDS) located HTTPS://WEBRIMS.AMC.AF.MIL/RDS/INDEX.cfm, Records
Disposition Schedule.

4.71. Processing RSFPP, SBP or RCSBP Annuity Payment When a Retiree Is Missing. A n S B P
beneficiary may apply for an annuity if the participating member’s retired pay has been suspended
because the member is missing.
   4.71.1. See paragraph 4.52. through 4.54. for RSFPP and SBP information.
118                                                        AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      4.71.2. DFAS-CL suspends a missing retiree's retired pay, but the CAR may begin processing annu-
      ity claims if the retiree is an RSFPP or SBP participant. NOTE: This procedure is not officially casu-
      alty assistance since there is no legal determination of death.
      4.71.3. Due to the unique circumstances of these cases, the CAR should immediately telephone HQ
      AFPC/DPFCS at DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048 for guidance on each case.
      4.71.4. Since it is not officially casualty assistance, do not start a case file or track annuity payment.
      4.71.5. The CAR helps the beneficiary collect and submit evidence that:
         4.71.5.1. The retiree has been missing for at least 30 days.
         4.71.5.2. A reasonable person would conclude that the retiree is dead.
         4.71.5.3. Such evidence must include:
             4.71.5.3.1. A statement signed by the applicant describing the circumstances of the retiree's
             disappearance.
             4.71.5.3.2. Supporting documents such as:
                 4.71.5.3.2.1. A police missing person report.
                 4.71.5.3.2.2. Signed statements from persons who last saw the retiree alive.
                 4.71.5.3.2.3. A detailed description of the geographical location, local weather conditions,
                 and the mental and physical condition of the retiree, with a statement regarding the retiree's
                 chance of surviving.
      4.71.6. DFAS/JA determines whether to start RSFPP or SBP annuity payments. A decision to begin
      payments does not constitute a legal determination of death.
      4.71.7. The date the Air Force suspended retired pay will be considered the date of death for payment
      purposes.
      4.71.8. If the retiree participated in RSFPP or SBP, the CAR:
         4.71.8.1. Completes the claim forms as listed in Table 4.3.
         4.71.8.2. Mails the original claim forms, with copies of any supporting documentation as listed in
         Table 4.3., to Defense Finance and Accounting Service, U. S. Military Annuitant Pay, P. O. Box
         7131, London KY 40742-7131.
      4.71.9. Contacts the base FSO to check on the payment status of the RSFPP or SBP annuity prior to
      checking with DFAS.
      4.71.10. If the Air Force later declares the retiree deceased, the CAR performs the appropriate casu-
      alty reporting and assistance.
