                                               Attachment 3

                                 DUSTWUN AND MISSING REPORTS
(RCS: DD-FM&P(AR)1664, REPORT OF CASUALTY)

A3.1. General.
      A3.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
      A3.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
      A3.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A3.2. Format.
      A3.2.1. Report on those persons indicated in Table 1.1.
      A3.2.2. Send the report to the addressees and locations indicated in Table 2.1. and Table 2.2..

A3.3. Specific Instructions.
      A3.3.1. File DUSTWUN Reports only on military members.
      A3.3.2. Prepare initial Casualty Reports on missing DoD and DAF civilian employees overseas in
      order to facilitate transportation of the NOK and household goods back to CONUS.
      A3.3.3. Prepare the report in an easily readable tabular form, with each item lettered and beginning
      on a new line.
      A3.3.4. If an initial Casualty Report cannot be submitted without including sensitive information,
      label it “ENCRYPT FOR TRANSMISSION ONLY” (EFTO).
      A3.3.5. If classified information must be used to complete any item on an initial Casualty Report,
      state in that item “SEE CLASSIFIED SUPPLEMENTAL REPORT” and submit a classified supple-
      mental report immediately after the unclassified initial report.
      A3.3.6. Label unknown or unconfirmed items “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” or “UNCONFIRMED”
      respectively, and report or confirm the information as soon as possible in a supplemental report.
      A3.3.7. Do not label any item “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” if there is reportable information avail-
      able that would be of interest to family members or of value to the addressees of the report. Instead,
      label such information “UNCONFIRMED.”
      A3.3.8. Label any item not required or not applicable “N/A.”
      A3.3.9. If an initial Casualty Report contains incorrect information, submit a supplemental report at
      once and label the corrected items “CORRECTED.”
      A3.3.10. All supplemental reports must reference the initial Casualty Report.

A3.4. Message Precedence.
      A3.4.1. Use IMMEDIATE for:
         A3.4.1.1. All action addressees (see Table 2.1. and Table 2.2.).
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                             189


      A3.4.1.2. Supplemental reports containing urgent information used to notify the NOK.
   A3.4.2. Use PRIORITY for:
      A3.4.2.1. Information addressees on initial reports (see Table 2.1. and Table 2.2.).
      A3.4.2.2. All addressees on supplemental reports from any overseas location.
   A3.4.3. Use ROUTINE:
      A3.4.3.1. For supplemental reports from any CONUS location.
      A3.4.3.2. To report any additional information or questions concerning the casualty.

A3.5. Subject Line of Message Report. Enter CASUALTY REPORT and:
   A3.5.1. INITIAL or SUPPLEMENTAL.
   A3.5.2. DUSTWUN or MISSING REPORT.
   A3.5.3. HOSTILE or NONHOSTILE (see Attachment 1 for definitions).

A3.6. Item-by-Item Instructions.
   A3.6.1. Item A—Name of Casualty:
      A3.6.1.1. Enter the last name.
      A3.6.1.2. Repeat the last name
      A3.6.1.3. Enter the first name, middle name, and suffix, if any.
      A3.6.1.4. EXAMPLE: WITHERSPOON, REPEAT WITHERSPOON , VALENCIA RENEY
   A3.6.2. Item B—Grade:
      A3.6.2.1. Enter the military grade, cadet grade, or civilian grade.
      A3.6.2.2. EXAMPLE: MAJOR; CADET FIRST CLASS; GS-11.
   A3.6.3. Item C—Social Security Number (SSN):
      A3.6.3.1. For a military member, cadet, or civilian, enter the SSN and repeat.
          A3.6.3.1.1. EXAMPLE: 123-45-6789 REPEAT 123-45-6789.
   A3.6.4. Item D—Organization, MAJCOM, and Installation:
      A3.6.4.1. List the complete name of the member's unit and installation of assignment, including
      Army, Air Force, or Fleet Post Office (APO or FPO), MAJCOM, and unit and installation of
      attachment, if applicable. Do not abbreviate.
          A3.6.4.1.1. EXAMPLE: 18TH TACTICAL FIGHTER WING, PACIFIC AIR FORCES,
          OSAN AIR BASE, KOREA, APO SAN FRANCISCO 96570.
      A3.6.4.2. If the member was on TDY or on TDY en route to a PCS, include the TDY and gaining
      unit and installation, as applicable.
          A3.6.4.2.1. EXAMPLE: TDY TO 343RD TACTICAL FIGHTER WING, EIELSON AIR
          FORCE BASE, ALASKA.
190                                                         AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


         A3.6.4.3. Follow these guidelines to report the member's duty status at the time the Air Force
         declared him/her DUSTWUN or missing:
             A3.6.4.3.1. Report members of the active Air Force, including USAFA cadets, as active duty
             (AD).
             A3.6.4.3.2. Report members of the ANG and USAFR as AD, active duty for training (ADT),
             inactive duty for training (IDT), or non-duty status. NOTE: The member's commander or a
             designee determines which duty status applies and whether this duty was under a competent
             authority. This is particularly true if the member was on a flight as a passenger rather than a
             crewmember.
             A3.6.4.3.3. Report AFROTC applicants and cadets as professional military training (PMT).
         A3.6.4.4. Include with the duty status whether the member was on duty, off duty, or on leave.
             A3.6.4.4.1. EXAMPLES: AD/ON DUTY; ADT/OFF DUTY; AD/ON LEAVE.
      A3.6.5. Item E—Last Known Location of Individual:
         A3.6.5.1. If the location or geographic coordinates are classified, so state and include them in a
         classified supplement.
         A3.6.5.2. If it is a flight position, also indicate the:
             A3.6.5.2.1. Flight's home base or origin.
             A3.6.5.2.2. Base of last departure.
             A3.6.5.2.3. Final destination.
             A3.6.5.2.4. Flight's last radar or radio position.
         A3.6.5.3. EXAMPLE: IN THE AREA NEAR VALDEZ, ALASKA, ON 12 MAR 98, AT
         APPROXIMATELY LATITUDE 61 DEGREES, 10 MINUTES NORTH AND LONGITUDE
         146 DEGREES, 30 MINUTES WEST. BASE OF ORIGIN/LAST DEPARTURE: EIELSON
         AFB AK. FINAL DESTINATION: EIELSON AFB AK.
      A3.6.6. Item F—Date and Time of Loss.
         A3.6.6.1. Use local date and approximate local time.
             A3.6.6.1.1. EXAMPLE: 12 MAR 98/1514L.
         A3.6.6.2. If submitting a Missing Report after having initially submitted a DUSTWUN Report,
         be sure the local date and approximate local time are the same as reported in the DUSTWUN
         Report, unless there is evidence to substantiate a different date and time.
      A3.6.7. Item G—Circumstances.
         A3.6.7.1. Furnish an accurate and explicit account of the circumstances leading to the current sta-
         tus of the individual so HQ AFPC/DPFC and intermediate commanders are aware of all facts
         available to the reporting commander.
         A3.6.7.2. Never report this item as "unknown."
             A3.6.7.2.1. At a minimum, report the information on which the commander based the mem-
             ber's status and confirm the information as soon as possible.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                  191


     A3.6.7.3. Report the local date and time that search personnel first arrived in the area.
         A3.6.7.3.1. Explain if conditions prevent aerial or ground search.
     A3.6.7.4. If the casualty resulted from an aircraft accident or incident, state whether that aircraft
     was military, aero club, private, or civilian, and state the aircraft's designation.
     A3.6.7.5. Report military crew position of record or actual position at the time of the accident or
     incident and the type of aircraft and mission.
     A3.6.7.6. When recommending a person be placed in a missing status, a detailed account of the
     circumstances surrounding the casualty, except non-duty status ANG and USAFR members, is
     very important.
         A3.6.7.6.1. HQ AFPC/DPFC will further categorize the casualty as missing in action,
         detained, captured, etc., based on the information provided (see Attachment 1, Terms, Miss-
         ing, for definitions).
         A3.6.7.6.2. Commanders must include all information available that may have a bearing on
         accurately categorizing the missing person.
     A3.6.7.7. In hostile situations in which the disappearance is considered to be due to hostile action,
     and active search and rescue efforts are impossible, state "NO SEARCH PROGRESS REPORTS
     REQUIRED" and give the reason why.
     A3.6.7.8. EXAMPLE: AN F-16 AIRCRAFT ON A ROUTINE TRAINING MISSION, AND
     CLEARED FOR THREE LOW APPROACHES AT VALDEZ, AK, LOST RADIO/RADAR
     CONTACT AFTER SECOND APPROACH AT 1514L. AERIAL SEARCH BEGAN 12 MAR
     98, 1700L, BY 24TH STRATEGIC RECONNAISSANCE SQUADRON, EIELSON AFB AK.
     PILOT/AIRCRAFT COMMANDER.
  A3.6.8. Item H—Date of vRED or DD Form 93.
     A3.6.8.1. Enter date of member's latest vRED or DD Form 93.
         A3.6.8.1.1. EXAMPLE: 2 FEB 97.
  A3.6.9. Item I—Persons Notified or To Be Notified.
     A3.6.9.1. Report the name, relationship, and address of persons listed on the member's vRED or
     DD Form 93.
     A3.6.9.2. For overseas addresses, include the Postal Service Center (PSC) box and the APO or
     FPO.
     A3.6.9.3. Report persons listed to receive gratuity pay, if no surviving spouse or child, or in item
     9 of the DD Form 93 only if they will receive the death gratuity payment or if they appear else-
     where on the form.
     A3.6.9.4. Report the name, relationship, and address of designated SGLI beneficiaries who will
     actually receive insurance proceeds if not previously listed on the member’s vRED or DD Form
     93.
     A3.6.9.5. If all persons listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 are deceased, report the name, rela-
     tionship to the member, and address of any other NOK listed on:
192                                                     AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


             A3.6.9.5.1. DD Form 1966, Record of Military Processing-Armed Forces of the United
             States, located in Section 4 of the member’s UPRG.
             A3.6.9.5.2. Any other documents within the member’s UPRG listing NOK.
         A3.6.9.6. If one or more persons listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 are active or retired military,
         so state and report their grade and service.
         A3.6.9.7. If one or more persons listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 are deceased or in ill health,
         so state.
         A3.6.9.8. EXAMPLE: SHIRLEY A. JONES, SPOUSE, 1328 LIBERTY ST, SAN ANTONIO,
         TX 78244; JOSEPH D. JONES, SON, SAME AS SPOUSE, JOSEPH (NMI) JONES, FATHER,
         601 COOK ST, BARRACKVILLE WV 26559; KATHRYN A. JONES, MOTHER, SAME AS
         FATHER.
         A3.6.9.9. When reporting that a family member is missing overseas, give the full name, relation-
         ship to the member, address and telephone number of each relative the sponsor desires to be noti-
         fied.
             A3.6.9.9.1. EXAMPLE: JOSEPH (NMI) JONES, FATHER, 601 COOK ST, BARRACK-
             VILLE, WV 26559; 200-345-6789; KATHRYN A. JONES, MOTHER, SAME AS FATHER.
      A3.6.10. Item J—Notification Source, Date, and Time.
         A3.6.10.1. Report who notified which persons from item I (see A3.6.9.).
             A3.6.10.1.1. Include the local date and time they made the notifications.
         A3.6.10.2. If the member's commander or a designated representative notified the NOK, state his
         or her grade, name, and assigned organization.
             A3.6.10.2.1. EXAMPLE: LT COL SUSAN E. MATTHEWS, 21ALS, RANDOLPH AFB
             TX NOTIFIED (name and relationship) ON 13 MAR 98 AT 1500L.
         A3.6.10.3. If someone outside the Air Force notified the NOK, state the person's name and title or
         organization, if applicable.
             A3.6.10.3.1. EXAMPLE: SHERIFF JOHN A. BLACK, KENT COUNTY SHERIFF, NOTI-
             FIED (name and relationship) ON 14 MAR 92 AT 1415L.
         A3.6.10.4. When the NOK wish to notify other family members, state the NOK's name and rela-
         tionship and when they notified or will notify the other family members.
             A3.6.10.4.1. Call HQ AFPC/DPFCS as soon as the NOK notifies the other family members.
                A3.6.10.4.1.1. EXAMPLE: MRS. MARY E. JONES, SPOUSE, WILL NOTIFY (name
                and relationship) ON 13 MAR 98 AT 1630L; WILL CALL AFPC/DPFCS WHEN
                ACCOMPLISHED.
         A3.6.10.5. If notification was made to a person on behalf of minor children not living with the
         spouse, state who made notification and the name of the person notified.
             A3.6.10.5.1. EXAMPLE: MAJOR CHARLES F. SWANK, 21ALS, RANDOLPH AFB TX
             NOTIFIED MRS. NANCY J. CURRAN (MEMBER’S EX-SPOUSE) ON BEHALF OF
             MINOR CHILDREN ON 13 MAR 98 AT 1530L.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                   193


     A3.6.10.6. If AFPC/DPFCS is to make notification, state: "Request AFPC make notification to
     the following persons: (Indicate name, relationship to member, and any other pertinent informa-
     tion)."
         A3.6.10.6.1. EXAMPLE: REQUEST AFPC MAKE NOTIFICATION TO THE FOLLOW-
         ING PERSONS: JOSEPH (NMN) JONES, FATHER, AND KATHRYN A. JONES,
         MOTHER, SAME AS ITEM I.
     A3.6.10.7. If notification is not advisable due to special circumstances such as ill health, state the
     reason.
     A3.6.10.8. If the address of anyone listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 is unknown and that per-
     son has not been notified, tell what efforts the Air Force has made for finding the person (who you
     queried, the results, etc.).
     A3.6.10.9. See paragraph 3.5. for notifying the NOK of foreign nationals in the US under the aus-
     pices of the Air Force.
  A3.6.11. Item K—Search Progress Reports:
     A3.6.11.1. If the Air Force is going to conduct a search, state the grade, name, and unit of the
     responsible commander who will provide the NOK with daily progress reports.
     A3.6.11.2. If an overseas commander wishes to ask AFPC to help provide Daily Progress Reports
     to the NOK, state "REQUEST AFPC PROVIDE DAILY PROGRESS REPORTS TO THE FOL-
     LOWING PERSONS: (indicate name and relationship)."
  A3.6.12. Item L—Casualty Assistance:
     A3.6.12.1. State that "THE REPORTING UNIT IS (OR IS NOT) PROVIDING CASUALTY
     ASSISTANCE to (name and relationship)."
     A3.6.12.2. If the reporting base is not providing casualty assistance, list the base that will assist
     the NOK and ensure that the base is an addressee on all reports.
     A3.6.12.3. If the NOK will be departing your area of assistance responsibility, state when they're
     moving and their new address and telephone number.
     A3.6.12.4. For a civilian employee, indicate the location of the Civilian Personnel Flight Office
     (CPFO) that will assist the NOK.
  A3.6.13. Item M—Circumstance Letters (Missing Report Only) (see paragraphs 5.2. and 5.4.) State
  to whom the Air Force will send letter and the projected dispatch date.
     A3.6.13.1. EXAMPLE: COMMANDER WILL SEND A CIRCUMSTANCE LETTER TO
     (name and relationship) ON 18 MAR 04.
  A3.6.14. Item N—Additional Information Required (Missing Report Only) for USAFA cadets,
  AFROTC applicants and cadets, civilian employees, and ANG and USAFR members on active duty
  for training or inactive duty training.
     A3.6.14.1. For ANG and USAFR members, report Home of Record.
     A3.6.14.2. For USAFA cadets, AFROTC applicants/cadets, and civilian employees, report:
         A3.6.14.2.1. Date and place of birth.
194                                               AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      A3.6.14.2.2. Home of record.
      A3.6.14.2.3. Religious preference.
      A3.6.14.2.4. Race, ethnic group, and sex.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                 195


                                              Attachment 4

  SEARCH PROGRESS REPORT--(RCS: HAF-DP(AR)9476, MISSING PERSONS REPORT)

A4.1. General.
   A4.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
   A4.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
   A4.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A4.2. Format.
   A4.2.1. Send the report to the addressees and locations indicated in Table 2.1. and Table 2.2..

A4.3. Specific Instructions.
   A4.3.1. In all nonhostile situations, when a military member is declared DUSTWUN or a person is
   declared Missing, the responsible commander ensures the CAR submits the appropriate Search
   Progress Report daily (see paragraphs 2.15. and 2.21.).
       A4.3.1.1. Submit similar reports in hostile situations if a search is possible.
   A4.3.2. Prepare the report in an easily readable tabular form, with each item lettered and beginning
   on a new line.
   A4.3.3. All progress reports must include items A through E.
   A4.3.4. Reference the initial Casualty Report and the most recent Search Progress Report.
   A4.3.5. Once the search is terminated, the commander evaluates all available evidence and after
   reviewing the provisions of paragraph 2.17., ensures the CAR submits the appropriate Casualty
   Report (see paragraphs 2.15. and 2.21.).
   A4.3.6. Report item F (see A4.6.6.) when the Air Force discontinues the search.

A4.4. Message Precedence.
   A4.4.1. Use IMMEDIATE for:
       A4.4.1.1. All action addressees (see Table 2.1. and Table 2.2.).
       A4.4.1.2. Supplemental reports containing urgent information used to notify the NOK.
   A4.4.2. Use PRIORITY for:
       A4.4.2.1. Information addressees on initial reports (see Table 2.1. and Table 2.2.).
       A4.4.2.2. All addressees on supplemental reports from any overseas location.
   A4.4.3. Use ROUTINE:
       A4.4.3.1. For supplemental reports from any CONUS location.
       A4.4.3.2. To report any additional information or questions concerning the casualty.
196                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


A4.5. Subject Line of Message Report. Enter:
      A4.5.1. CASUALTY REPORT, SEARCH PROGRESS REPORT or FINAL SEARCH PROGRESS
      REPORT.
      A4.5.2. HOSTILE or NONHOSTILE (see Attachment 1 for definitions).

A4.6. Item-by-Item Instructions.
      A4.6.1. Item A—Date and Type of Incident:
         A4.6.1.1. Use local date and provide a brief description of the incident.
         A4.6.1.2. EXAMPLE: F-16C AIRCRAFT MISSING IN FLIGHT NEAR VALDEZ, ALASKA,
         ON 12 MAR 98, AT APPROXIMATELY LATITUDE 61 DEGREES, 10 MINUTES NORTH
         AND LONGITUDE 146 DEGREES, 30 MINUTES WEST.
      A4.6.2. Item B—Number of Persons Involved.
         A4.6.2.1. Enter the total number of persons in each of these categories still unaccounted for:
            A4.6.2.1.1. Air Force military personnel.
            A4.6.2.1.2. Civilians.
            A4.6.2.1.3. Family members.
            A4.6.2.1.4. Military personnel from other US Services. Specify Services.
            A4.6.2.1.5. Military personnel from foreign countries. Specify countries.
            A4.6.2.1.6. EXAMPLE: ONE AIR FORCE.
      A4.6.3. Item C—Search and Investigation Data.
         A4.6.3.1. Provide all pertinent information on the extent, duration, participants, and findings of
         search and rescue operations and investigations the commander conducts.
         A4.6.3.2. Indicate areas searched and investigation findings since last report.
         A4.6.3.3. Report any findings or sightings of equipment, wreckage, or debris, where they are
         located, and if they belong to the missing conveyance or personnel (if known).
         A4.6.3.4. Include a brief summary of interviews with witnesses or others having information con-
         cerning the incident. Indicate whether the Air Force has verified the data.
         A4.6.3.5. EXAMPLE: SEARCH DAY WAS LAUNCHED AT 0850L USING 50 AIRCRAFT
         FROM CIVIL AIR PATROL, US COAST GUARD, AND AIR FORCE. WEATHER IN THE
         PRIMARY SEARCH AREA WAS GOOD PERMITTING THOROUGH COVERAGE. A
         HIGHLY EXPERIENCED GROUND SEARCH TEAM FROM ALASKA STATE PARK SYS-
         TEM WAS FLOWN OVER THE SEARCH AREA TO EVALUATE THE POSSIBILITY OF
         PERFORMING GROUND SEARCH. THEY STATED THAT THE AMOUNT OF SNOW AND
         DANGER OF AVALANCHES PRECLUDE A GROUND SEARCH AT THIS TIME. PRI-
         MARY SEARCH AREA IS FROM 25 MILES SOUTH TO 50 MILES NORTH AND 35 MILES
         WEST TO 8 MILES EAST OF VALDEZ, ALASKA. PLANS FOR TOMORROW’S SEARCH
         INCLUDE EXPANSION OF THE PRIMARY AREA. SUMMARY OF SEARCH AS OF 13
         MAR 98: 154 SORTIES, 330.8 HOURS AND COVERAGE OF 3,250 SQUARE MILES.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                 197


  A4.6.4. Item D—Changes in Casualty Status.
     A4.6.4.1. Report all evidence that might support a future change in casualty status, including
     descriptions of:
        A4.6.4.1.1. The area in which the incident occurred, including its terrain (mountains, desert,
        jungle, etc.) or water conditions (currents, depths, sharks, distance to land, waves, tempera-
        tures, etc.).
        A4.6.4.1.2. The weather conditions in the area (snow, winds, floods, temperatures, etc.)
        A4.6.4.1.3. The physical condition of personnel, including known injuries or evidence that
        any of the persons involved are incapacitated (specify which persons).
        A4.6.4.1.4. The clothing and personal equipment available to improve chances of survival.
        A4.6.4.1.5. Relevant background information on specific personnel, such as swimming abil-
        ity, survival training, and anything in the past that shows personal behavior, habits, or hobbies
        that would increase or decrease chances of survival.
        A4.6.4.1.6. Estimate how long the missing individuals could survive.
        A4.6.4.1.7. Report any information that indicates the Air Force should change a person's sta-
        tus to AWOL or deserter.
        A4.6.4.1.8. EXAMPLE: MOUNTAINOUS TERRAIN WITH DEEP CREVICES, FRE-
        QUENT AVALANCHES REPORTED, SNOW COVERED; MODERATE WINDS.
        WEATHER CONDITIONS GOOD; HOWEVER, CAN CHANGE ON SHORT NOTICE.
        ARCTIC GEAR, FANNY PACK, ON BOARD. PER SQUADRON COMMANDER, MEM-
        BER WAS PREVIOUSLY AN AWARD-WINNING MEMBER OF A CROSS-COUNTRY
        SKI TEAM IN MICHIGAN. BASED ON MEMBER’S CONDITION, TERRAIN, AND CLI-
        MATE, SURVIVAL POSSIBLE FOR 4-6 DAYS, IF NOT SERIOUSLY ILL OR INJURED.
  A4.6.5. Item E—Information of Interest to NOK:
     A4.6.5.1. Report any information that would be of interest to NOK, such as:
        A4.6.5.1.1. The condition of other family members.
        A4.6.5.1.2. Participation of family members in search operations.
        A4.6.5.1.3. Arrival or departure of family members in search area.
        A4.6.5.1.4. Well-being of children.
        A4.6.5.1.5. EXAMPLE: SPOUSE ARRIVED IN ALASKA TODAY AT 1300L. SHE HAS
        BEEN PROVIDED LODGING ON BASE AND IS BEING PERSONALLY ESCORTED
        AND ADVISED OF SEARCH EFFORTS BY COLONEL ROBERT MORRIS, DEPUTY
        COMMANDER OPERATIONS.
  A4.6.6. Item F—Search Discontinued:
     A4.6.6.1. Report the local date and time the Air Force discontinued the search and give the rea-
     sons why, such as presence of hostile forces, inclement weather, darkness, etc.
     A4.6.6.2. Report the number of survivors or remains recovered, if any, and when appropriate
     Casualty Reports will follow.
198                                                  AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      A4.6.6.3. Indicate local date and time search will resume, if applicable.
      A4.6.6.4. EXAMPLE: THE SEARCH WAS DISCONTINUED ON 13 MAR 98 AT 1836L DUE
      TO DARKNESS. NEGATIVE RESULTS. SEARCH WILL RESUME ON 14 MAR 98, AT
      FIRST LIGHT.
      A4.6.6.5. Final Search Progress Report. If AFPC/DPFCS waives the Final Search Progress
      Report, report all information collected since submitting the last Search Progress Report on the
      appropriate Casualty Report.

   ATE STATUS).
   A5.5.2. HOSTILE or NON-HOSTILE (see Attachment 1 for definitions).

   A5.6.1. Item A—Name of Casualty:
       A5.6.1.1. Enter the last name.

         A5.6.1.2. Repeat the last name.

      A5.6.2. Item B—Grade:
         A5.6.2.1. Enter the military grade, cadet grade, or civilian grade.
         A5.6.2.2. EXAMPLE: MAJOR; CADET FIRST CLASS; GS-11.
      A5.6.3. Item C—Social Security Number (SSN):

            A5.6.3.2.3. SSN.

         tion.

         BEEN TRANSPORTED TO THE BASSETT ARMY HOSPITAL, FORT WAINWRIGHT AK.

      A5.6.6. Item F—Message to NOK:
         A5.6.6.1. The member may provide a personal message that AFPC/DPFCS immediately for-

         HOME WHEN RELEASED.

        A5.6.7.1.4. Return the individual to duty.
     A5.6.7.2. Give the dates when the Air Force plans to move the individual, if known, and
     addresses of future locations.
     A5.6.7.3. EXAMPLE: TENTATIVE PLANS ARE TO MEDEVAC MEMBER TO BROOKE
     ARMY MEDICAL CENTER, FORT SAM HOUSTON, SAN ANTONIO TX ON/OR ABOUT
     19 JUL 98.

                                                Attachment 6

          AF IMT 484, NON-HOSTILE MISSING PERSONS SUPPLEMENTARY REPORT
(RCS: HAF-DP(AR)9476, MISSING PERSONS REPORTS)

A6.1. General.
      A6.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
      A6.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
      A6.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A6.2. Specific Instructions.
      A6.2.1. Classify only those entries that contain classified information.
      A6.2.2. Within 5 calendar days from the date the commander recommends placement of a person into
      missing status, the commander, after review of the report by the installation staff judge advocate,
      sends:
         A6.2.2.1. Two original copies of the report directly to HQ AFPC/DPFCM, 550 C Street, West,
         Suite 15, Randolph AFB TX 78150-4717.
         A6.2.2.2. A copy of the report through channels to the parent MAJCOM.
         A6.2.2.3. A copy of the report to the installation CAR.
      A6.2.3. If the commander cannot submit the report within 5 calendar days, notify HQ AFPC/DPFCM
      by message of the reason for delay and the date commander expects to mail the report.
      A6.2.4. For incidents resulting in multiple missing persons, such as an aircraft mishap, submit one
      report listing all missing personnel.
         A6.2.4.1. Send a copy to each missing person’s home installation commander.
      A6.2.5. The commander must include either:
         A6.2.5.1. A recommendation to change the casualty status to deceased.
         A6.2.5.2. Detailed reasons why a person should be placed into a missing status.

A6.3. Item-by-Item Instructions.
      A6.3.1. Items 1, 2, and 3. The information in these items must be consistent with the information in
      items E, F, and G of the initial Missing Persons Report.
         A6.3.1.1. If they differ, attach an explanation.
         A6.3.1.2. Use local date and time.
      A6.3.2. Item 4. Enter airport destination or a target's name and geographic coordinates.
      A6.3.3. Item 5. Enter the intended flight route by name or geographic coordinates.
      A6.3.4. Item 6. Describe the weather conditions in the last known location.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                 203


  A6.3.5. Item 7:
     A6.3.5.1. Use exact geographic coordinates, if possible.
     A6.3.5.2. List the approximate distance from an identifiable location, if known.
     A6.3.5.3. Indicate in degrees the compass direction in which the aircraft was headed.
  A6.3.6. Item 8. Self-explanatory.
  A6.3.7. Items 9a through 9e. Self-explanatory.
  A6.3.8. Items 9f through 9h. List the specific types of armaments, special equipment, and weapons.
  A6.3.9. Item 9i. Self-explanatory.
  A6.3.10. Item 10. Self-explanatory.
  A6.3.11. Item 11:
     A6.3.11.1. List the names of all witnesses believed to have knowledge of missing personnel or
     aircraft.
     A6.3.11.2. Submit signed witness statements with the form if available.
  A6.3.12. Item 12. Provide a brief summary of:
     A6.3.12.1. The circumstances surrounding the disappearance.
     A6.3.12.2. Search efforts made.
     A6.3.12.3. List all factors that could contribute to the victim's chance of surviving, including:
         A6.3.12.3.1. Survival equipment available.
         A6.3.12.3.2. Arms available.
         A6.3.12.3.3. Natural shelter in the area.
         A6.3.12.3.4. Intelligence on local population.
     A6.3.12.4. Explain any conflicts with witness statements or other facts.
  A6.3.13. Item 13:
     A6.3.13.1. Enter the commander's recommendation on whether or not to change the casualty sta-
     tus of any missing person to deceased.
     A6.3.13.2. Include the commander's opinion on the chances for survival and the maximum sur-
     vival time likely under the stated circumstances. NOTE: The failure to find remains or the lack of
     an eyewitness account of a death are not by themselves adequate bases for determining survival is
     possible.

                                               Attachment 7

                                   SAMPLE WITNESS STATEMENT
On 5 February 1991, I was pilot of an F-15C flying MIG cover for Shark 01, piloted by Colonel Barry T.
Smith. Prior to reaching the target area, at approximately 0720L, I observed a MIG-25 making a
high-speed attack on Colonel Smith's aircraft. As I dove to intercept, I alerted Colonel Smith and
instructed him to break hard right. As Shark 01 began his break, the enemy fire hit him. I observed both
Colonel Smith and Lieutenant Colonel Irwin ejecting and that they had good parachutes. I continued in
pursuit of the MIG, got radar lock, and fired my missile, destroying the aircraft. I then returned to the inci-
dent location. At that time, I received bogey dope on inbound bandits and we were receiving a lot of
radar-guided flak. We did not conduct an organized search due to the intense enemy flak and aircraft in
the area. I saw both Colonel Smith and Irwin on the ground in what seemed to be good condition.
                                                       JENNIFER CAMPBELL, Major, USAF

                                               Attachment 9

                         SAMPLE, 9-MONTH INVESTIGATION REPORT
Appropriate Letterhead
Memorandum for AFPC/DPFCM                                                                            (date)
FROM: (Organization Mailing Address)
SUBJECT: 9-Month Investigation Report on a Missing Person
       This 9-month investigation report pertains to Major Roger C. Smith, 023-45-6789, missing from
Eglin AFB FL since 15 May 1997. I am forwarding it IAW AFI 36-3002, Casualty Services, Chapter 2.
        The initial circumstances surrounding the loss of Major Smith in an Eglin AFB Aeroclub Cessna
172 aircraft incident remain unchanged. We have maintained close contact with Air Force, state, and fed-
eral investigative agencies in an attempt to establish Major Smith's true status. However, all follow-up
actions have been negative. The only supplemental information you haven't received in subsequent
reports is that on 14 December 1997, the Federal Aviation Administration office in Pensacola FL thought
a dredging machine had recovered the tail section of the missing aircraft in a body of water adjacent to
Eglin AFB. Further analysis revealed it was from a Piper Cub rather than a Cessna.
       I based my decision to place Major Smith in a missing status on my belief that he probably
encountered severe weather soon after his departure on a routine night training flight, and that the aircraft
crashed within 20 miles of Eglin AFB. Given his outstanding physical condition, I felt it was possible for
him to survive on one of the small islands in the area, even if injured, until located by search and rescue
personnel or recreational boaters or fishermen. Considering the passage of time without any information
from or about Major Smith or anything whatsoever concerning the missing aircraft, it now appears that
Major Smith did not survive the crash of his aircraft, which apparently occurred over water. Accordingly,
I recommend that the Air Force change the status of Major Roger C. Smith from missing to deceased.
                                                      JOHN J. DOE
                                                      Brigadier General, USAF
                                                      Commander

  VSI, SI, AND III CASUALTY REPORTS--(RCS: HAF-DP(AR)9477, MEDICAL CASUALTY
                                   REPORTS)

A10.1. General.
   A10.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
   A10.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
   A10.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A10.2. Format.
   A10.2.1. Report on those persons indicated in Table 1.1.
   A10.2.2. Send the report to the addressees and locations indicated in Table 2.3.

A10.3. Specific Instructions.
   A10.3.1. Prepare the report in an easily readable tabular form, with each item lettered and beginning
   on a new line.
   A10.3.2. If an initial Casualty Report cannot be submitted without including sensitive information,
   label it “ENCRYPT FOR TRANSMISSION ONLY” (EFTO).
   A10.3.3. If classified information must be used to complete any item on an initial Casualty Report,
   state in that item “SEE CLASSIFIED SUPPLEMENTAL REPORT” and submit a classified supple-
   mental report immediately after the unclassified initial report.
   A10.3.4. Label unknown or unconfirmed items “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” or “UNCONFIRMED”
   respectively, and report or confirm the information as soon as possible in a supplemental report.
   A10.3.5. Do not label any item “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” if there is reportable information avail-
   able that would be of interest to family members or of value to the addressees of the report. Instead,
   label such information “UNCONFIRMED.”
   A10.3.6. Confirm all previously unconfirmed items in a supplemental report as soon as possible.
   A10.3.7. If an initial Casualty Report contains incorrect information, submit a supplemental report at
   once and label the corrected items “CORRECTED.”
   A10.3.8. Supplemental reports must contain items A, B, and C and reference the initial Casualty
   Report.

   A10.4.1. Use IMMEDIATE for action addressees (see Table 2.3.).
   A10.4.2. Use PRIORITY for information addressees (see Table 2.3.).

  A10.6.4. Item D—Organization, MAJCOM, and Installation.

  A10.6.6. Item F—Date of Hospitalization and Diagnosed as VSI, SI, or III.
     A10.6.6.1. Use local dates.
     A10.6.6.2. EXAMPLE: HOSPITALIZED: 27 MAR 98. DIAGNOSED VSI: 28 MAR 98.
  A10.6.7. Item G—Diagnosis of Illness or Injury.
     A10.6.7.1. Precisely describe the illness or injury.
     A10.6.7.2. Use both lay and medical terminology.
     A10.6.7.3. If the spine or neck is injured, indicate if there is any paralysis, its extent, and whether
     it's temporary or permanent.
     A10.6.7.4. EXAMPLE: COMPOUND FRACTURE OF THE LEFT FEMUR {OPEN BREAK
     OF THIGH BONE} WITH ARTERIAL LACERATION {CUT ARTERY}; FRACTURE OF
     LEFT TIBIA {SHINBONE} MULTIPLE FACIAL LACERATIONS, FRACTURED CERVIX 3
     AND 4 OF SPINE {NECK}, EXTENT OF PARALYSIS UNKNOWN AT THIS TIME;
     INTRA-ABDOMINAL HEMORRHAGE {BLEEDING WITHIN STOMACH}; 3 FRAC-
     TURED RIBS {LEFT SIDE 3, 4, 5}; RUPTURED SPLEEN {ORGAN ABOVE STOMACH};
     ENUCLEATION OF LEFT EYE {LOSS OF EYEBALL}; FRACTURED LEFT CLAVICLE
     {COLLARBONE}; FRACTURE OF RIGHT HUMERUS {UPPER ARM BONE}; COLLES
     FRACTURE OF LEFT RADIUS (A FRACTURE ABOVE THE WRIST}.
210                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      A10.6.8. Item H—Prognosis, Condition, and Treatment.
         A10.6.8.1. Prognosis and Condition:
            A10.6.8.1.1. Report in simple terms, but avoid vagueness.
            A10.6.8.1.2. State if the prognosis is undetermined.
            A10.6.8.1.3. Indicate the member's present condition.
            A10.6.8.1.4. EXAMPLE: PROGNOSIS: RECOVERY NOT ASSURED.
         A10.6.8.2. Condition and Treatment. Completely and accurately address any of this information
         that applies:
            A10.6.8.2.1. Surgery. State the type, reasons for, and results of surgery. State the member's
            chances for full or partial recovery.
            A10.6.8.2.2. Medication. State type and dosage.
            A10.6.8.2.3. Life Support. State if the member is on a ventilator, if member is conscious or
            unconscious, or if member is comatose (natural or drug-induced), etc.
            A10.6.8.2.4. Diet. State if liquid, intravenous (IV), or regular.
            A10.6.8.2.5. EXAMPLE: CONDITION AND TREATMENT: MEMBER IS IN EMER-
            GENCY SURGERY FOR LACERATIONS AND INTERNAL BLEEDING. TESTS ARE
            BEING CONDUCTED TO DETERMINE EXTENT OF PARALYSIS, IF ANY. WILL
            ADVISE OF RESULTS OF TESTS AND SURGERY IMMEDIATELY FOLLOWING THE
            SURGERY IN A MEDICAL PROGRESS REPORT. FOLLOWING THE SURGERY,
            MEMBER WILL LIKELY REMAIN SEDATED, ON A RESPIRATOR AND WILL BE
            FED INTRAVENOUSLY. NO CURRENT MEDICATION PRESCRIBED. ADDITIONAL
            SURGERY FOR THE SPINAL CORD INJURY MAY BE NEEDED. MEMBER WILL BE
            IN TRACTION FOR AN UNSPECIFIED TIME PERIOD. A SERIES OF CASTS HAVE
            ALSO BEEN PLACED TO TREAT HIS MULTIPLE FRACTURES.
         A10.6.8.3. Inadequate Information. If you don't have prognosis and treatment information, do not
         delay submission of report.
            A10.6.8.3.1. Report the information in medical progress reports (see Attachment 11).
      A10.6.9. Item I—Cause and Circumstances:
         A10.6.9.1. Report the cause of the illness or injury and give a brief account of the circumstances.
         A10.6.9.2. Report whether any other family members were involved in the incident. If so, report
         their condition.
         A10.6.9.3. If the casualty resulted from a military aircraft accident or incident, state crew posi-
         tion, if applicable.
         A10.6.9.4. When submitting a report on a hostile casualty, state how the injuries occurred.
         A10.6.9.5. EXAMPLE: MEMBER WAS INVOLVED IN A SINGLE VEHICLE ACCIDENT
         WHILE TRAVELING EAST ON SUFFOLK ROAD. MEMBER FAILED TO NEGOTIATE A
         CURVE, LOST CONTROL OF THE VEHICLE AND ROLLED DOWN A 100-FOOT
         EMBANKMENT. NO OTHER PERSONS INVOLVED. A PASSERBY NOTIFIED LOCAL
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                               211


     AUTHORITIES WHO TRANSPORTED HIM TO BROOKE ARMY MEDICAL CENTER,
     FORT SAM HOUSTON ARMY POST, SAN ANTONIO TX.
  A10.6.10. Item J—Date of vRED or DD Form 93, Record of Emergency Data:
     A10.6.10.1. Enter the date of the member's latest vRED or DD Form 93.
     A10.6.10.2. EXAMPLE: 18 JAN 02.
  A10.6.11. Item K—Persons Notified or To Be Notified:
     A10.6.11.1. Report the name, relationship, and address of persons listed on the member's vRED
     or DD Form 93.
     A10.6.11.2. For overseas addresses, include the Postal Service Center (PSC) box and the APO or
     FPO.
     A10.6.11.3. If all persons listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 are deceased, report the name, rela-
     tionship to the member, and address of any other NOK listed on:
        A10.6.11.3.1. DD Form 1966 series, located in Section 4 of the member’s UPRG.
        A10.6.11.3.2. Any other documents within the member’s UPRG listing NOK.
     A10.6.11.4. If the member is incapacitated and the spouse is either deceased or incapacitated, and
     the member's children are in the care of someone else, report the children's status and health and
     the name, address, and telephone number of persons caring for them.
     A10.6.11.5. If one or more persons listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 are active or retired mili-
     tary, so state and report their grade and service.
     A10.6.11.6. If one or more persons listed on the vRED or DD Form 93 are deceased or in ill
     health, so state.
     A10.6.11.7. EXAMPLE: GEORGE M. FLEMING/FATHER/121 DUNN STREET, ROME, NY
     09991, 904-555-1212; MILDRED T. FLEMING/MOTHER/SAME AS FATHER.
  A10.6.12. Item L—Notification Source, Date, and Time.
     A10.6.12.1. Report who notified which persons from item K (see A10.6.11.).
     A10.6.12.2. Include the local date and time they made the notifications.
     A10.6.12.3. Indicate the member's desires on which NOK to notify, if any.
     A10.6.12.4. EXAMPLE: DR. KATHERINE DEER, BROOKE ARMY MEDICAL CENTER,
     NOTIFIED (name and relationship) ON 28 MAR 98 AT 1415L.
     A10.6.12.5. If the member's commander or a designated representative notified the NOK, state
     his or her grade, name, and assigned organization.
        A10.6.12.5.1. EXAMPLE: CMSGT ROY ROGERS, 12TH MSS, NOTIFIED (name and
        relationship) ON 28 MAR 98 AT 1400L.
     A10.6.12.6. If someone outside the Air Force notified the NOK, state the person's name and title
     or organization, if applicable.
212                                                     AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


        A10.6.12.7. When the NOK wish to notify other family members, state the NOK's name and rela-
        tionship and when they notified or will notify the other family members. Call AFPC/DPFCS at
        DSN 665-3505 or 1-800-433-0048, as soon as the NOK notifies the other family members.
           A10.6.12.7.1. EXAMPLE: MRS. MARY A. RAY, SPOUSE, WILL NOTIFY (name and
           relationship) ON 28 MAR 98 AT 1630L; WILL CALL AFPC/DPFCS WHEN ACCOM-
           PLISHED.
        A10.6.12.8. If notification was made to a person on behalf of minor children not living with the
        spouse, state who made the notification and the name of the person notified.
           A10.6.12.8.1. EXAMPLE: MAJOR JAMES E. MAY, 56MSSQ, MCGUIRE AFB NJ NOTI-
           FIED MRS. SALLY A. SMITH, MEMBER’S EX-SPOUSE, ON BEHALF OF MINOR
           CHILDREN ON 28 MAR 98 AT 1530L.
        A10.6.12.9. If AFPC/DPFCS is to make notification, state: "REQUEST AFPC MAKE NOTIFI-
        CATION TO THE FOLLOWING PERSONS: (Indicate name, relationship, and any other perti-
        nent information)."
           A10.6.12.9.1. State who requested that AFPC/DPFCS make notifications (the member,
           spouse, commander, etc.).
        A10.6.12.10. If notification is not advisable due to special circumstances such as ill health, state
        the reason.
        A10.6.12.11. For notifying the NOK of foreign nationals in the United States under the auspices
        of the Air Force, see paragraph 3.5.
      A10.6.13. Item M—Emergency Family Member Travel
        A10.6.13.1. See the instructions in paragraph 2.29. NOTE: This item does not apply in an official
        combat zone or qualified hazardous duty area.
        A10.6.13.2. When the NOK are in an overseas area, and the member is hospitalized in another
        overseas area, include the base nearest the NOK as an information addressee.
        A10.6.13.3. Before recommending invitational travel, consider the likelihood of a medical evac-
        uation.
        A10.6.13.4. Indicate with "YES" or "NO" whether doctors consider it medically advisable to
        bring the NOK to the patient's bedside.
        A10.6.13.5. Report the name and grade of the requesting physician and the MTF commander
        concurring with the request.
        A10.6.13.6. Indicate the names and relationships of NOK offered travel in this statement:
        "(Names/relationships) ARE AUTHORIZED TO ENTER THE THEATER IF OVERSEAS.”
        A10.6.13.7. Requests AFPC/DPFCS publish travel message and other instructions.
        A10.6.13.8. Indicate the type of clothing the NOK should pack and an approximate daily expense
        for food and lodging (in dollars).
        A10.6.13.9. Report visa requirements, if any, IAW DoDD 4500.54-G, DoD Foreign Clearance
        Guide.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                          213


     A10.6.13.10. Enter the name and phone (home and duty) to include country code if overseas, of
     the individual who will assist the NOK during their stay.
     A10.6.13.11. EXAMPLE: YES. PARENTS REQUESTED AT BEDSIDE BY ATTENDING
     PHYSICIAN, DR. ROGER CURALL (CAPT/USAF). DR. JOSEPH N. PAINE (BG/USA), MTF
     COMMANDER, APPROVED THE REQUEST. GEORGE M. AND MILDRED T. FLEMING,
     PARENTS, ARE AUTHORIZED TO ENTER THE THEATER. REQUEST AFPC/DPFCS PUB-

     RECOMMENDED. WEATHER IS FAIR WITH OCCASIONAL SHOWERS. DAILY

     NOK DURING THEIR STAY.

                                               Attachment 11

   VSI, SI, AND III MEDICAL PROGRESS REPORTS-(RCS: HAF-DP(AR)9477, MEDICAL
                               CASUALTY REPORTS)

A11.1. General:
      A11.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
      A11.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
      A11.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A11.2. Format:
      A11.2.1. Report on those persons indicated in Table 1.1.
      A11.2.2. Send the report to the addressees and locations indicated in Table 2.3.

A11.3. Specific Instructions:
      A11.3.1. Prepare the report in an easily readable tabular form, with each item lettered and beginning
      on a new line.
      A11.3.2. All reports must contain items A, B, and C and reference the initial Casualty Report and the
      most recent Medical Progress Report.
      A11.3.3. Label unknown or unconfirmed items “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” or “UNCONFIRMED”
      respectively, and report or confirm the information as soon as possible in a supplemental report.
      A11.3.4. Do not label any item “TO BE SUPPLEMENTED” if there is reportable information avail-
      able that would be of interest to family members or of value to the addressees of the report. Instead,
      label such information “UNCONFIRMED.”
      A11.3.5. Confirm all previously unconfirmed items as soon as possible.
      A11.3.6. Report items A through K if the member is being removed from a reportable status.

A11.4. Message Precedence:
      A11.4.1. Use IMMEDIATE for action addressees (see Table 2.3.).
      A11.4.2. Use PRIORITY for information addressees (see Table 2.3.).

A11.5. Subject Line of Message Report. Enter CASUALTY REPORT, MEDICAL PROGRESS
REPORT, and:
      A11.5.1. VSI, SI, or III.
      A11.5.2. HOSTILE or NONHOSTILE (see Attachment 1 for definitions).

A11.6. Item-by-Item Instructions.
      A11.6.1. Item A—Name of Casualty:
         A11.6.1.1. Enter the last name.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                                215


     A11.6.1.2. Repeat the last name.
     A11.6.1.3. Enter the first name, middle name, and suffix, if any.
     A11.6.1.4. EXAMPLE: PIZANA REPEAT PIZANA, JOSE ENRIQUE
  A11.6.2. Item B—Grade:
     A11.6.2.1. Enter the military grade, cadet grade, or civilian grade.
     A11.6.2.2. EXAMPLE: MSGT.
  A11.6.3. Item C—Social Security Number (SSN):
     A11.6.3.1. Enter the SSN and repeat.
     A11.6.3.2. EXAMPLE: 123-45-6789 REPEAT 123-45-6789.
  A11.6.4. Item D—Prognosis and Condition, Changes or Extensions to Diagnosis, and Treatment:
     A11.6.4.1. Prognosis and condition:
        A11.6.4.1.1. Report any improvement or deterioration in the member's condition.
        A11.6.4.1.2. Indicate prognosis toward recovery.
        A11.6.4.1.3. EXAMPLE: PRESENTLY IN STABLE BUT GUARDED CONDITION.
        PROGNOSIS TOWARD RECOVERY IS GOOD. PATIENT REMAINS IN THE ICU
        UNDER THE CARE OF DR. MACDAVITT.
     A11.6.4.2. Changes or extensions to diagnosis:
        A11.6.4.2.1. Report any changes or extensions to previously reported diagnoses.
        A11.6.4.2.2. EXAMPLE: PATIENT IS FEVERISH AND HAS FLUID PRESENT IN HIS
        LUNGS.
     A11.6.4.3. Treatment:
        A11.6.4.3.1. Address any changes to treatment, including:
            A11.6.4.3.1.1. Life support.
                A11.6.4.3.1.1.1. State if member is on ventilator, conscious or unconscious, or coma-
                tose (trauma or drug induced).
                A11.6.4.3.1.1.2. Describe the member's response to treatment so far.
            A11.6.4.3.1.2. Surgery:
                A11.6.4.3.1.2.1. State the type, reasons for, and results of surgery.
                A11.6.4.3.1.2.2. Indicate if doctors have scheduled or canceled surgery, and why.
            A11.6.4.3.1.3. EXAMPLE: PATIENT IS ON VENTILATOR TO HELP HIS BREATH-
            ING. HE REMAINS IN A DRUG—INDUCED COMA. INTERNAL BLEEDING WAS
            STOPPED DURING 3-HOUR EMERGENCY SURGERY. PATIENT TOLERATED
            SURGERY WELL AND RECEIVED 4 UNITS OF BLOOD. SURGERY TO CORRECT
            SPINAL CORD INJURY IS BEING CONTEMPLATED BUT WILL NOT TAKE
216                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


                PLACE UNTIL MEMBER IS MEDEVACED. PATIENT RESPONDS TO STIMULI.
                PARALYSIS HAS NOT BEEN RULED OUT; TEST RESULTS ARE PENDING.
      A11.6.5. Item E—Evacuation Plans:
         A11.6.5.1. Overseas: Indicate if there are any plans to evacuate the patient to the CONUS or to
         another overseas MTF or civilian hospital.
         A11.6.5.2. CONUS: Indicate if there are any plans to evacuate the patient to another MTF or
         civilian hospital within the CONUS.
         A11.6.5.3. Report the complete itinerary, including the flight and mission number, and the name
         of the MTF or civilian hospital destination.
         A11.6.5.4. Include the gaining MTF and servicing MPF at final destination as action addressees;
         MTF(s) and MPF(s) at intermediate stops, if applicable, and the losing MTF as information
         addressees on the report.
         A11.6.5.5. EXAMPLE: TENTATIVE MEDEVAC TO TRIPLER ARMY MEDICAL CENTER,
         HI WITHIN 2 WEEKS. WILL ADVISE ONCE ITINERARY IS KNOWN.
      A11.6.6. Item F—NOK Accompanying Patient Evacuation.
         A11.6.6.1. Report the names of NOK who will accompany the patient when evacuated (MOVED
         or BROKE).
         A11.6.6.2. Address any special needs of the NOK on arrival (i.e., transportation, lodging , ARC
         assistance, etc.).
         A11.6.6.3. If the patient's minor children will not travel, list the names, addresses, and telephone
         numbers of individuals caring for them.
         A11.6.6.4. EXAMPLE: MARY A. FLEMING, SPOUSE, WILL ACCOMPANY THE
         PATIENT WHEN EVACUATED (MOVED OR BROKE). NOK WILL REQUIRE TRANS-
         PORTATION AND LODGING UPON ARRIVAL AT MTF OF FINAL DESTINATION.
      A11.6.7. Item G—Patient Progress Terms:
         A11.6.7.1. Use these terms to report the patient's condition and status:
            A11.6.7.1.1. AGATE. Making normal improvement.
            A11.6.7.1.2. BROKE. Patient evacuated from an overseas MTF to a CONUS MTF.
            A11.6.7.1.3. CRIMP. Not recovering satisfactorily.
            A11.6.7.1.4. IMPEL. Condition has worsened (patient was III and now is SI or VSI, or patient
            was SI and now is VSI). Indicate patient's new status.
            A11.6.7.1.5. MOVED. Patient is evacuated from one overseas MTF to another.
            A11.6.7.1.6. PROVE. Condition has improved (patient moved from VSI to SI or III, or SI to
            III). Indicate patient's new status.
            A11.6.7.1.7. SCRAM. Patient is removed from the VSI, SI, or III list and will return to the
            United States on date indicated.
            A11.6.7.1.8. STALE. Condition remains the same.
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                             217


        A11.6.7.1.9. WRITE. Patient is removed from the VSI, SI, or III list. Member no longer in a
        reportable status.
     A11.6.7.2. Use combinations of the terms, if applicable, such as BROKE-AGATE or
     MOVED-STALE.
     A11.6.7.3. Be sure the terms you use agree with the contents of the report.
     A11.6.7.4. EXAMPLE: BROKE-AGATE.
  A11.6.8. Item H—Emergency Family Member Travel:
     A11.6.8.1. See the instructions in paragraph 2.29. NOTE: This item does not apply in an official
     combat zone.
     A11.6.8.2. When the NOK are in an overseas area, and the member is hospitalized in another
     overseas area, include the base nearest the NOK as an information addressee.
     A11.6.8.3. Before recommending invitational travel, consider the likelihood of a medical evacua-
     tion.
     A11.6.8.4. Indicate with "YES" or "NO" whether doctors consider it medically advisable to bring
     the NOK to the patient's bedside.
     A11.6.8.5. Report the name and grade of the requesting physician and the MTF commander con-
     curring with the request.
     A11.6.8.6. Indicate the names and relationships of NOK offered travel in this statement:
     "(Names/relationships) ARE AUTHORIZED TO ENTER THE THEATER IF OVERSEAS.
     A11.6.8.7. Requests AFPC/DPFCS publish travel message and other instructions.
     A11.6.8.8. Indicate the type of clothing the NOK should pack and an approximate daily expense
     for food and lodging (in dollars).
     A11.6.8.9. Report visa requirements, if any, IAW DoD 4500.54-G, DoD Foreign Clearance
     Guide.
     A11.6.8.10. Enter the name and phone (home and duty) to include country code if overseas, of the
     individual who will assist the NOK during their stay.
     A11.6.8.11. EXAMPLE: YES. PARENTS REQUESTED AT BEDSIDE BY ATTENDING
     PHYSICIAN, DR. ROGER CURALL (CAPT/USAF). DR. JOSEPH N. PAINE (BG/USA), MTF
     COMMANDER, APPROVED THE REQUEST. GEORGE M. AND MILDRED T. FLEMING,
     PARENTS, ARE AUTHORIZED TO ENTER THE THEATER. REQUEST AFPC/DPFCS PUB-
     LISH TRAVEL MESSAGE AND OTHER INSTRUCTIONS. LIGHT SUMMER CLOTHING
     RECOMMENDED. WEATHER IS FAIR WITH OCCASIONAL SHOWERS. DAILY
     EXPENSES FOR FOOD AND LODGING APPROXIMATELY $25 PER PERSON, IF BASE
     FACILITIES ARE USED. TEMPORARY ENTRY VISA MAY BE OBTAINED UPON
     ARRIVAL FOR VISIT NOT EXCEEDING 21 DAYS. MSGT CRISTI WARREN, (HOME
     PHONE), (DUTY PHONE), A MEMBER OF THE PATIENT’S UNIT, WILL ASSIST THE
     NOK DURING THEIR STAY.

                                               Attachment 12

 ABBREVIATED/HASTY CASUALTY REPORT; - MULTIPLE REPORTABLE CASUALTIES
(RCS: DD-FM&P(AR)1664, REPORT OF CASUALTY)

A12.1. General.
      A12.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
      A12.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
      A12.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A12.2. Format.
      A12.2.1. Report on those persons indicated in Table 1.1.
      A12.2.2. Send the report to the addressees and locations indicated in Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and
      Table 2.3..

A12.3. Specific Instructions.
      A12.3.1. Prepare the report in an easily readable tabular form, with each item lettered and beginning
      on a new line.
      A12.3.2. Report first those casualties requiring personal notification to the NOK.
         A12.3.2.1. Give reports on deceased and missing persons priority.
         A12.3.2.2. Do not delay reporting while obtaining information on less serious casualties.
      A12.3.3. Report information on injured personnel in a subsequent abbreviated Casualty Report.

A12.4. Message Precedence.
      A12.4.1. Use IMMEDIATE for action addressees (see Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3., as
      applicable).
      A12.4.2. Use PRIORITY for information addressees (see Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3., as
      applicable).

A12.5. Subject Line of Message Report. Enter CASUALTY REPORT, ABBREVIATED, and either
HOSTILE or NONHOSTILE (see Attachment 1 for definitions).

A12.6. Item-by-Item Instructions.
      A12.6.1. Item A—Reason for Abbreviated Casualty Report:
         A12.6.1.1. State primary reason for using an abbreviated report as “AIRCRAFT ACCIDENT/
         INCIDENT”, “MULTIPLE REPORTABLE CASUALTIES”, “III OR NSI” (see paragraph
         2.30.2.).
      A12.6.2. Item B—Type of Incident and Location:
AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007                                                               219


     A12.6.2.1. Fully identify the type of incident (AIRCRAFT MISSING OR IN AN ACCIDENT,
     NATURAL DISASTER, BOMBING INCIDENT, HOSTILE ACTION, etc.) and the location.
     A12.6.2.2. EXAMPLE: AIRCRAFT ACCIDENT. A C-5 AIRCRAFT STRUCK A UTILITY
     POLE, SHEARING OFF ITS LEFT WING. ACCIDENT OCCURRED SHORTLY AFTER
     TAKE-OFF WHEN THE AIRCRAFT COULD NOT ATTAIN NECESSARY ALTITUDE FOR
     A SUCCESSFUL FLIGHT.
  A12.6.3. Item C—Date and Time of Occurrence:
     A12.6.3.1. Use local date and time.
     A12.6.3.2. EXAMPLE: 12 MAR 98 AT 0800L.
  A12.6.4. Item D—Total Number of Casualties by Status:
     A12.6.4.1. Enter the number of casualties of each status (DECEASED, DUSTWUN, MISSING,
     VSI, SI, III, OR NSI) and repeat.
     A12.6.4.2. EXAMPLE: SI 5 REPEAT 5; NSI 7 REPEAT 7.
     A12.6.4.3. If you do not have the information, enter an estimated number of casualties as reported
     by a competent authority.
  A12.6.5. Item 1E—Name of Casualty:
     A12.6.5.1. Enter the last name.
     A12.6.5.2. Repeat the last name.
     A12.6.5.3. Enter the first name, middle name, and suffix, if any.
     A12.6.5.4. State if the casualty is a civilian.
     A12.6.5.5. If the casualty is the dependent of a military member, give the relationship.
     A12.6.5.6. If the casualty is a crewmember, state crew position, if known.
     A12.6.5.7. EXAMPLE: JOHNSON REPEAT JOHNSON, DAVID ALAN, PILOT.
  A12.6.6. Item 1F—Grade, SSN, and Branch of Service:
     A12.6.6.1. Enter the appropriate information:
        A12.6.6.1.1. EXAMPLE: LT COL, 123-45-6789, USAF.
     A12.6.6.2. For dependents give the sponsor’s data:
        A12.6.6.2.1. Last, first, and middle names, and suffix, if any.
        A12.6.6.2.2. Grade.
        A12.6.6.2.3. SSN.
        A12.6.6.2.4. Branch of Service.
        A12.6.6.2.5. Unit of assignment or attachment.
        A12.6.6.2.6. EXAMPLE: JOHNSON, THOMAS ROBERT, CAPTAIN, 123-45-6789,
        USAF, 12FTW, RANDOLPH AFB, TX.
220                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      A12.6.7. Item 1G—Casualty Status. Include:

         A12.6.7.3. Specific cause.
         A12.6.7.4. Prognosis, if applicable.
         A12.6.7.5. EXAMPLE: SI, COLLAPSED RIGHT LUNG, SHRAPNEL, FULL RECOVERY
         EXPECTED.
      A12.6.8. Item 1H—Date of vRED or DD Form 93, Record of Emergency Data:
         A12.6.8.1. Enter the date of AF member’s vRED or DD Form 93, if available.
         A12.6.8.2. EXAMPLE: vRED - 22 DEC 03.
      A12.6.9. Item 1I—Notification to NOK:
         A12.6.9.1. Indicate by relationship the NOK that the reporting installation will attempt to notify.

                                            Attachment 13

ABBREVIATED CASUALTY/INCIDENT REPORT--(RCS: DD-FM&P(AR)1664, REPORT OF
                            CASUALTY)

A13.1. General.
   A13.1.1. This report is designated emergency status code C-1.
   A13.1.2. Continue reporting during emergency conditions, priority precedence.
   A13.1.3. Continue reporting during MINIMIZE.

A13.2. Format.
   A13.2.1. Report on those persons indicated in Table 1.1.
   A13.2.2. Enter the addressees and locations indicated in Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3.

A13.3. Specific Instructions.
   A13.3.1. Prepare the report in an easily readable tabular form, with each item lettered and beginning
   on a new line.
   A13.3.2. Submit an abbreviated report when information is available and cleared by the responsible
   commander or the base public affairs office.
   A13.3.3. No casualties, report only items A through C.
       A13.3.3.1. If there are casualties, but no names available, report items A through D.
   A13.3.4. Use this report when minimal information on the incident is available and no names are
   available.
       A13.3.4.1. Use abbreviated message (Attachment 12) for reporting when the names of the casu-
       alties are available.

A13.4. Message Precedence.
   A13.4.1. Use IMMEDIATE for action addressees (see Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3., as
   applicable).
   A13.4.2. Use PRIORITY for information addressees (see Table 2.1., Table 2.2., and Table 2.3., as
   applicable).

A13.5. Subject Line of Message Report. Enter CASUALTY REPORT, ABBREVIATED, and either
HOSTILE or NONHOSTILE (see Attachment 1 for definitions).

A13.6. Item-by-Item Instructions.
   A13.6.1. Item A—Reason for Abbreviated Casualty Report:
       A13.6.1.1. State the primary reason for using an abbreviated report. Example: TERRORIST
       ACTIVITY, HOSTILE ACTION or AIRCRAFT ACCIDENT.
222                                                     AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      A13.6.2. Item B—Type of Incident and Location:
         A13.6.2.1. Fully identify the type of incident (AIRCRAFT MISSING OR IN AN ACCIDENT,
         NATURAL DISASTER, BOMBING INCIDENT, HOSTILE ACTION, etc.) and the location.
         A13.6.2.2. If there are no known casualties state “No known casualties.”
         A13.6.2.3. EXAMPLE: AIRCRAFT MISHAP.A B-1B FROM DYESS AFB TX CRASHED
         APPROXIMATELY FIVE MILES NORTH OF DYESS IN AN UNPOPULATED AREA DUR-
         ING A ROUTINE TRAINING MISSION. THE CREW OF FOUR EJECTED AND THERE
         WAS NO COLLATERAL DAMAGE. CREW WAS PICKED UP BY A RESCUE HELICOP-
         TER AND TAKEN TO THE BASE HOSPITAL FOR TREATMENT. EXACT CAUSE OF MIS-
         HAP IS UNKNOWN; HOWEVER, THE AIRCRAFT APPARENTLY DEVELOPED ENGINE
         TROUBLE DURING FINAL APPROACH.
      A13.6.3. Item C—Date and Time of Occurrence:
         A13.6.3.1. Use local date and time.
         A13.6.3.2. EXAMPLE: 12 MAR 98 AT APPROXIMATELY 0930L.
      A13.6.4. Item D—Total Number of Casualties by Status :
         A13.6.4.1. Enter the approximate number of casualties of each status (DECEASED, DUSTWUN,
         MISSING, VSI, SI, III, SI or NSI) and repeat.
         A13.6.4.2. EXAMPLE: SI 1 REPEAT 1; NSI 2 REPEAT 2; NOT INJURED 1 REPEAT 1.
         A13.6.4.3. If you do not have the information, enter an estimated number of casualties as reported
         by a competent authority.

   A14.6.1. Item 1A—Name, Grade, SSN of Casualty:
      A14.6.1.1. Enter the last name.
      A14.6.1.2. Repeat the last name.
      A14.6.1.3. Enter the first name, middle name, and suffix, if any.

      123-45-6789.
224                                                      AFI36-3002_50SWSUP_I 10 OCTOBER 2007


      A14.6.2. Item 1B—Current Condition:
         A14.6.2.1. Enter the patient's diagnosis and prognosis and one or more of the following appropri-
         ate terms:
            A14.6.2.1.1. AGATE. Making normal improvement.
            A14.6.2.1.2. BROKE. Patient evacuated from an overseas MTF to a CONUS MTF.
            A14.6.2.1.3. CRIMP. Not recovering satisfactorily.
            A14.6.2.1.4. IMPEL. Condition has worsened (patient was III and now is SI or VSI, or patient
            was SI and now is VSI). Indicate patient's new status.
            A14.6.2.1.5. MOVED. Patient evacuated from one overseas MTF to another.
            A14.6.2.1.6. PROVE. Condition has improved (patient moved from VSI to SI, VSI to III, or
            SI to III). Indicate patient's new status.
            A14.6.2.1.7. SCRAM. Patient removed from the VSI, SI, or III list and will return to the
            United States on date indicated.
            A14.6.2.1.8. STALE. Condition remains the same.
            A14.6.2.1.9. WRITE. Patient removed from the VSI, SI, or III list. Member no longer in a
            reportable status.
         A14.6.2.2. Use combinations of the terms, if applicable, such as BROKE-AGATE or
         MOVED-STALE.
         A14.6.2.3. Be sure the terms you use agree with the contents of the report.
         A14.6.2.4. EXAMPLE: VSI, BROKEN BACK, PERMANENT PARALYSIS POSSIBLE
         FROM NECK DOWN, PROGNOSIS IS GUARDED (STALE).
      A14.6.3. Item 1C—Other Information:
         A14.6.3.1. Enter the name and location of MTF or civilian hospital.
         A14.6.3.2. If the Air Force is going to evacuate the patient, enter the planned date, the name and
         location of the receiving MTF or civilian hospital.
            A14.6.3.2.1. EXAMPLE: COUNTY HOSPITAL, WARD 4F, ROOM 13, DOVER DE.
         A14.6.3.3. If the Air Force removed the patient from the casualty list, report the local date and
         time removed.
            A14.6.3.3.1. EXAMPLE: PATIENT REMOVED FROM THE CASUALTY LIST ON 23
            MAY 04, 0940L (WRITE).
      A14.6.4. Items 2A through 2C—Casualty Data for Second Person, Etc:
         A14.6.4.1. Enter the same data items as listed in A14.6.1. through A14.6.3. if applicable, until all
         personnel have been reported.
         A14.6.4.2. Each additional person will be numbered 3A through 3C, 4A through 4C, etc.
